401 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hill


No. 50635


Supreme Court of Illinois


78 Ill. 2d 465; 401 N.E.2d 517; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 275; 36 Ill. Dec. 676



February 22, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Hill v. Walker, 397 Ill. App. 3d 1090, 924 N.E.2d 554, 2010 Ill. App. LEXIS 147, 338 Ill. Dec. 348 (Ill. App. Ct. 5th Dist., 2010)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. John J. Moran, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court, Cook County (Illinois), convicting him of murder and conspiracy to commit murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder and conspiracy to commit murder. Defendant appealed, arguing that the trial court erred in admitting into evidence testimony concerning certain admissions made by defendant in the course of plea bargaining. The court ruled that under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 402(f), if a plea discussion did not result in a plea of guilty, or if a plea of guilty was not accepted or was withdrawn, or if judgment on a plea of guilty was reversed on direct or collateral review, neither the plea discussion nor any resulting agreement, plea, or judgment was admissible against defendant in any criminal proceeding. The court reversed the judgment convicting defendant, concluding that the admission of the testimony was so prejudicial as to require reversal.


OUTCOME: The judgment convicting defendant was reversed.

 

402 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Valdez


Nos. 52368, 52472 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


79 Ill. 2d 74; 402 N.E.2d 187; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 285; 37 Ill. Dec. 297



February 1, 1980, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 28, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Earl E. Strayhorn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court allowed direct appeals by both defendant and the Director of Mental Health and Developmental Disabilities (department) from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois). The order directed the department to establish a treatment plan for defendant and to publish regulations for custody, care, and control of patients committed under the Illinois Unified Code of Corrections, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1975, ch. 38, para. 1005-2-4.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was acquitted of murder by reason of insanity, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-3 (1977). In a hearing pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-2-4(a) (1977), he was found in need of mental treatment and remanded to the department, which placed him at a mental health center for treatment. In apparent response to the department's consideration of off-grounds privileges, which were later denied, the state requested a hearing under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-2-4(d) (1977), and defendant petitioned for discharge or release. After an evidentiary hearing, the circuit court ordered establishment of a specific treatment plan for defendant, and publication of procedures and regulations for processing patients committed under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-2-4 (1977). On appeal, the court affirmed the order as to the treatment plan, but vacated that part of the order directing the department to publish general procedures applicable to commitments under para. 1005-2-4. The court held that the circuit court improperly addressed the department's general practices and procedures when the issue before it was the adequacy of defendant's course of treatment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order in part with respect to the issues raised by defendant regarding release from involuntary commitment. The court vacated that part of the order directing the department to issue a memorandum, and in all other respects affirmed the order of the circuit court.

 

403 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Makowicz v. County of Macon


No. 51841


Supreme Court of Illinois


78 Ill. 2d 308; 399 N.E.2d 1302; 1980 Ill. LEXIS 265; 35 Ill. Dec. 774



January 23, 1980, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County, the Hon. John P. Shonkwiler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, superintendent of a county veterans' assistance commission, sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fourth Judicial District (Illinois), which held that the appointment of the superintendent by the commission was unconstitutional because the commission was a private body. The commission's secretary filed a protest of her discharge as secretary with appellee county board.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held that the superintendent's express right to hire under the Bogardus Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 3081-3090 (1977) included an implied authority to discharge, the appellate court found that the commission's appointment of the superintendent was unconstitutional because the commission was a private body. On appeal, the issue was whether the appellate court was correct in holding that the appointment of the superintendent of the commission was an appointment by a private body and invalid, and whether the discharge of a secretary of the commission was to be governed by rules or guidelines of the commission or of the board. The court found that the commission was not a private body or group. The court found that the Illinois General Assembly did not exceed its constitutional limitations in granting the commission authority to select the superintendent under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 8. The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment because the superintendent had the implied authority to discharge.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's judgment.

 

404 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Carbondale v. Brewster


No. 51711


Supreme Court of Illinois


78 Ill. 2d 111; 398 N.E.2d 829; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 422; 34 Ill. Dec. 838



December 20, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jackson County, the Hon. Brocton Lockwood, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Jackson County (Illinois), which dismissed the city's complaint against appellee property owner for violations of a city ordinance requiring the removal of ice and snow from sidewalks. The city maintained that its ordinance requiring the removal was a valid exercise of its police power.


OVERVIEW: A city ordinance required that persons in control of property fronting or abutting on paved sidewalks had to remove snow and ice from the sidewalks within 24 hours of the precipitation. An Illinois statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-80-13 (1977), allowed the city to require the owner or occupant of any premises to keep the sidewalks abutting the premises free from snow or other obstructions. The city's complaint against a property owner for violating the ordinance was dismissed, on the basis that the statute and ordinance were invalid, and the city appealed. The court reversed and held that the statute and ordinance were valid. The court ruled that, based on the development and scope of police power, two related decisions were invalid and not binding upon the court. The court held that keeping sidewalks free from snow and ice was closely related to and in furtherance of the public's welfare and that the city was entitled to undertake by ordinance the requirement to keep the sidewalks clear in the interest of public safety. The means were not arbitrary or unreasonable nor was the burden manifestly disproportional or unrelated to a legitimate classification.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court in an action to determine the validity of a state statute and a city ordinance requiring property owners to remove snow and ice from sidewalks.

 

405 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Carey v. Cousins


No. 51659


Supreme Court of Illinois


77 Ill. 2d 531; 397 N.E.2d 809; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 408; 34 Ill. Dec. 137



November 21, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After defendant was found guilty of murder, aggravated kidnapping, and armed robbery, the trial court held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(d) (1977), allowing the prosecutor to request a proceeding to determine whether the death penalty should be imposed, was unconstitutional. Petitioner State sought a writ of mandamus to direct respondent trial court to expunge its order and to conduct a sentencing proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The court granted the writ of mandamus. It held that the statute did not violate the separation of powers provision of the Illinois Constitution, rejecting the argument that because whether a death penalty sentencing proceeding took place depended on whether the prosecutor requested such a proceeding, the prosecutor was in essence participating in the sentencing process. It stated that there were many occasions in a criminal trial where a judicial ruling adverse to a defendant would not be made unless requested by the prosecution. It held that the statute did not violate the Eighth Amendment, noting that the United States Supreme Court had held in a similar case that the fact that a prosecutor had the discretion whether to seek the death penalty did not mean that there were no standards to guide the prosecutor's decision. Considering the argument that a defendant would be unable to make an intelligent plea decision unless he knew in advance of trial whether the state would seek the death penalty, it held that this argument did not provide a basis for denying the writ, writing that it could not be resolved without the determination of factual matters on which the record was silent.


OUTCOME: The court issued a writ of mandamus directing the trial court to expunge its order holding unconstitutional the statute allowing the prosecution to request a proceeding to determine whether the death penalty should be imposed. It ordered the trial court to conduct a hearing to determine whether a death sentence should be imposed on defendant.

 

406 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Kerasotes Rialto Theater Corp. v. Peoria


No. 51003


Supreme Court of Illinois


77 Ill. 2d 491; 397 N.E.2d 790; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 404; 34 Ill. Dec. 118



November 21, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County, the Hon. James D. Heiple, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order of the Circuit Court for Peoria County (Illinois) that declared a two-percent tax on admissions to appellee corporations' theaters to have been unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The city challenged the trial court's order that declared a two-percent admission tax imposed on the patrons of the corporations' theaters to have been unconstitutional. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part, and determined that the corporations had to burden to establish that the tax was arbitrary and unreasonable. The corporations challenged two categories of exemptions to the tax as having been unreasonable, arbitrary, and unrelated to the purposes of the ordinance. The court held that the corporations failed to establish the invalidity of the classifications contained in the ordinance. The court found that the exemptions contained in the city's ordinance was limited to entities that benefited and improved the community. The court noted that the ordinance placed a burden on the corporations to collect and hold the tax for the city and imposed a cost of collection on the corporations. The court pointed out that the classification system that exempted public entities from the cost of collecting the tax freed them to spend their money to benefit the public. The court held that the corporations failed to establish intentional discrimination on the part of the city.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part because the corporations failed to establish that the city's tax classification scheme was arbitrary and unreasonable, and that the city engaged in intentional discrimination against the corporations.

 

407 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Continental Illinois Nat'l Bank & Trust Co. v. Zagel


Nos. 52339, 52366 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


78 Ill. 2d 387; 401 N.E.2d 491; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 437; 36 Ill. Dec. 650



November 21, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Nos. 52339, 52366. -- Original petitions for declaratory judgment and injunction.



DISPOSITION: Injunction denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Illinois legislature, after abolishing ad valorem personal property taxes, enacted the Illinois replacement tax act (act), Pub. Act 81 --1SS--1 to replace lost taxes. The replacement tax targeted corporations, trusts, and partnerships, and invested capital. In a consolidated action, petitioner taxpayers sought declaratory judgments and injunctions against respondent revenue officials, seeking to have the act declared invalid.


OVERVIEW: The court found that none of the taxpayers' claims against the act established it was invalid, so that the revenue officials should be enjoined for enforcing it. First, the court established that, because the act replaced a tax, but did not create a new tax, it was within the gubernatorial amendatory veto power, provided by Ill. Const. art. IV, § 9(e). Although the replacement tax would raise more than the abolished ad valorem tax did, it was not a new tax on that basis and, so, it was not a prohibited revenue-generating measure. The tax under the act also did not violate a class-imposition restriction under Ill. Const. art. IX, § 5(c), because the corporations and partnerships affected by the income tax under the act, correlated to the classes subject to the ad valorem property tax. Moreover, partnerships were not excluded from tax liability under the act. Further, the act did not impose double taxation by taxing partners on partnership income and individual income. Nor did it double tax corporations whose main corporate asset was real property, because the income tax under the act was directed at the business aspect of the invested capital, not at its identity as real property.


OUTCOME: The court denied the taxpayers' petitions for an injunction against the act and declined to hold it constitutionally invalid.

 

408 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Parkins


Nos. 51467, 51468, 51504 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


77 Ill. 2d 253; 396 N.E.2d 22; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 379; 32 Ill. Dec. 909



October 19, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Nos. 51467, 51468. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County, the Hon. Bradner C. Riggs, Judge, presiding.

No. 51404. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Jerry S. Rhodes, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the judgments of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois) allowing the motion to dismiss filed by defendants, who had been charged with the offense of harassment by telephone in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 134, para. 16.4-1(2) (1977). The state also appealed from the judgment of the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) allowing the motion of defendant to dismiss similar charges.


OVERVIEW: Defendants in both cases filed a motion to dismiss the charge of harassment by telephone. The trial courts granted the motions on the basis that the Illinois telephone harassment act was unconstitutional. Defendants contended that, when a statute, which was susceptible of application to conduct protected by the First Amendment presented the danger of a chilling effect, it was unconstitutionally overbroad. They argued that the telephone harassment statute was impermissibly vague because no standard of conduct was specified. The court, in reversing the judgments of the trial courts, held that the statute was neither vague nor overbroad. In the phrase, "with the intent to abuse, threaten, or harass any person," the words "abuse" and "harass" took color from the word "threaten" and acquired more restricted meanings. The statute did not attempt to particularize all conduct that fell within the statute because it would have been a futile effort to enumerate all methods of harassing someone over the telephone.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the trial court, which had dismissed the charges against defendants for harassment by telephone.

 

409 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Kutner


No. 51608


Supreme Court of Illinois


78 Ill. 2d 157; 399 N.E.2d 963; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 427; 35 Ill. Dec. 674; 11 A.L.R.4th 123



October 19, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 1, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: Disciplinary proceeding.



DISPOSITION: Respondent censured.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent attorney sought review of a decision from the Hearing Board for the Attorney Registration and Disciplinary Commission (Illinois), which recommended that the appropriate measure of discipline for respondent's violation of Ill. Code of Prof'l Responsibility DR 2-106 (1970) was censure.


OVERVIEW: The administrator of the Attorney Registration and Disciplinary Commission filed a complaint against respondent attorney with unprofessional conduct. The complaint alleged that respondent was guilty of overreaching, the use of a curriculum vitae to induce the payment of an excessive fee, and charging an excessive fee in violation of Ill. Code of Prof'l Responsibility DR 2-106 (1970). The Hearing Board made a recommendation that the appropriate measure of discipline was censure. On appeal, the court adopted the Hearing Board's recommendation for censure. The court held that an attorney-client fixed-fee agreement could form the basis for disciplinary action against an attorney. Further, respondent's receipt of a $ 5,000 fee constituted an excessive fee under Ill. Code of Prof'l Responsibility DR 2-106 (1970). The court found that respondent's violation of the disciplinary rule did warrant discipline, and it found that censure was the appropriate sanction to impose.


OUTCOME: The court adopted the recommendation that the appropriate measure for respondent attorney's violation of the disciplinary rules was censure. The gross overcharge of a fee by respondent warranted discipline and censure was the most appropriate sanction.

 

410 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Getto v. Chicago


No. 51581


Supreme Court of Illinois


77 Ill. 2d 346; 396 N.E.2d 544; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 388; 33 Ill. Dec. 155



October 19, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 30, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Nathan M. Cohen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and telephone company, appealed an interlocutory order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which directed defendant telephone company to segregate and sequester that portion of the message tax alleged by plaintiff customer to be excessive.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff customer filed an action against defendants, city and telephone company, alleging that defendants erroneously collected sums greatly in excess of the amounts due under the Messages Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 467.1, from defendant telephone company's customers. Defendants appealed the circuit court's interlocutory order directing defendant telephone company to segregate and sequester that portion of the message tax alleged by plaintiff to be excessive. The court affirmed the circuit court's order because having paid the tax, plaintiff was entitled to the benefit of the rule that taxing laws were to be strictly construed and that they were not to be extended beyond the clear import of the language used. The court determined that the rule's application would proscribe the construction of the statute, which would result in an increase both in the amount of the tax paid to defendant city and the "costs of accounting" permitted to be charged by the nominal taxpayer. The court remanded for further proceedings, holding that construing the term "gross receipts" to include the municipal tax was erroneous.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order because due to the fact that plaintiff customer paid the tax, he was entitled to the benefit of the rule that taxing laws were to be strictly construed and that they were not to be extended beyond the clear import of the language used. The court remanded for further proceedings, holding that construing the term "gross receipts" to include the municipal tax was erroneous.

 

411 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Johnston v. Bloomington


No. 51126


Supreme Court of Illinois


77 Ill. 2d 108; 395 N.E.2d 549; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 344; 32 Ill. Dec. 319



October 2, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County, the Hon. Charles E. Glennon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs sought review of the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District's (Illinois), which reversed and remanded the circuit court's decision which had allowed the motion for dismissal of plaintiff's action filed by defendants, city and its treasurer. The speeding ordinance under which plaintiffs were convicted had been declared unconstitutional and plaintiffs sought to recover the fines paid to defendant city.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs contended that the effect of an ordinance that had been held unconstitutional was the same as though it had never existed and that judgments of conviction based upon it were void and that fines paid under a void ordinance were not voluntarily paid. On appeal, the court held that judgments entered in a civil proceeding could be collaterally attacked as void only where there was a total want of jurisdiction in the court which entered the judgment, either as to the subject matter or as to the parties. If the court had jurisdiction, it was empowered to make either a correct or an erroneous decision and the fact that the statute or ordinance upon which the decision was based was void did not serve to deprive it of jurisdiction. The complaint contained no allegations that purported to attack the jurisdiction of the circuit court, which entered the judgments under which the fines were paid, either on the ground of lack of jurisdiction over the subject matter, or of the parties.


OUTCOME: The appellate court's judgment was reversed and the circuit court's judgment was affirmed.

 

412 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Kezerian


No. 51149


Supreme Court of Illinois


77 Ill. 2d 121; 395 N.E.2d 551; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 346; 32 Ill. Dec. 321



October 2, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. John J. Hoban, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state sought review of a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois), which affirmed a judgment of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County suppressing certain tape recordings and testimony in defendant's trial.


OVERVIEW: During an investigation of a reported burglary plan, the state's attorney gave oral authorizations, followed by written authorizations, to the Illinois Bureau of Investigation (IBI) for electronic recordings of conversations between defendant and an informant. At trial, the trial court suppressed the recordings and barred the information from testifying about the recorded conversations because the request to eavesdrop was made by the IBI and not the state's attorney. The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment. On further appeal, the court reversed the judgments below an held that the tape recordings were obtained in compliance with the then-existing statutory requirements for electronic surveillance and, therefore, were not subject to the exclusionary rule. The court found that, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 14-2(a), electronic recordings were permitted with the consent of one party and at the request of the state's attorney and that authorization by the state's attorney was the same as a request.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the appellate and trial courts, which had suppressed electronic recordings and related testimony, and remanded the cause to the trial court.

 

413 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Roth v. Yackley


No. 51478


Supreme Court of Illinois


77 Ill. 2d 423; 396 N.E.2d 520; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 393; 33 Ill. Dec. 131



October 2, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 30, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of La Salle County, the Hon. Leonard Hoffman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff probationers appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of La Salle County (Illinois), which granted defendant government's motions to strike and dismiss both complaints. The violators brought suit against the government for return of fines and costs paid as conditions of probation incident to deferred dispositions of criminal charges.


OVERVIEW: The probationers were sentenced under § 10 of the Cannabis Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 710 (1973), and § 410 of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1410 (1973). Both complaints were premises on new case law which held that fines and costs were not reasonable terms and conditions of probation as that term was used in § 10 of the Cannabis Control Act and that, therefore, the imposition of fines and costs were not authorized by statute. The government contended that amendatory acts to the stated statutes expressly authorized the imposition of fines and costs as conditions of probation. The court reversed the order of the circuit court striking and dismissing the probationers' complaints on the basis of the amendments to the Cannabis Control Act and the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, and remanded the matter. The court held that the legislature could not constitutionally overrule a decision of the court by declaring that an amendatory act applied retroactively to cases decided before its effective date.


OUTCOME: The judgments were reversed and the case was remanded for determination of whether the cause was properly brought as a class action and whether the probationers were entitled to the relief they sought.

 

414 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Anderson v. Wagner


Nos. 50880, 50980, 50981


Supreme Court of Illinois


79 Ill. 2d 295; 402 N.E.2d 560; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 442; 37 Ill. Dec. 558



October 2, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 28, 1980.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 50880. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County, the Hon. A. G. Webber III, presiding.

Nos. 50980, 50981. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. Creed D. Tucker, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: These consolidated cases involved the validity of § 21.1 of the Limitations Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. 1977, ch. 83, para. 22.1, which provided for a special limitation period for plaintiff patients' medical malpractice actions against defendants, physicians and hospital. One panel of the Fourth District Appellate Court (Illinois) held § 21.1 to be constitutional. Another panel of the appellate court for the same district held § 21.1 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff patients contended that § 21.1was unconstitutional for several reasons. The patients claimed that § 21.1 violated the due process and equal protection clauses of both the Federal and State constitutions. The plaintiffs' primary contention was, however, that § 21.1 violated Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 (1970) in that it was special legislation because it (1) set medical malpractice apart from all other professional malpractice and (2) conferred a special privilege upon only two classes of medical health providers, physicians and hospitals. The court found no due process violation, noting that it had not been demonstrated that the legislative action in establishing the four-year outer limit within which to file a complaint for medical malpractice was unreasonable. The court concluded that § 21.1 was a reasonable attempt to remedy what the legislature perceived to be a medical malpractice insurance crisis. The court further concluded that there was a reasonable basis for differentiating between physicians and hospitals and other members of the general class of health-care providers for the purpose of § 21.1. The court also held that § 21.1 was not special legislation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the panel of the appellate court which held the Limitations Act constitutional. The court reversed the judgment of the other panel of the appellate court which held the Limitations Act unconstitutional.

 

415 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Polyvend, Inc. v. Puckorius


No. 51011


Supreme Court of Illinois


77 Ill. 2d 287; 395 N.E.2d 1376; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 383; 7 A.L.R.4th 1185; 32 Ill. Dec. 872



October 2, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for declaratory judgment brought by plaintiff, public contract bidder (bidder), defendant, state and officials (state), appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the circuit court's judgment. The state argued that the appellate court erred in finding that § 10.1 of the Illinois Purchasing Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 127, para. 132.10.1, violated due process.


OVERVIEW: The bidder was the successor corporation to one whose bid for the production of auto license plates was accepted by the state for the previous three years. The bidder's former president, who still owned a controlling interest in the bidder, had been convicted of bribery in the past. The bidder's proposal, which was the only one received, was rejected because of the application of para. 132.10.1 due to of the bribery conviction. The bidder filed an action for declaratory judgment and argued that para. 132.10.1 violated its due process rights. The circuit court granted the state's motion for summary judgment, but the appellate court reversed. The state appealed. The court reversed and held that the bidder did not have a protectable property interest in the award of a contract within the meaning of the due process clause because the bidder did not have a legitimate claim of entitlement to the award. There was no recognized property right in a future government contract. The Act was not unconstitutionally vague, and it did not invalidly delegate legislative power to administrative officials. The Act was not applied retroactively to the bidder, and it was not a bill of attainder.


OUTCOME: In the bidder's declaratory judgment action, the court reversed the appellate court's reversal of the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the state.

 

416 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Graham v. Illinois Racing Board


No. 51621


Supreme Court of Illinois


76 Ill. 2d 566; 394 N.E.2d 1148; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 361; 31 Ill. Dec. 771



September 19, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Raymond K. Berg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, Illinois Racing Board, sought review of a permanent injunction issued by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) enjoining defendant from proceeding with any hearing against plaintiff horse owner. The trial court found that plaintiff had no adequate remedy at law, that he would be irreparably harmed if the injunction were not granted, and that the probability of damage to defendant as a result of the injunction was remote.


OVERVIEW: In his complaint against defendant Illinois Racing Board (board), plaintiff horse owner claimed that defendant had charged him with various rules violations and had scheduled a hearing, at which time it proposed to introduce testimony, test results, and documents concerning urine specimens that were allegedly "kept, transported, and delivered" in violation of the board's own rules. Plaintiff asserted that if the board held its hearing he would be irreparably harmed in that his reputation and earning capacity would be severely damaged; that he had no adequate remedy at law; and that the board would suffer no injury should an injunction issue. The lower court issued a permanent injunction prohibiting the board from proceeding with any hearing against plaintiff that would utilize the tests or specimens involved in the present case. In reversing the lower court, the court held that plaintiff failed to exhaust the administrative remedies provided by the Illinois Horse Racing Act of 1975, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 8, para. 37 -- 1 et seq. (1977).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the lower court granting a permanent injunction against defendant, Illinois Racing Board. The court held that plaintiff horse owner failed to exhaust his administrative remedies.

 

417 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Saltiel v. Olsen


No. 51648


Supreme Court of Illinois


77 Ill. 2d 23; 394 N.E.2d 1197; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 366; 31 Ill. Dec. 820



September 19, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Nathan M. Cohen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, the recorder of deeds and the county treasurer, appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), in favor of plaintiff taxpayer, which entered an injunction restraining them from retaining as a fee a portion of monies received from the sale of revenue stamps pursuant to the Real Estate Transfer Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 1003 (1977).


OVERVIEW: The complaint alleged that para. 1003 violated Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(a) (1970) by authorizing the retention of transfer tax funds as a fee by the local recorder of deeds. The trial court found a constitutional violation and entered the injunction sought by the taxpayer. The recorder of deeds and county treasurer appealed and the court affirmed. The constitutional provision prohibited compensation of officers from fees collected and prohibited fees from being based on taxes collected. Because the portion of the tax to be retained was to kept as a fee, it violated the prohibition against fees being based on amounts collected. This was true even though the officials' compensation was not based on the fees they collected. The court noted that later amendments deleting the reference to amount to be retained as being a fee did not reflect on the original intent of the statute. In fact, the court looked at prior history and determined that compensation and fees had historically been based on the amounts collected, which was specifically what the constitutional provision was designed to prevent.


OUTCOME: The affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

418 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Taylor


No. 50913


Supreme Court of Illinois


76 Ill. 2d 289; 391 N.E.2d 366; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 323; 29 Ill. Dec. 103



June 8, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County, the Hon. John S. Ghent, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, a juvenile, sought review of a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which reversed and remanded defendant's conviction for burglary, armed robbery, and rape, holding that defendant's confession should have been suppressed in the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant juvenile was convicted as an adult by the trial court of burglary, armed robbery, and rape. The appellate court held that defendant's confession should have been suppressed and reversed without considering whether the evidence at trial was sufficient to support the convictions. The court held that, pursuant to the Juvenile Court Act, 37 Ill. Comp. Stat. 702/7(3), a juvenile court was permitted to enter an order requesting prosecution under the criminal laws. The juvenile court must have accompanied such waiver order with a statement of the reasons for transfer with sufficient specificity to permit meaningful review. The court held that defendant was not denied due process because he was not permitted to appeal his transfer order until after his trial. The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court. However, the court found that it was error for the appellate court to fail to determine whether the evidence adduced at trial was sufficient to sustain defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, which held that defendant juvenile's confession should have been suppressed during his trial for burglary, armed robbery, and rape. The court held that defendant was not denied due process because he was not permitted to appeal his transfer order until after his trial.

 

419 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Haughton v. Haughton


No. 50923


Supreme Court of Illinois


76 Ill. 2d 439; 394 N.E.2d 385; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 335; 31 Ill. Dec. 183



May 24, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 28, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Lawrence J. Genesen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; judgment here for plaintiffs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother challenged the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the orders of the trial court that awarded the mother enforcement of a foreign support order against defendant father pursuant to the Uniform Foreign Judgments Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 77, par. 88 et seq. Pending the outcome of the action, the mother died and the administrator was substituted as plaintiff.


OVERVIEW: The mother had two daughters out of wedlock. The mother was awarded support orders in two different states based on the father's relocation. The appellate court held that the mother's actions for enforcement of the two separate orders were time barred. On appeal, the administrator for the mother's estate argued that application of the tolling provisions applied to residents but not nonresidents were unconstitutional. The court reversed the appellate court's order because the mother had a money judgment payable in periodic installments. Therefore, the statute of limitations began to run on each installment as it became due. However, the running of the statute was tolled during defendant's absence from the forum state. The court held that tolling provisions applicable only to residents was unconstitutional because it violated the Equal Protection Clause. Therefore, the mother's action to enforce two foreign support orders should not have been dismissed. The court also held that the subsequent support order was not a modification of the original but was a separate judgment.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the court found the mother's estate was entitled to judgment in her action for enforcement of two separate foreign support orders.

Eastern v. Canty


No. 50522


Supreme Court of Illinois


75 Ill. 2d 566; 389 N.E.2d 1160; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 307; 27 Ill. Dec. 752



May 18, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, the Hon. Richard P. Goldenhersh, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, chairmen of county boards and a sanitary district, appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois), which denied their motions to dismiss and granted a motion by plaintiff board member for summary judgment in the his action seeking declaratory and injunctive relief because the Metro-East Sanitary District Act of 1974, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 42, para. 503, § 1 (1977), violated the Equal Protection Clause.


OVERVIEW: A board member's complaint alleged that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 42, para. 503, § 1 was unconstitutional, as it permitted only two appointed members of the board to be residents of the St. Clair County portion of the sanitary district and, as a result, did not give the residents fair and adequate representation. The circuit court granted summary judgment for the member on the grounds that the formula for the composition of the board of commissioners prescribed by the statute called for a comparison of assessed valuation between the portion of each county lying within the district, not between each county as a whole. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded with directions to dismiss the complaint for failure to state a cause of action. The court determined that the circuit court had jurisdiction to decide the case because the petition of the chairmen and district for removal was dismissed before the entry of the final judgment. The court further held that there was no constitutional requirement that the appointed governing body of the district be so constituted that a majority of its members "represent" the more populated of the areas that composed the district.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the judgment in favor of the board member with directions to dismiss the complaint.

Strukoff v. Strukoff


No. 50706


Supreme Court of Illinois


76 Ill. 2d 53; 389 N.E.2d 1170; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 313; 27 Ill. Dec. 762



May 18, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Charles J. Fleck, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff ex-wife challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County, (Illinois), which held that § 403(e) of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 403(e), was an unconstitutional legislative encroachment on the rulemaking powers of the judiciary.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held the trial on the grounds for the ex-wife and defendant ex-husband's divorce in the morning and the trial on the distribution of marital property in the afternoon of the same day. The Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 403(e), required a bifurcated trial with at least 48 hours between the two trials. The ex-wife filed a post trial motion for a new trial because the trial court did not follow the bifurcation procedure. The trial court held that § 403(e) was an unconstitutional encroachment on the rulemaking powers of the judiciary. On appeal, the court affirmed that part of the trial court's judgment that dissolved the marriage. The court reversed the trial court's ruling that § 403(e) was unconstitutional and the trial court's holding on the property distribution. The court stated that compliance with the statute was mandatory and that noncompliance by the trial court required reversal. Section 403(e) was not unconstitutional. It did not violate the separation of powers requirement, and its purpose was to promote amicable property settlements. The case was remanded.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and reversed in part the holding of the trial court. The trial court failed to comply with a bifurcation of divorce trials' statute. Therefore, the action was remanded.

Williams v. Department of Labor


No. 51024


Supreme Court of Illinois


76 Ill. 2d 72; 389 N.E.2d 1177; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 315; 27 Ill. Dec. 769



May 18, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County, the Hon. Clayton R. Williams, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Department of Labor (department) challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which declared § 1200 of the Unemployment Insurance Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, par. 530 (1977), that authorized the department to limit the fee charged by appellee claimant's attorney, to be an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power.


OVERVIEW: The claimant's attorney had sent the department a letter requesting that his attorney fee be approved. The department denied the attorney's request for reconsideration after it had reduced the sum of the permissible fee to be charged the claimant. On appeal, the court held that the claimant lacked standing to challenge the department's decision to reduce the fee requested by his attorney. It noted that the claimant was a party to the department's decision, which denied him unemployment benefits, as well as a party to the department's decision, which limited the fee of his attorney to $ 500. However, the claimant was not a party aggrieved by the department's decision not to reconsider. The claimant stood only to benefit financially from the decision limiting the amount of fee, which his attorney could charge him for services rendered. The claimant's interest regarding the attorney fee was adverse not to the department's decision but to his attorney's attempt to nullify the fee limitation. Had the attorney had sought review in his own behalf under the Administrative Review Act, the claimant would properly have been made a defendant, rather than a party plaintiff.


OUTCOME: The court found that the claimant lacked standing, vacated the judgment order of the circuit court, and remand the cause with directions to dismiss the claimant's amended complaint for administrative review.

McCabe v. Burgess


No. 50676


Supreme Court of Illinois


75 Ill. 2d 457; 389 N.E.2d 565; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 286; 27 Ill. Dec. 501



April 18, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 30, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. Harold L. Jensen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state challenged the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which reversed the trial court's determination that the two prerequisites for a class action set forth in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, par. 57.2 (1977), were not present in the claims of appellee convict and others purported to be in the class.


OVERVIEW: Appellee convict brought an action to enforce the court's prior holdings in People v. McCabe (1971), 49 Ill. 2d 338, and People v. Meyerowitz (1975), 61 Ill. 2d 200, through a class action. The trial court dismissed the action, and the appellate court reversed. On further challenge by appellant state, the court held that the appellate misapprehended its role and misapplied the governing principles with regard to the holding of the trial court that the two prerequisites to a class action were not present in the case. Under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, par. 57.2 (1977), these prerequisites must be established by the proponents of the class action. Although the trial court considered the size of the class and the fairness of a class action to the members of the class, The court held that there were no questions of law or fact common to the members of the class to be litigated in a class action and that the class action would not result in any increased efficiency to the court or to the litigants in the adjudication of the claims. The court held that the determination of the trial court as to the absence of these two criteria did not constitute an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the appellate court was reversed and the judgment of the circuit court that there were no questions of law or fact common to the members of the class to be litigated in a class action and that the class action would not result in any increased efficiency to the court or to the litigants in the adjudication of the claims brought by appellee convict and others, and the cause was remanded to the circuit court of Champaign County.

Cooney v. Society of Mt. Carmel


No. 50992


Supreme Court of Illinois


75 Ill. 2d 430; 389 N.E.2d 549; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 282; 27 Ill. Dec. 485



April 3, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Daniel P. Coman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant private school was granted leave to appeal an order of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) denying its motion to dismiss a complaint filed against it by plaintiff former student. The appellate court held that the General Assembly did not intend that the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 8-102 (1975), should apply to private schools.


OVERVIEW: After the former student instituted an action against the private school, the school filed a motion to dismiss the complaint because notice had not been given as provided in the Local Government and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Act). In affirming a decision denying the private school's motion to dismiss, the court stated that a review of the statutory language and purpose of the Act clearly indicated that it did not apply to private schools. While private schools served the public good by educating children, the performance of that beneficial function did not transform such schools from private into public entities. Cases did not require equal treatment of public and private schools beyond the application of the tort liability provisions of the School Code. The General Assembly was free to treat public schools differently from private schools by including only public schools in the provisions of the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision that denied the private school's motion to dismiss the former student's tort action.

Griffitts Constr. Co. v. Department of Labor


No. 50951


Supreme Court of Illinois


76 Ill. 2d 99; 390 N.E.2d 333; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 318; 28 Ill. Dec. 166



March 20, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 30, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employer appealed a decision of an appellate court (Illinois), which affirmed a ruling that it was an employing unit subject to the provisions of the Unemployment Compensation Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 300 et seq. (1965), in an action involving the status of its salesmen and canvassers assigned by defendant Director of Labor (director).


OVERVIEW: The employer was a company in the home-improvement business. Much of its business was generated through the efforts of salesmen and canvassers. The director determined that the employer was liable to the unemployment compensation fund because of the services performed by its salesman and canvassers. The employer made the payment but later filed a claim for refund, which was denied. The employer filed a protest, and the determination was affirmed after a hearing. The employer filed a complaint for administrative review, and the decision was affirmed again there and by the appellate court. The employer sought review, arguing that the services were exempt under the independent contractors exemption of § 212 of the Act. The court affirmed, holding that the employer failed to prove that the salesman at issue and the canvassers were free from its control, so it failed to satisfy § 212(a) of the Act. The exemption required that the salesman and canvassers were free from control, the service was outside the usual course of business or performed outside all the places of business of the enterprise, and the individual was engaged in an independently established trade or occupation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a holding that the employer was liable to pay money into the unemployment compensation fund in an action to determine whether the employer was entitled to exemption for its salesman and canvassers.

Illinois Gamefowl Breeders Ass'n v. Block


No. 51066


Supreme Court of Illinois


75 Ill. 2d 443; 389 N.E.2d 529; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 284; 27 Ill. Dec. 465



March 14, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 30, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Bureau County, the Hon. C. Howard Wampler, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee gamefowl breeders association (association) filed a declaratory judgment action against appellant state, challenging the constitutionality of § 4.01(a) and (c) of the Humane Care for Animals Act (act), codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 8, para. 704(a), (c) (1975) et seq. The Circuit Court of Bureau County (Illinois) declared the challenged provisions unconstitutional. The state appealed.


OVERVIEW: The association challenged those portions of the act that prohibited owning, breeding, training, selling, shipping or receiving animals which one knew or should have known are intended to be used for fighting purposes. The trial court found that those provisions were unconstitutional. On appeal the court held that: (1) the association had standing to challenge the constitutionality of the act because they had alleged an actual controversy that admitted of an immediate and definitive determination and the association had a real interest in the outcome of the controversy, (2) the act was a legitimate exercise of the state's police power because it was intended to strengthen the ban on animal fighting, (3) the act was not unconstitutional because in the exercise of its police power the state had not enacted a statute that was arbitrary or discriminatory; the language of the act only prohibited conduct related to fighting, not to ownership of animals that may have been bred to fight.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment that the act was unconstitutional.

 

427 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Client Follow-Up Co. v. Hynes


No. 51598


Supreme Court of Illinois


75 Ill. 2d 208; 390 N.E.2d 847; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 453; 28 Ill. Dec. 488



March 14, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 30, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard L. Curry, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed its class action suit against defendant county tax assessor brought on behalf of similarly situated corporations regarding taxation of capital stock.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was representative of a certified class of plaintiffs alleging that the assessor's attempt to collect personal property tax in 1979 on shares of capital stock owned in 1978 was unconstitutional. Ill. Const. art. IX, § 5(c) abolished previous ad valorem personal property tax for corporations after 1979 and instilled a real property taxation scheme to replace the revenue lost. However, the general assembly had not yet passed legislation implementing this provision. The circuit court granted the assessor's motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court reversed. The court held that the constitutional convention implementing the constitutional provision sought to abolish the ad valorem taxation system. The language of § 5(c) constituted a limitation on the power to tax after January 1, 1979 and not a mandate. Therefore, the courts were entitled to enforce the limitation. Nonetheless, the corporations were still required to pay the 1978 ad valorem taxes because the owner of personal property is liable for taxes on that property on April 1 of the tax year. The court concluded that the general assembly had a continuing mandate to implement the constitutional provision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court, which dismissed the corporation's class action suit regarding implementation of a constitutional provision calling for the abolishment of ad valorem personal property taxes.

Thygesen v. Callahan


No. 50667


Supreme Court of Illinois


74 Ill. 2d 404; 385 N.E.2d 699; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 244; 24 Ill. Dec. 558



January 26, 1979, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard L. Curry, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, currency exchange owners and operators, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found § 19.3 of the Currency Exchange Act (Act), codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 16 1/2, para. 49.3 (1977), constitutional. The currency exchange owners and operators filed a suit against defendant Director of Financial Institutions (Director) because there were no guidelines for setting rates.


OVERVIEW: The currency exchange owners and operators alleged that the total absence of standards or guidelines rendered § 19.3 of the Act, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 16 1/2, para. 49.3 (1977), unconstitutional. The court found that § 19.3 delegated the power to regulate rates to the Director. The court determined that the legislative delegation was valid if it identified the persons and activities potentially subject to the regulations, the harm sought to be prevented, and the general means intended to be available to the Director to prevent the identified harm. The court concluded that the legislature in § 19.3 identified the persons and activities potentially subject to the regulations, but made no attempt to identify the harm sought to be prevented. The court further determined that there were no meaningful standards to guide the Director in setting maximum rates. The court concluded that the legislature unlawfully delegated its power and that § 19.3 was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court.

Northern Ill. Auto. Wreckers & Rebuilders Ass'n v. Dixon

Supreme Court of Illinois

DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant government official sought review of a judgment entered in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted plaintiff business entities a declaratory judgment that declared the government official's administrative rule unconstitutional and void and enjoined its enforcement against plaintiff business entities.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 2-101, the government official promulgated Ill. Admin. R. 5-401A that required the business entities to maintain records of certain information on the acquisition and disposition of vehicles and parts. The trial court granted the business entities' declaratory judgment relief and determined that the rule promulgated by the government official was unconstitutionally vague under the due process clause of both the state and federal constitutions. On appeal, the government official contended that the rule had sufficient certainty to afford the business entities' due process. The court agreed with the government official. The court pointed out that administrative rules and regulations had the force and effect of law and were to be construed under the same standards, which governed the construction of statutes. The court noted that the administrative rule at issue in this case carried a presumption of validity. On review of the challenged language within the rule, the court concluded that the rule sufficiently informed the business entities of the records they were required to keep and thus they were not denied due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment.

Miller v. Department of Registration & Education


Nos. 50570, 50571, 50663


Supreme Court of Illinois


75 Ill. 2d 76; 387 N.E.2d 300; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 259; 25 Ill. Dec. 644



January 26, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 30, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Nos. 50570, 50571. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Richard L. Curry, Judge, presiding.

No. 50663. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed. Judgment affirmed. Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, pharmacist and the Department of Registration and Education (Department), and appellees, pharmacists and the Department, challenged decisions by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which decided if the pharmacists' convictions under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1396h(b)(1) constituted gross immorality under the Pharmacy Practice Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111, para. 4019 (1977), and provided grounds to revoke their licenses.


OVERVIEW: The pharmacists were convicted of violating § 1396h(b)(1) for he offering or making of a kickback or bribe in connection with furnishing of drugs and pharmaceutical services for which payment was made in whole or part out of federal funds under an approved state medical assistance plan. The Department followed the recommendations of the State Board of Pharmacy and revoked the pharmacists' licenses. The trial court affirmed two revocations and reversed one revocation. The court reversed the two decisions affirming the revocations and affirmed the decision reversing the revocation. The court determined that violation of § 1396h(b)(1) was not concerned with the exercise of the professional skill of a pharmacist. It was extraneous to the central concern of the Act, the protection of public health, safety, and welfare through the regulation of the practice of pharmacy. A misdemeanor conviction for the payment of kickbacks or bribes was not gross immorality for the purposes of pharmacy license revocations.


OUTCOME: The court determined that the Department could not revoke the pharmacists' licenses on the ground of gross immorality based upon their convictions of a federal misdemeanor offense involving the payment of kickbacks or bribes.

Lopez v. Fitzgerald


No. 50131


Supreme Court of Illinois


76 Ill. 2d 107; 390 N.E.2d 835; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 319; 28 Ill. Dec. 476



January 26, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Opinion Filed on Denial of Rehearing May 30, 1979, Reported at 76 Ill. 2d 107 at 130.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Walter P. Dahl, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, individuals and community groups, sought review of the decision from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the declaratory judgment order of the circuit court. The circuit court had granted the individuals and community groups' motion for summary judgment and denied appellee, Department of Building's, motion for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: Individuals and community groups brought a class action complaint for injunctive and declaratory relief against the department of Buildings. Individuals and community members sought access to building inspection reports made by the Department of Buildings. The court held that there was insufficient basis in the Local Records Act to justify access by the individuals and community groups to reports by building inspectors. The court held that even if the investigation reports fell within the definition of public records under the Local Records Act, it did not follow that they were subject to public disclosure. The court held that in the absence of factors supporting disclosure other than a general policy of openness in government and the individuals and community groups' interest in the condition of buildings, and in the face of strong countervailing factors, investigative reports were not open to public access.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court, which denied declaratory relief because there was no public right of access to initial building investigation reports.

 

432 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Application of Skidmore


No. 49625


Supreme Court of Illinois


75 Ill. 2d 33; 387 N.E.2d 290; 1979 Ill. LEXIS 255; 25 Ill. Dec. 634



January 26, 1979, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 30, 1979.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County, the Hon. Lloyd A. Van Duesen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tax collector (collector) sought review of a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which reversed a circuit court judgment and held that a statute abolishing an exemption from taxation for certain highway property was an impairment of a valid, existing contract between appellee authority and appellee taxpayer.


OVERVIEW: The county assessed real estate taxes on the taxpayer's leasehold interest in property owned by the authority. The taxpayer and the authority paid the taxes under protest and filed objections. The portion of the circuit court's decree that held that the leasehold interest was exempt from taxation and that enjoined the county from assessing the tax was vacated on the collector's motion. The authority appealed. The appellate court found that an amendment to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121, para. 100-22, which abolished an exemption from taxation of highway property if the property was leased for certain purposes, impaired a valid, existing contract. On appeal by the collector, the court reversed the appellate court and affirmed the circuit court. A taxpayer had no vested right in the continued existence of a taxing statute. The statute that created the exemption contained no language that would serve to form a contract that the grant of exemption would remain in force. The contention that the property was exempt because it was state property was without merit because the property sought to be taxed was the taxpayer's leasehold interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment which held that a statute abolishing an exemption from taxation for certain highway property was an impairment of a contract between the authority and the taxpayer. The court affirmed the circuit court judgment that held that the taxpayer's leasehold interest in property owned by the authority was not exempt from taxation.

 

433 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Northwestern University v. Evanston


No. 50383


Supreme Court of Illinois


74 Ill. 2d 80; 383 N.E.2d 964; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 380; 23 Ill. Dec. 93



December 4, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed from a judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the circuit court's dismissal of plaintiff university's declaratory judgment action concerning a city zoning ordinance forbidding professional sports. The appellate court found that, in light of the history of dispute over the ordinance, the university had fully exhausted its remedies before the city zoning authorities.


OVERVIEW: The university sought an amendment and a variation of the city's zoning ordinance, which forbid professional sports. While that action was pending, the university then sought declaratory relief that the zoning ordinance was unconstitutional. The circuit court dismissed the complaint for failure to exhaust local and administrative remedies. The appellate court reversed. On appeal, the court reversed the appellate court's judgment and affirmed the trial court's order dismissing the complaint. The court held that, if the university had challenged the validity of the city's ordinance on its face, it would not have needed to exhaust administrative remedies. However, the university did not avoid the exhaustion of remedies requirement because it merely alleged that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The university claimed that the ordinance was inherently arbitrary because it was permitted to maintain athletic facilities but prohibited from using them for professional sports. That proposition, however, was not self-evident. Whether other aspects of the differing impact of commercial versus noncommercial uses were significant required additional proof beyond the face of the ordinance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment that the university had exhausted its remedies before the city's zoning authorities. The court affirmed the circuit court's dismissal of the university's declaratory judgment action against the city.

 

434 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Berland


Nos. 50012, 50534 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


74 Ill. 2d 286; 385 N.E.2d 649; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 390; 24 Ill. Dec. 508



December 4, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Opinion Filed on Denial of Rehearing February 20, 1979, Reported at: 1979 Ill. LEXIS 454.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Marvin E. Aspen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were convicted of arson with intent to defraud an insurer in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 20 -- 1(b) (1969). The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) reversed the convictions. The State petitioned for leave to appeal under 65 Ill. 2d R. 315.


OVERVIEW: The lower court found that defendants received ineffective assistance of counsel because one attorney represented both of them and that the evidence was insufficient to support the convictions. The court found that each defendant has selected and retained the counsel to represent him, that neither had made any objection to the joint representation, and that the record was devoid of any evidence of an actual conflict of interest. The court found that a defendant must show an actual conflict of interest manifested at trial in order to prevail on a constitutional claim of ineffective assistance of counsel due to joint representation of co-defendants by a single attorney. The court found the evidence sufficient to support the convictions reasoning that a conviction could not be set aside merely because the evidence was contradictory and that circumstantial evidence could support a conviction as long as it produced a reasonable and moral certainty that defendant had committed the crime. The court found no basis to disturb the lower court's conclusion that the State's eyewitnesses were credible.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

435 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Compagnie Nationale Air France v. Giliberto


Nos. 50584, 50769


Supreme Court of Illinois


74 Ill. 2d 90; 383 N.E.2d 977; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 381; 23 Ill. Dec. 106



December 4, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 50584. -- Original petition for mandamus or prohibition. No. 50769. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Louis J. Giliberto, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Petition dismissed. Order vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant airlines sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the airlines motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction pursuant to the Warsaw Convention, 49 U.S.C.S. 3000 et seq., appellee passengers action against the airlines to recover damages for injuries suffered by the passengers at the hands of terrorists who hijacked their plane.


OVERVIEW: The passengers filed an action against the airlines to recover damages for injuries suffered by the passengers or for the deaths of the decedents of some of the passengers at the hands of terrorists who hijacked the airlines' plane in which the passengers or their decedents were traveling. The airlines moved to dismiss the action on the ground that the court lacked jurisdiction of the action by virtue of the Warsaw Convention, 49 U.S.C.S. 3000 et seq,. The circuit court denied the airlines' motion to dismiss. The court vacated the order of the circuit court and held that the circuit court was a distant, uninvolved, and inappropriate forum in relation to the parties and incidents that occurred thousands of miles away. There were other forums as between the passengers and airlines that would better serve the accomplishment of justice, the convenience of the parties, and the courts. Therefore, the circuit court abused its discretion in denying the motion of the airlines to dismiss the passengers action.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded the order of the circuit court.

 

436 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bilyew


No. 50330


Supreme Court of Illinois


73 Ill. 2d 294; 383 N.E.2d 212; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 366; 22 Ill. Dec. 736



November 22, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Williamson County, the Hon. Dorothy Spomer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The people appealed a judgment from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois), which held that the trial court unconstitutionally allocation the burden of proving that defendant was not competent to stand trial on defendant, and vacated his convictions.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held a competency hearing in defendant's murder, rape, and concealment of homicide trial. At the time of the hearing, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005 -- 2 -- 1(i) (1975), placed the burden of proving incompetency on the party that raised the issue - defendant, in this case. This statutory allocation was determined to be unconstitutional. In reversing the judgment, the court held that the application in theory of an unconstitutional burden of proof did not necessarily taint the competency hearing. The court noted that the allocation of the burden of proof in preponderance of the evidence issues only had meaning when the evidence was in equipoise. The court noted that the evidence, as relied upon by the trial court, was not in this state, and did not approach the preponderance standard. Accordingly, the allocation had not been necessary to tip the scales, and the competency finding was valid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of defendant and reinstated his convictions.

 

437 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Sass v. Kramer


No. 50390


Supreme Court of Illinois


72 Ill. 2d 485; 381 N.E.2d 975; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 331; 21 Ill. Dec. 528



October 6, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. Barry E. Puklin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The plaintiff individual filed an action against the defendant, the Secretary, Department of Transportation (DOT), State of Illinois, to quiet title to and for a writ of possession of land in the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois). The circuit court held that the price for the release of the land was unconstitutional and entered an order to quiet title in the individual and issued a writ of possession in his favor. The DOT appealed.


OVERVIEW: The DOT had acquired an easement for a public highway by virtue of a dedication and executed by the individual's predecessors in title to the land. The DOT contended that the action was in fact a suit against the state and was barred by the statute that proscribes making the state a party to an action in any court. The court held that the action could not have been maintained in any court. Since the property of the state was involved, the suit directly and adversely affected the state and the action was held by the court to have been one against the state. It was necessary for the trial court to determine whether, under the facts, there had in fact been an abandonment of the easement by the state. An abandonment of the land necessarily involved and affected an interest in property that had been conveyed to and vested in the state. Although the suit was nominally against an officer of the state, it clearly affected property of the state.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court that quieted title in the individual and issued a writ of possession in his favor. The court dismissed the action.
