Adler v. Illinois Bell Tel. Co.


No. 50443


Supreme Court of Illinois


72 Ill. 2d 295; 381 N.E.2d 294; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 311; 21 Ill. Dec. 216



September 19, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. George J. Schaller, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs commenced an action against defendants, a telephone company and city officials, challenging the constitutionality of a city's transmission of messages tax ordinance. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) dismissed plaintiffs' action for failure to state a cause of action. Plaintiffs filed a notice of appeal to the intermediate appellate court, and the court granted the city officials' motion to transfer the case directly to it.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, individually and as representatives of a class of persons similarly situated, claimed that the ordinance's exemption of interstate phone calls from the tax was an unreasonable classification which denied plaintiffs equal protection of the laws and that the ordinance was, on its face, unconstitutionally vague and indefinite. The court affirmed. The court stated that the city, by distinguishing between interstate and intrastate telephone calls, might seek to favor such commerce to attract business to the city and could find that administration of a tax upon interstate calls was unduly burdensome. The court found that because plaintiffs failed to rebut either consideration in their pleadings, such pleadings failed to state a cause of action as to the distinction in question. The court further found that plaintiffs failed to plead facts establishing that the ordinance was unconstitutionally vague and therefore an unlawful delegation of the legislative authority of the city council to the city officers.


OUTCOME: In plaintiffs' action challenging the constitutionality of the city's transmission of messages tax ordinance, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment for defendants.

Kerner v. State Employees' Retirement System


No. 50239


Supreme Court of Illinois


72 Ill. 2d 507; 382 N.E.2d 243; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 334; 21 Ill. Dec. 879



September 19, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 1, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Harvey Beam, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant governor's representative sought review of a judgment entered by the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois) reversing the trial court's judgment that the governor was not entitled to pension benefits terminated under Ill. Pension Code § 14-199, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 14-199 (1975). The governor's representative filed suit against appellees, retirement system and others, to recover the terminated benefits.


OVERVIEW: While in office, the governor participated in the state employee retirement system. The retirement system's board voted to terminate the governor's benefits due to the governor's conviction after leaving office of felonies related to service in office. The trial court reversed the board, ordering payment of arrearages for the then deceased governor. The court affirmed the appellate court, which reversed the trial court and held that the governor was not entitled to benefits pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 14-199 (1975). The court held that 1) the governor's conviction of federal felonies qualified as "any felony" under the statute, which was otherwise clear as to the denial of benefits in such cases; 2) the phrase "heretofore acquired" in the statute meant benefits acquired prior to the enactment of the felony provision and was not applicable to the governor, whose pension rights vested long after the statute's effective date; and 3) rights under Ill. Const. of 1970, art. XIII, § 5 were not impinged by the statute, because the lack of felony convictions was a condition of the contractual relationship to which the governor consented by applying for membership.


OUTCOME: In the governor's representative's suit to recover the governor's terminated pension benefits, the court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court sustaining the state retirement system board's denial of such pension benefits to the governor.

Consolidated Distilled Products, Inc. v. Allphin


No. 49288


Supreme Court of Illinois


73 Ill. 2d 19; 382 N.E.2d 217; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 343; 21 Ill. Dec. 853



September 19, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 1, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Raymond K. Berg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Revenue (department) appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted default judgment to plaintiffs, importing distributors of wine. The department had elected to stand on a motion to dismiss the circuit court had denied. The department made its appeal directly to the court pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 302(a), 58 Ill.2d R. 302(a).


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed two lawsuits against the department seeking to have a portion of § 1 of art. VIII of the Liquor Control Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 158 (1969) declared unconstitutional. Plaintiffs alleged entitlement to a credit for taxes paid between January 1968 and August 1971 because during that time distributors of wine made from grapes grown in Illinois were unconstitutionally taxed at a lower rate. The court reversed the circuit court's entry of a default judgment for plaintiffs, holding that under the principle of res judicata, plaintiffs were barred from relitigating their claim for a reimbursement of taxes. The court found that the plaintiffs were all parties in interest in a prior class action lawsuit involving the same issues for periods during 1970 and 1971. In that case, plaintiffs were denied relief because they had not borne the burden of the tax they claimed was unconstitutional. The court found that the judgment applied to the new lawsuit, thus precluding plaintiffs' claims. Although the new lawsuit claimed relief for taxes for an earlier time period, the prior decision was binding on all claims that could have been presented and decided.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause remanded to the trial court with directions to grant the department's motion to dismiss.

Supreme Court of Illinois


72 Ill. 2d 131; 379 N.E.2d 290; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 296; 19 Ill. Dec. 626

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which found that appellee messenger services, who operated a business for running racetrack bets were being unconstitutionally restrained from running their businesses and reversed the decision of the circuit court, which had dismissed the messenger services' complaint for failure to state a cause of action.

The state appealed. 442 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Grant


No. 49486


Supreme Court of Illinois


71 Ill. 2d 551; 377 N.E.2d 4; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 282; 17 Ill. Dec. 814



May 26, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Logan County, the Hon. John T. McCullough, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state sought leave to appeal reversal and remand of defendant's conviction for aggravated battery and obstructing a police officer from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), arguing that defendant was not entitled to jury instructions on both an insanity defense and on the defense of involuntary conduct, the jury was not confused, and the law had not been misstated.


OVERVIEW: A fight erupted, and a police officer was struck by defendant, who was diagnosed with alcoholism and epilepsy. At trial, a physician testified that because defendant experienced a seizure, he lacked substantial capacity to appreciate the criminality of his conduct or conform it to the law. Both parties tendered jury instructions regarding the insanity defense. The trial court charged the jury with the state's instruction, and defendant objected only to the second paragraph and the verdict forms. He was convicted at trial, but on appeal, won reversal. The state sought leave to appeal. On review, the court held that defendant proceeded at trial and on appeal solely on the theory of insanity. His objections did not preserve his right to now raise the defense of involuntary conduct. Failure to sua sponte instruct the jury on involuntary conduct did not deprive defendant of full and fair consideration as to his volitional capacity. Omission of such instruction was not substantial error requiring reversal. The verdict forms did not confuse the jury or prejudice defendant, there was no denial of equal protection, and defendant was not entitled to elect sentencing under a new act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court, and affirmed the trial court's conviction and sentence for aggravated battery.

Kujawinski v. Kujawinski


No. 50288


Supreme Court of Illinois


71 Ill. 2d 563; 376 N.E.2d 1382; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 283; 17 Ill. Dec. 801



May 26, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Donald J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant filed a declaratory judgment action, seeking a declaration that certain provisions of the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 101 et seq. (1977), were unconstitutional. The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) declared that several sections of the Act were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Divorce action party argued that § 801(b) of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 801(b), was unconstitutional, as it applied to property acquired prior to the effective date of the Act. Specifically, divorce action party contended that § 801(b) retrospectively applied the "marital property" provisions of § 503(b), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 503(b) (1977), to his case and thereby unconstitutionally impaired the obligation of contracts and unconstitutionally deprived him of property without due process of law. Divorce action party claimed that the retrospective application of § 801(b) conveyed a property interest to a spouse who had no interest in the property before the Act was passed into law. The court held that § 801(b) did not impair contractual obligations that were owed to third parties that were not a part of the dissolution proceeding because distribution of "marital property," as defined in § 503(b), was not triggered until the time of dissolution. The court also held that § 801(b) did not violate divorce action party's due process rights because § 801(b) did not directly divest or transfer property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment.

 

444 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Galvin v. Galvin


Nos. 49791, 50156, 50327 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


72 Ill. 2d 113; 378 N.E.2d 510; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 293; 19 Ill. Dec. 9



May 26, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Herbert R. Friedlund, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; orders vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant husband appealed from a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which ordered temporary support for plaintiff wife. The husband contended that the court lacked jurisdiction under § 2 of An Act in relation to married men and women (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 22 et seq. (1975), repealed and superseded by the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 101 et seq. (1977).


OVERVIEW: The wife filed a petition for separate maintenance in the county where she resided. The husband was served with a summons at the marital home in another county. The husband contested the court's jurisdiction and sought to quash the return of the summons, asserting that under § 2 of the Act, jurisdiction over the action existed solely in the county where the defendant resided. The circuit court asserted jurisdiction on the ground that § 2 of the Act was unconstitutional and ordered temporary support. On appeal, the wife argued that the error was cured when she filed an amended petition under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 101 et seq. The court reversed and vacated the order, concluding that § 2 of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 68, para. 23 (1975), was valid. The court held that the statutory scheme did not discriminate against the wife in defiance of equal protection because the Act required filing the action in the county where the defendant spouse resided whether the complaint was brought by the husband or by the wife. The wife's filing of an amended petition under the new law did not cure the error because the venue provisions of the Act were mandatory and jurisdictional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment as to the circuit court's finding that the venue provision of a former separate maintenance act was unconstitutional. The court vacated the orders for temporary support that were entered against the husband.

Chicago v. Wilson


No. 49229


Supreme Court of Illinois


75 Ill. 2d 525; 389 N.E.2d 522; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 402; 27 Ill. Dec. 458; 12 A.L.R.4th 1242



May 26, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. David J. Shields, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants were charged with wearing clothing of the opposite sex with the intent to conceal his or her sex in violation of Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 192-8. After their motion to dismiss the complaint based on the unconstitutionality of § 192-8 was denied, defendants were convicted of the charge. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) affirmed. Defendants were granted leave to appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendants, transsexuals undergoing psychiatric therapy in preparation for a sex-reassignment operation, were convicted of violating § 192-8 by wearing clothing of the opposite sex with the intent to conceal his or her sex. The appellate court affirmed their convictions. Reversing the judgments and remanding the case for dismissal, the court found that § 192-8, as applied to defendants, was unconstitutional. While the choice of appearance was not considered a "fundamental" right, the state's power to regulate matters pertinent to one's choice of a life-style which had not been demonstrated to be harmful to society's health, safety or welfare was restricted. Although cross-dressing was recommended as part of their preoperative therapy program and the city offered no evidence to substantiate its reasons for infringing on defendants' choice of dress under the circumstances, the court did not find the ordinance invalid on its face. However, it did find that § 192-8 as applied to defendants was an unconstitutional infringement of their liberty interest because individuals contemplating such surgery were entitled to the necessary therapy to insure that their decisions were correct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the appellate court and the circuit court, which convicted defendants of wearing clothing of the opposite sex with the intent to conceal his or her sex. The court remanded the cause to the circuit court with directions to dismiss.

 

446 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Garcia v. Tully


No. 49685


Supreme Court of Illinois


72 Ill. 2d 1; 377 N.E.2d 10; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 285; 17 Ill. Dec. 820



May 26, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Nathan M. Cohen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order vacated; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, publishers and taxpayers, challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dissolved a preliminary injunction under which defendants, county authorities and publisher, were enjoined from contracting to publish certain personal property and real estate tax assessment lists in accordance with § 104 of the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 585 (1975).


OVERVIEW: The finance committee of the board of commissioners recommended that the tax lists be published in defendant publisher's newspaper. Plaintiffs obtained a preliminary injunction that enjoined defendants from contracting to publish the tax lists. Plaintiffs challenged the trial court's subsequent dissolution of the preliminary injunction and the finding that § 104 was unconstitutional. On appeal, the trial court vacated the order dissolving the injunction and remanded. Section 104 in no manner limited a publisher's right to publish the tax lists; it merely prescribed certain qualifications to be met in order for a publisher to be eligible to publish them for compensation. The First Amendment prohibition of the abridgement of freedom of the press was not implicated, and the provisions of § 104 fell within the permissible bounds of time, place and manner restrictions on commercial speech. Also, there was no equal protection violation. Simultaneous circulation of defendant publisher's newspapers in the townships involved did not make them newspapers published within the township within the contemplation of § 104. Defendant publisher was not eligible to be compensated under § 104.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order dissolving the injunction and remanded the cause for further proceedings to determine whether the factual situation continued without change subsequent to the time involved in the proceeding.

In re Baker


No. 49925


Supreme Court of Illinois


71 Ill. 2d 480; 376 N.E.2d 1005; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 275; 17 Ill. Dec. 676



May 16, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. Robert J. Steigmann, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent juvenile sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which adjudged her to be in contempt of court for violation of the court's prior order that she would be held in contempt if she ran away from a children's home without leave. The circuit court also held that §§ 2-2(b) and 2-3(d) of the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, paras. 702-2 and 702-3 (1975), were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: After she repeatedly ran away from home, a 14 year old juvenile was adjudged to be a minor otherwise in need of supervision and she was placed in a children's home. When the juvenile left the home without leave, the circuit court entered another order saying that any further unauthorized leave would result in a finding of contempt. When she left the home again, a show cause petition was filed. When the juvenile sought to dismiss the petition, the circuit not only found her in contempt but ruled that §§ 2-2(b) and 2-3(d) of the Juvenile Court Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, paras. 702-2, 702-3 (1975), were unconstitutional. The court affirmed in part and reversed in part. The court held that the revised portions of the Juvenile Court Act, which allowed a finding of delinquency only on a finding of a violation of law, did not remove a court's inherent power of contempt. Therefore, the contempt finding was affirmed. However, the statute did prevent a court from finding a juvenile to be delinquent just because the juvenile had disobeyed the court's order. Further, the statutes in question were not unconstitutional, as they did not infringe on the court's inherent power.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's order finding the juvenile to be in contempt but reversed the circuit court's adjudication of delinquency.

 

448 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re March


No. 49022


Supreme Court of Illinois


71 Ill. 2d 382; 376 N.E.2d 213; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 265; 17 Ill. Dec. 214



April 3, 1978, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 26, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Disciplinary proceeding.



DISPOSITION: Respondent suspended.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney sought review of a judgment by appellee inquiry board (board). The attorney failed to comply with a subpoena and contended that the Fifth Amendment guarantee against self-incrimination applied to exempt him from any obligation to produce the requested documents or to testify to the matters in question.


OVERVIEW: An attorney challenged the board's recommendation that he be suspended for three years or that he be disbarred. The court held that disciplinary proceedings were not criminal in nature and that the Fifth Amendment privilege against self-incrimination did not apply. The court held that an attorney was not entitled to be automatically protected from the future use of testimony given by him in a disciplinary proceeding. The court held that such protection should be afforded only where testimony had been given after respondent's assertion of a valid Fifth Amendment privilege and the court's resulting grant of immunity from the future use of that testimony or its fruits in criminal proceedings. The court held that if the testimony would incriminate the attorney, the attorney could refuse to speak and that a grant of immunity from further use of the testimony could be sought from the court should the Administrator deem the testimony essential.


OUTCOME: The court held that the attorney had no automatic Fifth Amendment right against self-incrimination in a disciplinary proceeding. The court held that the proof was insufficient to support disbarment and that suspension for a year was appropriate because there was no record of prior disciplinary action against the attorney.

 

449 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Coryn v. Moline


No. 50005


Supreme Court of Illinois


71 Ill. 2d 194; 374 N.E.2d 211; 1978 Ill. LEXIS 245; 15 Ill. Dec. 776



March 23, 1978, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County, the Hon. L. E. Ellison, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff property owner sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois), which granted judgment on the pleadings for defendants, city, mayor, clerk, and treasurer, in the owner's action seeking to enjoin defendants from executing an ordinance that provided for additional taxes from certain property within a specified area. The trial court dismissed the action.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance designating an area within its boundaries as a special services area subject to additional taxes in order to fund the building and maintenance of a shopping mall. The property owner brought an action seeking to enjoin enforcement of the ordinance, and the trial court granted defendants' motion for judgment on the pleadings and dismissed the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court found that the property owner had not sustained his burden of showing that the ordinance was invalid, unauthorized, or unconstitutional. The court held that the language of Ill. Const. of 1970, art. VII, § 6(m) was to be construed liberally and that the power of the city to establish the special service area was broad enough to encompass the proposed shopping mall. The court noted that the involvement of substantial assets did not prevent a mall from being a "service." Further, the court noted that the fact that benefit would accrue to more than the designated area did not defeat the ordinance's validity. The court found no merit in any constitutional challenges to the ordinance under the due process or equal protection clauses.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment on the pleadings in favor of defendants in the property owner's action which sought to enjoin the enforcement of an ordinance which specified certain property as being within a special services area and subject to additional taxation. The dismissal of the action was also affirmed.

 

450 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wolgemuth


No. 49149


Supreme Court of Illinois


69 Ill. 2d 154; 370 N.E.2d 1067; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 419; 13 Ill. Dec. 40



December 12, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County, the Hon. Conway L. Spanton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Illinois sought review of a decision of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois) reversing a trial court's conviction of appellee defendant for unlawful possession of narcotics. The court determined that the trial court had erroneously denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence discovered incident to his unlawful, warrantless arrest.


OVERVIEW: A criminal defendant was convicted for unlawful possession of narcotics. The appellate court reversed the trial court's conviction of the defendant, finding that evidence discovered incident to his unlawful and warrantless arrest ought to have been suppressed. The court reversed the appellate court's decision, first finding that the arrest was not warrantless under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 107 -- 2(b), because a police officer may arrest a suspect on the basis of out-of-state warrants and in such situations the officer need not have the warrant on his person to make the arrest. Further, the court found that there was no statutory requirement in the State of Illinois that an arresting officer announce his authority and purpose prior to making an arrest. In reaching this decision, the court noted that in the absence of any constitutional law to the contrary, the requirement that an arresting officer announce his authority and purpose was but one factor to be weighed in determining the validity of any particular arrest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision, and affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

451 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Hoffmann v. Clark


No. 49012


Supreme Court of Illinois


69 Ill. 2d 402; 372 N.E.2d 74; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 440; 14 Ill. Dec. 269; 98 A.L.R.3d 886



December 12, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County, the Hon. Philip F. Locke, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, county and state officials, appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois), which granted declaratory and injunctive relief in favor of the property owners in an action brought by plaintiff property owners. The circuit court also held that §§ 20a -- 1 to 20a -- 3 of the Revenue Act of 1939 (Act), pertaining to the assessment and taxation of real estate used for agricultural purposes, were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The property owners' real estate was previously assessed at a value for farming purposes. As a result of alleged changes in the land use, tax bills were sent indicating that additional "rollback" taxes were due. On appeal, the court held (1) the property owners properly sought equitable relief to contest the constitutionality of the tax statutes, and their action was not barred under the doctrines of waiver and estoppel. (2) Sections 20a -- 1 to 20a -- 3 of the Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 501a -- 1 to 501a -- 3 (1973), did not constitute an invalid classification of real property for purposes of taxation in violation of Ill. Const. art. IX, §§ 4(a), 4(b). (3) In light of the state legislature's recognition of the need to preserve farmland and open space, the tax rollback provision, § 20a -- 3 of the Act, had a rational basis and did not constitute a denial of equal protection. (4) The statutory requirements that both rollback taxes and interest on the taxes be paid did not constitute a violation of due process because the amounts were due as the result of a changed land use after the property owners had requested and accepted the lower tax assessment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment granting declaratory and injunctive relief in favor of the property owners.

 

452 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Sanko v. Carlson


No. 49138


Supreme Court of Illinois


69 Ill. 2d 246; 371 N.E.2d 613; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 427; 13 Ill. Dec. 678



November 30, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 26, 1978. Opinion Modified April 3, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. John S. Page, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the clerk of the court for Kane County, Illinois, appealed the judgment of the Kane County Circuit Court (Illinois), which entered summary judgment for plaintiffs, four individuals and two businesses, regarding their suit for a declaratory judgment that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 25, para. 27.1(m) (1976 Supp.) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed suit seeking a declaration that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 25, para. 27.1(m) (1976 Supp.) was unconstitutional based on a claim that the statute, which outlined a schedule of court fees to be charged in the circuit courts of Illinois, violated Ill. Const. art. I, § 12. The statute imposed fees for filing tax objections in counties with a population of less than 1,000,000, but imposed no fee in counties with a population of more than 1,000,000. Plaintiffs contended that the statute violated the ban against special or local laws under the Illinois state constitution. Plaintiffs also contended that the statute violated Ill. Const. art. VII, § 9(a) because it inhibited plaintiffs ability to "obtain justice by law, freely." The trial court granted plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court found that the right to obtain justice did not mean that litigation could be conducted free of reasonable fees. The court further held that the statutory classification of counties by population was a rational classification based on an underlying tax collection scheme. As such, the court reversed the summary judgment granted to plaintiffs, and remanded with directions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's decision granting summary judgment to plaintiffs.

 

453 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jackson


No. 48704


Supreme Court of Illinois


69 Ill. 2d 252; 371 N.E.2d 602; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 428; 13 Ill. Dec. 667



November 30, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Marvin E. Aspen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant for armed robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried by a jury on a charge of armed robbery, found guilty, and sentenced to imprisonment. The trial court held unconstitutional an amendment to Ill. Code Crim. P., Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-4(f) (1975), which gave counsel the right to conduct voir dire of each prospective juror. On appeal, defendant argued that the trial court erred in failing to follow the procedure set forth in § 115-4(f), asserting that it superseded Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 234, which also related to voir dire, 58 Ill. 2d R. 234. At issue was whether Rule 234 or Ill. Code Crim. P., Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-4(f) (1975) regulated the method of voir dire examination of prospective jurors. The court affirmed the conviction and held that: (1) Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 234, 58 Ill. 2d R. 234, was a product of the court's supervisory and administrative responsibility; (2) the basic constitutional right to a trial by an impartial jury did not require that the parties themselves be permitted to interrogate the jurors; and (3) Ill. Code Crim. P. , Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115-4(f) (1975), was a legislative infringement upon the powers of the judiciary and was thus void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for armed robbery and held that the statute that gave counsel the right to conduct voir dire of prospective jurors was unconstitutional.

People ex rel. Harrod v. Illinois Courts Com.


No. 49118


Supreme Court of Illinois


69 Ill. 2d 445; 372 N.E.2d 53; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 441; 14 Ill. Dec. 248



November 30, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 26, 1978.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original petition for mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writ awarded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner judge sought a writ of mandamus against respondents, members of the Illinois Courts Commission, requesting that the commission be directed to expunge an order suspending the judge from his duties under Ill. Const. 1970, art. VI, § 15(e) (1970). Upon a complaint by the Illinois Judicial Inquiry Board, the commission found that the judge violated the sentencing mandates of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 61(c)(18), 58 Ill. 2d R. 61(c)(18).


OVERVIEW: A disciplinary action was initiated against the judge by a complaint filed with the commission by the Illinois Judicial Inquiry Board for alleged violations of the sentencing mandates of Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 61(c)(18), 58 Ill. 2d R. 61(c)(18), by requiring defendants to get haircuts, pick up litter, and carry a card identifying them as probationers. After serving his suspension, the judge filed a petition for a writ of mandamus directing the commission to expunge its order. The judge contended that his sentences were permissible under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-6-3(a) (1973), which established the conditions of probation. The court granted the writ, holding that (1) the court had responsibility to determine whether the commission's acts were beyond its constitutional grant of authority; (2) only judicial conduct that violated the supreme court rules of judicial conduct could be the subject of a complaint before the commission; (3) the commission exceeded its authority because it applied its own contrary interpretation and construction of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-6-3(a) (1973) to the judge's conduct, thus usurping a function that was vested solely in the courts.


OUTCOME: The court declared that the commission's order suspending the judge from his judicial duties was void, granted the judge's petition for a writ of mandamus, and directed the commission to expunge the suspension order from its records.

American Nat'l Bank & Trust Co. v. Kusper


Nos. 49266-67 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


69 Ill. 2d 374; 372 N.E.2d 66; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 438; 14 Ill. Dec. 261



November 30, 1977, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. F. Emmett Morrissey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, banks and individuals, challenged an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed counts of plaintiff's complaints against defendant tax officials on grounds that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 500.12b (1975) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, banks and individuals, brought a declaratory action against defendant tax officials to determine that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch.120, para. 500.21b (1975) was a valid legislative enactment exempting from personal property taxation for 1975 and subsequent years all personal property held by trustee for exclusive benefit of a natural person. The lower court dismissed counts of plaintiffs' complaints on the basis that the statute was unconstitutional. The court affirmed the lower court. The court considered the constitutionality of the statute and found it unconstitutional because the General Assembly did not impose a replacement tax as required by Ill. Const. art IX, § 5(c). The court stated that the General Assembly had to concurrently replace all revenue lost by the abolished taxes by imposing statewide taxes solely on those classes relieved of the burden of the taxes abolished.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's ruling dismissing counts of plaintiffs, banks and individuals', complaints on the basis that the tax law was unconstitutional because the General Assembly did not impose a required replacement tax.

People v. Johnson


No. 48349


Supreme Court of Illinois


68 Ill. 2d 441; 369 N.E.2d 898; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 391; 12 Ill. Dec. 191



October 17, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County, the Hon. William D. Vanderwater, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which granted appellee plumber's motion to dismiss the State's complaint against the plumber for violating the Plumbing License Law under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, para 116.36 (1973) by installing plumbing pipe and fixtures without a license. The plumber asserted that the provisions of the Act that prevented him from taking the licensing exam were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the criminal offense of engaging in the plumbing trade without a license. Defendant moved to dismiss the complaint, arguing that the requirement of a 5-year apprenticeship or completion of an approved course of study was an arbitrary obstruction to the taking of the examination and bore no reasonable relation to the protection of public health. The trial court granted defendant's motion and held the statutory prerequisites for the taking of the licensing examination unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that the requirement in the educational alternative that one enroll in a course of study equal to the time required and curricula offered by the University of Illinois lacked the specificity contemplated by the legislature when it authorized the Director to prescribe rules regarding the details of the Act's educational alternative. In light of the deficiencies in the statute, the alternative to apprenticeship that the Act purported to create was illusory. Unless properly implemented the education alternative preserved the seeds of the same monopolistic practices previously condemned in the apprentice program.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

 

457 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Chicago v. Groffman


No. 49001


Supreme Court of Illinois


68 Ill. 2d 112; 368 N.E.2d 891; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 363; 11 Ill. Dec. 283



October 5, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. John J. Moran, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged their convictions from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed the convictions for violations of Chicago, Ill., Municipal Code § 104.1-2, which made it unlawful to operate an unlicensed motion picture theatre.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with multiple violations of § 104.1-2 for operating unlicensed motion picture theatres. On appeal, the court reversed the convictions. The court concluded that § 101-5 dealt with the approval of licenses. The court found that motion pictures were within the scope of protection of the free speech and press guarantees of the First and Fourteenth amendments. The court then found that § 101-5 was unconstitutional because it contained no standards, and therefore, the exercise of a constitutional right was dependent upon the unfettered discretion or whim of the mayor. The court reasoned that the whole matter was purely subjective, and that constitutional rights were meaningless if they depended upon the discretion or whim of some official or administrator. The court held that the ordinance was so wanting in standards that it was void on its face.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendants' convictions for operating an unlicensed motion picture theatre.

 

458 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Stofer v. Motor Vehicle Casualty Co.


No. 48290


Supreme Court of Illinois


68 Ill. 2d 361; 369 N.E.2d 875; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 387; 12 Ill. Dec. 168



October 5, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 23, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Abraham W. Brussell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant insurers in two cases consolidated for appeal, brought an interlocutory appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held that a standard clause prescribed by regulation and providing a 12-month limitation period for bringing an action on an insurance policy was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative authority violating the separation of governmental branches and powers mandated by Ill. Const. art. II, § 1.


OVERVIEW: The state legislature granted the director of insurance authority to establish a standard policy form for fire and lightning insurance. That form contained a 12-month limitations period. Defendant insurers raised this clause as an affirmative defense in plaintiffs' actions. The trial court held that the clause was invalid because it violated the separation of powers mandated by Ill. Const. art. II, § 1. Defendant insurers brought interlocutory appeals which were consolidated. The court reversed and remanded the cases, holding that the limitations period was a valid delegation of legislative power. The court rejected the legislative vs. administrative distinction in favor of an analysis of the power to promulgate regulations pursuant to a comprehensive regulatory statute. The court said that the legislature, in delegating its authority, must provide sufficient identification of the persons and activities potentially subject to regulation; the harm sought to be prevented, and the general means intended to be available to the administrator to prevent the identified harm.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order striking defendants' affirmative defenses based on a limitations period provided in the policies as required by regulation. The delegation of authority to establish a limitations period by regulation was valid because the legislature adequately identified the harm sought to be remedied and the means intended to prevent such harm.

Andruss v. Evanston


Nos. 48832, 48841 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


68 Ill. 2d 215; 369 N.E.2d 1258; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 374; 12 Ill. Dec. 244



October 5, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 23, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Samuel B. Epstein, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant municipalities appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) entered in favor of plaintiff real estate brokers in their action seeking a declaration that the municipal ordinances that required the brokers have city licenses were void under Ill. Const. of 1970, art. VII, § 6(a), (h), and (i). The municipalities contended that their ordinances were valid under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 114 1/2, para. 124 (1975).


OVERVIEW: The municipalities contended that the circuit court erred in declaring that the ordinances were unconstitutional and in requiring each municipality to deposit all sums collected under their ordinances into a segregated account. On appeal, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment. The court held that the ordinances were invalid under the state constitution and the Real Estate Brokers and Salesmen License Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 114 1/2, para. 101 et seq. (1975). The court held that through the Act, the General Assembly determined that the state had the exclusive power to regulate the licensing of real estate brokers and salesmen. The court stated that para. 124 only reserved to municipalities the power to enact and enforce antidiscrimination ordinances, and that such laws could be enforced without the power to license the real estate brokers and salesmen. The court also found that the municipalities did not have the power to license brokers pursuant to the general licensing section of the Illinois Municipal Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-42-1 (1975). The court stated that the term "brokers" in para. 11-42-1 did not serve to repeal the Act.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment in favor of the real estate brokers.

Friedman & Rochester, Ltd. v. Walsh


No. 48924


Supreme Court of Illinois


67 Ill. 2d 413; 367 N.E.2d 1325; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 335; 10 Ill. Dec. 559



September 20, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Raymond S. Sarnow, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board sought review of an order from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 108 1/2, para. 6--213 of the Illinois Pension Code unconstitutional and in violation of the equal protection clauses of the United States and Illinois constitutions. The circuit court further found para. 6--213 to be in violation of the special legislation provisions of the Illinois Constitution.


OVERVIEW: The appeal involved the constitutionality of the provision of the Illinois Pension Code, para. 6--213, which granted immunity from garnishment orders to pensions paid pursuant to the Fireman's Annuity and Benefit Fund. Appellee creditor filed a complaint against appellee former fireman to enforce a judgment note. The former fireman received benefits from the board. Judgment was confessed on the note, and the judgment was confirmed. The creditor caused a wage deduction summons to be issued against the board. The board filed a motion to dismiss asserting the statutory exemption from attachment. The circuit court denied the motion and held para. 6--213 unconstitutional. The board appealed. On appeal, the court held that the legislative classification created by para. 6--213 could not be considered arbitrary or unreasonable merely because private pensioners did not enjoy the same immunity. Further, para. 6--213 did not contravene the dictates of equal protection of the law under either the constitution of Illinois or the constitution of the United States. In addition,. Para. 6--213 did not constitute prohibited special legislation in violation of Ill. Const. art. IV, § 13 (1970).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the circuit court, which found the statute unconstitutional and in violation of the special legislation provisions of the Illinois Constitution, was reversed. The cause was remanded.

People ex rel. Lignoul v. Chicago

Supreme Court of Illinois


67 Ill. 2d 480; 368 N.E.2d 100; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 343; 10 Ill. Dec. 614



September 20, 1977, Filed

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, city and national banks, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), that granted summary judgment in favor of plaintiff state in an action challenging the constitutionality of a city ordinance regulating branch banking.


OVERVIEW: The city enacted an ordinance that permitted and regulated branch banking. The state, on behalf of the commissioner of banks and trust companies, filed suit against the city claiming that the ordinance was unconstitutional. The national banks were permitted to intervene as defendants. The trial court granted the state's motion for summary judgment, and defendants appealed. The court affirmed. Ill. Const. art. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granting the state's motion for summary judgment in an action challenging the constitutionality of a ordinance regulating branch banking.

 

463 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Fujimura v. Chicago Transit Authority


No. 48927


Supreme Court of Illinois


67 Ill. 2d 506; 368 N.E.2d 105; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 346; 10 Ill. Dec. 619



September 20, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Nicholas J. Bua, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Chicago Transit Authority (CTA), sought review of a judgment entered by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which declared § 41 of the Metropolitan Transit Authority Act (Transit Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 341 (1973), unconstitutional in the personal injury actions brought by appellee victims. The court allowed a motion to directly take the interlocutory appeal that had been granted to the CTA.


OVERVIEW: The CTA operated mass transit systems in and around the City of Chicago. Section 41 of the Transit Act required the presentation of claims within six months of the incident. That provision also provided a one-year limitations period for actions against the CTA. By comparison, provisions of the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (Tort Immunity Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, paras. 8-101--8-102 (1973), provided time periods of one and two years. The victims challenged the constitutionality of § 41 in their actions against the CTA for that reason. The trial court declared § 41 unconstitutional. On appeal, that judgment was reversed. The matter was remanded. While the Tort Immunity Act provided for longer time periods, that fact, by itself, did not render § 41 of the Transit Act unconstitutional. Given that the sole purpose of the CTA was to operate mass transit systems, it performed a unique governmental function that could not be compared to the traditional functions of local governments. Therefore, there was a rational basis for providing shorter limitations periods. As a result, § 41 of the Transit Act did not violate equal protection standards.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which had declared the notice and limitations periods provided by the Transit Act unconstitutional. The matter was remanded for further proceedings.

 

464 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Department of Public Aid


No. 48510


Supreme Court of Illinois


67 Ill. 2d 529; 367 N.E.2d 1286; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 348; 10 Ill. Dec. 520



September 20, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County, the Hon. William J. Sunderman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff food stamp recipients challenged a decision of defendant Illinois Department of Public Aid (IDPA), which increased the price of their food stamps. The Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois) held in favor of the recipients, finding that the increase violated § 2019(d) of the Food Stamp Act of 1964, 7 U.S.C.S. § 2011 et seq., and that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, par. 11 -- 8.7)(1975) and 7 U.S.C.S. § 2022 were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Aid to Families with Dependent Children program (AFDC), 42 U.S.C.S. § 601 et seq., exempted a portion of earned income in determining the amount of aid. However, the Food Stamp Act of 1964, 7 U.S.C.S. § 2011 et seq., did not exempt any earned income. On appeal, the recipients asserted that AFDC exempt income should be disregarded in computing the cost of food stamps. They claimed that its inclusion decreased AFDC aid, thus, violating 7 U.S.C.S. § 2019(d). The court reversed, holding that a reduction in AFDC aid due to an increase in food stamp price was not a decrease of a welfare grant under 7 U.S.C.S. § 2019(d). The state properly made no distinction between food stamp recipients and nonrecipients. The court declined to add to the Food Stamp program an incentive for employment not included by Congress. The court also reversed the trial court's finding that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, par. 11 -- 8.7 (1975) and 7 U.S.C.S. § 2022 were unconstitutional. Those sections did not deny recipients the right of judicial review. IDPA food stamp decisions were reviewable under common law certiorari and food stamp recipients had standing to challenge entitlement decisions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and concluded that the recipients were not entitled to any relief on their complaint.

 

465 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Borchers


No. 48666


Supreme Court of Illinois


67 Ill. 2d 578; 367 N.E.2d 955; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 351; 10 Ill. Dec. 346



September 20, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County, the Hon. Richard Mills, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a decision by the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of theft of more than $ 150, theft of less than $ 150, and official misconduct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that § 3-4(c)(2) of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 3-4(c)(2) (1973), barred the state prosecution. The court reviewed the records in the federal and state trials, and the records were practically alike as far as the evidence presented was concerned. Indeed, it could have been said that the two records excepting, of course, proof of use of the mails, were nearly interchangeable, even as to the reputation witnesses called by defendant. With a few minor exceptions, the testimony was the same. Viewing the question realistically and set in a practical frame, that court considered that the questions were the same. The controlling fact or question in both prosecutions was whether defendant had an intent to commit a fraud. The verdict of acquittal in the federal prosecution resolved this factual question in favor of defendant, and his conviction under the state prosecution required that the same factual question to be resolved in favor of the prosecution. Thus, relitigating this factual question was violative of the doctrine of collateral estoppel. According, the court reversed the judgment of conviction.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded defendant's convictions for theft of more than $ 150, theft of less than $ 150, and official misconduct.

 

466 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Regenold v. Baby Fold, Inc.


No. 49046


Supreme Court of Illinois


68 Ill. 2d 419; 369 N.E.2d 858; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 390; 12 Ill. Dec. 151



September 20, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 23, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County, the Hon. James A. Knecht, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant mother challenged a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois) reversing the decision of the trial court holding that mother's consent to her infant's adoption was invalid and ordering the return of the infant.


OVERVIEW: Mother executed a surrender document pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 4, para. 9.1-10 (1975) and had physically surrendered her child to adoption agency. In her petition for a writ of habeas corpus, she contended that the surrender was not valid because it was executed as the result of fraud and duress. On appeal, the court held that to preserve the legislative policy, a court should not set aside a consent or a surrender executed in accordance with para. 9.1-10 unless the one seeking to invalidate the document proved by clear and convincing evidence that its execution was procured by fraud or duress. The court found that mother did not sustained this burden of proof. The court determined that mother did not contend that anything adoption agency did involved a wrongful intent or was calculated to deceive. Thus, the court held that mother's allegation of fraud was patently not supported by clear and convincing proof.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

467 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Nabisco, Inc. v. Korzen


Nos. 48251, 48313


Supreme Court of Illinois


68 Ill. 2d 451; 369 N.E.2d 829; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 392; 12 Ill. Dec. 122



September 20, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 23, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 48251. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. F. Emmett Morrissey, Judge, presiding.

No. 48313. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Francis T. Delaney, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 48251 -- Reversed and remanded. No. 48313 -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lessees of land belonging to tax-exempt university fought the tax assessment and collection of property taxes on the leased property by defendants, county, tax assessor, clerk, and treasurer (county). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) enjoined collection of the taxes and found that taxes were properly assessed against one of the lessees, who appealed. The county appealed the judgment for the other lessee.


OVERVIEW: The corporate charter of the university was amended to provide that its property was tax-exempt. Under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 507 (1939), taxes were assessed on leased land even though the property was tax-exempt in the hands of the lessor. Two lessees of land from the university challenged the county's tax assessment of the leased property. One trial court found in favor of the county, and the other trial court enjoined taxation against the other lessee. The one lessee and the county appealed the judgments against them. The court found for the county in both cases and held that the land was taxable. The court found that the tax exemption did not flow to a lessee who was not granted tax-exempt status unless the legislature clearly stated so. In addition, the decision had retroactive application because it was not a change in existing law.


OUTCOME: The court found in favor of the county and held that the property that was leased by the lessees from the university was subject to taxation.

 

468 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


GTE Automatic Electric, Inc. v. Allphin


No. 48578


Supreme Court of Illinois


68 Ill. 2d 326; 369 N.E.2d 841; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 384; 12 Ill. Dec. 134



September 20, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 23, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Daniel A. Covelli, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a decision of the Appellate Court for the First District, Illinois, which affirmed the lower court's grant of appellee director of revenue's motion to dismiss in an action seeking a judgment declaring that certain of the taxpayer's sales should be excluded in computing the fraction of its business income to be allocated to Illinois.


OVERVIEW: A taxpayer brought an action which sought a judgment declaring that certain of its sales should be excluded in computing the fraction of its business income to be allocated to Illinois. The circuit court dismissed the action, the appellate court affirmed, and the taxpayer appealed. The court affirmed, holding that although the taxpayer had not exhausted its administrative remedies, it would consider the merits. The court found that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 3 -- 304(a)(3)(B) did not make a "drop-shipment" sale, where both the origin and destination of the sale were outside the state and the taxpayer was not taxable in either of those states, a sale "within Illinois." The court found that the General Assembly failed to take into account this type of sale, and there was a gap in § 304(a)(3)(B). The court held that the supplier's selection of an out-of-state inventory from which to make shipment to an out-of-state customer did not of itself show insufficient nexus to render those sales includable, and it followed that the supplier's selection of Illinois as the place from which to make shipment did not of itself show insufficient nexus.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment upholding the decision that granted the director of revenue's motion to dismiss the taxpayer's action seeking exclusion from income of certain sales.

OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by way of complaint with a violation of § 406(a)(1). He moved to dismiss the action against him, alleging that the substance he was charged with illegally prescribing, diethylpropion, was not among the substances enumerated in the Act on the date of his alleged violation. 470 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Renslow v. Mennonite Hospital


No. 48782


Supreme Court of Illinois


67 Ill. 2d 348; 367 N.E.2d 1250; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 328; 10 Ill. Dec. 484; 91 A.L.R.3d 291



August 8, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County, the Hon. Luther H. Dearborn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed the decision of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois) reversing the decision of the trial court that dismissed plaintiff's cause of action on behalf of her minor child for negligence for acts committed before the child was conceived.


OVERVIEW: When plaintiff was an adolescent, defendants gave her a blood transfusion with blood that was incompatible with her own. As a result of the transfusion, plaintiff's minor child was born premature and had a variety of health problems. Plaintiff sued defendants on behalf of herself and her minor child. The trial court dismissed the action on behalf of the minor child. The appellate court reinstated the claim. Defendants sought further review. The court affirmed the reinstatement of plaintiff's claim on behalf of the minor child because the fetus did not have to be viable at the time prenatal injuries were sustained to support an action for those injuries. Further, as the risk of harm to the child was reasonably foreseeable, the delay between defendants' acts and the injury to plaintiff's minor child did not bar the action. Finally, defendants could be held liable to a person whose existence was not apparent at the time of their acts; therefore, relief was not barred simply because the child was not conceived at the time of defendants' negligent actions.


OUTCOME: The order reversing the dismissal of plaintiff's claims on behalf of her minor child was affirmed because defendants could be held liable to a person whose existence was not apparent at the time of their acts: therefore, relief was not barred simply because the child was not conceived at the time of defendants' negligent actions.

People v. Redmond


No. 49360


Supreme Court of Illinois


67 Ill. 2d 242; 367 N.E.2d 703; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 319; 10 Ill. Dec. 250



June 27, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Frank B. Machala, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to quash a charge of attempted murder presented in an information without the benefit of a probable cause hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the crime of aggravated battery and provided with a preliminary hearing for the determination of probable cause. Subsequently, defendant was charged with attempted murder based on the same events, but not provided with another probable cause hearing. Defendant moved to quash the charge of attempted murder on the ground that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 111-2(e) (1975) was unconstitutional under Ill. Const. art. I, § 7 (1970) and the United States Constitution, which the trial court granted. The court held that the statute, which permitted a criminal charge to be brought by information if it was based on the same events for which a probable cause hearing had been conducted, was not unconstitutional as the Illinois Constitution permitted the General Assembly to eliminate or modify the requirement for a grand jury. The court further found that the statute did not violate the United States Constitution and the court reversed the order of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the trial court, which granted defendant's motion to quash the charge of attempted murder contained in an information without the benefit of a probable cause hearing, and remanded the matter for further proceedings.

Anderson v. Schneider

Supreme Court of Illinois

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, potential candidates for public office (candidates), sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) in favor of appellee election officials, in the candidates suit to have their names printed on the ballot.


OVERVIEW: The candidates sought to have their names places on the ballot for an election. The officials refused to print the names and contended that the candidates were in violation of Ill. Rev. The court reversed the prior order in favor of the officials.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the prior judgment in favor of the officials, having determined that denial of the printing of the candidates names on the ballot was an unconstitutional violation of the rights of the candidates and the electorate.

Urbana v. Houser


No. 48793


Supreme Court of Illinois


67 Ill. 2d 268; 367 N.E.2d 692; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 323; 10 Ill. Dec. 239



June 1, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County, the Hon. Creed D. Tucker, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Champaign County (Illinois), which held that the city was not empowered by statute to demolish appellee building owner's building.


OVERVIEW: The city, a home rule municipality, filed a complaint for demolition against the building owner under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-31-1 (1975). The building owner filed a motion to dismiss, which the trial court granted on the basis that the statute had not authorized the city to conduct demolition proceedings. The city appealed, and the appeal was transferred to the court, which reversed. The court noted that the trial court's decision was based on an amendment to § 11-31-1 that stated that the act did not apply within the jurisdiction of any home rule unit. The court declared that amendment void because it would have created an unconstitutional classification. The court found no reason for differentiating between the classes of municipalities to which demolition authority applied and those to which it did not apply. The court severed the unconstitutional provision and held that the city had the authority to conduct demolition proceedings under the remainder of the act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed a decision that the city was not empowered to demolish the building owner's building.

Grand Liquor Co. v. Department of Revenue


No. 48412


Supreme Court of Illinois


67 Ill. 2d 195; 367 N.E.2d 1238; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 313; 10 Ill. Dec. 472



June 1, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 3, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County, the Hon. Raymond S. Sarnow, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Revenue assessed plaintiff taxpayer for a tax deficiency due under the Retailers' Occupation Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 440 et seq. (1973), and the Municipal Retailers' Occupation Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 8-11-1 (1973). Defendant appealed from the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the trial court's order confirming the assessment.


OVERVIEW: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision. The Retailers' Occupation Tax Act provided that proof of the department's correction of the retailers' occupation tax returns could be made by a reproduced copy of the department's record relating thereto and that such reproduced copy was prima facie proof of the correctness of the amount of tax due. In this case, the department based its correction on a computer printout, which related to the records on file with the state as to payment of the retailers' occupation tax and municipal retailers' occupation tax. However, the department auditor who testified in the trial court acknowledged that he did not know what data were fed into the computer. The court held that before the department's correction of the taxpayer's occupation tax returns based on the computer printout was deemed prima facie proof of its correctness pursuant to the Retailers' Occupation Tax Act, the department must explain the method it employed in reaching the assessment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision and remanded the cause to the department for a new hearing consistent with the directions expressed in the opinion.

People v. Estate of Scott


No. 48537


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 522; 363 N.E.2d 823; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 298; 6 Ill. Dec. 876



May 20, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Marvin E. Aspen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pleaded guilty in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) to the offense of attempted robbery and was sentenced to five years' probation. The trial court denied the People's motion for costs pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 180-3 (1975) from defendant's deposit of bail security, ordered a refund, and the People appealed. Defendant died while the appeal was pending, and her estate was substituted for her.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the statutory cost pattern was unconstitutionally vague on its face and that the manner in which it was applied and enforced violated the equal protection clause of the Fourteenth Amendment in that it created three separate classifications of burdened individuals. Further, defendant claimed that failing to provide a hearing before imposing the costs violated procedural due process guarantees. Briefs were filed by amici curiae. The trial court held that the statutory cost scheme was unconstitutional and entered an order requiring that the bail security that was deposited be refunded to defendant. In reversing the decision, the court held that the method selected by the legislature for recouping the costs of administering the criminal justice system was not unconstitutional and that there was nothing in the statute that served to deny procedural due process. Defendant had the opportunity and did object to the People's motion at trial. Finally, the court held that the cost statutes were not invalid by reason of the manner in which they were applied. The record did not show that the statutes were unconstitutionally applied to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's decision and remanded for further proceedings consistent with the opinion.

Day v. Regional Transp. Authority


No. 48789


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 533; 363 N.E.2d 829; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 300; 6 Ill. Dec. 882



May 20, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted the motion to strike of defendants, Regional Transportation Authority and state officials (RTA), and dismissed the citizen's complaint that challenged the constitutionality of certain municipal finance and bonding provisions.


OVERVIEW: The citizen filed a complaint that challenged the constitutionality of bonding and finance provisions of the Regional Transportation Authority (RTA) under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 2/3, para. 701.01 et seq. (1975) and a related provision which allocated to the RTA a portion of vehicle registration fees pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 2-119(d) (1975). The trial court granted the RTA's motion to strike and dismissed the citizen's complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed the decision of the trial court. The court held that bonding and finance provisions at issue did not create "state debt" under Ill. Const. art. The court determined that the laws did not constitute an unconstitutional delegation of power to the RTA. The court held that the vehicle registration fees were uniformly assessed across the state and the distribution of the funds could lawfully vary depending on the needs of the local government.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court that granted the RTA's motion to strike and dismissed the citizen's complaint.

People v. Klick


No. 48332-33 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 269; 362 N.E.2d 329; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 252; 5 Ill. Dec. 858; 95 A.L.R.3d 406



April 5, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John J. McDonnell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110A, para 302(a)(1) (1973), that granted defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint against them for disorderly conduct in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 26-1(a)(2) (1973).


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged in separate complaints with disorderly conduct in that they knowingly made a telephone call or calls with the intent to annoy another in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 26-1(a)(2) (1973). The trial court granted defendants' motions to dismiss on the grounds that § 26-1(a)(2) was unconstitutional. The state argued that the statute was not overly broad in that it merely regulated conduct and did not deprive citizens of their U.S. Const. amend. I freedoms. Defendants claimed that the statute deprived them of first amendment freedoms and made criminal otherwise protected conduct. The supreme court held that the legislature could not abridge one's first amendment freedoms merely to avoid slight annoyances caused to others. Section 26-1(a)(2), by its very terms, proscribed any call made with the intent to annoy, regardless of its purpose or nature. Such an unlimited intrusion on first amendment freedom was not permitted. The court concluded that § 26-1(a)(2) made criminal conduct that was protected by the U.S. Const. amend. I, XIV and was therefore overly broad.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court that dismissed the complaint against defendants for disorderly conduct.

People v. McCullum


No. 48207


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 306; 362 N.E.2d 307; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 255; 5 Ill. Dec. 836

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Thomas W. Vinson, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Illinois sought review of the order from the Third District Appellate Court (Illinois), which reversed defendant's conviction for unlawful possession of over 30 grams of heroin. The appellate court determined that § 5-2-1(i) of Unified Code of Corrections (Code), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-2-1(i) (1973), was not applicable to defendant's fitness hearing. Defendant cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: During the course of her trial and after the code became effective, defendant raised the issue of her competency to stand trial. The trial court held a competency hearing and instructed the jury that defendant had the burden of proving herself unfit to stand trial in accordance with § 1005-2-1(i). Defendant appealed and the appellate court reversed her conviction finding that the Code was not applicable to defendant because the action against her began before the effective date of the Code. On appeal, the court affirmed the appellate court's reversal of defendant's conviction and remanded the action for a new trial. The court disagreed with the appellate court that the Code did not apply, because the facts which gave rise to defendant's fitness hearing were not presented until after the effective date of the Code. On the cross-appeal, the court found that the police officer's failure to leave a copy of the search warrant did not invalidate the search.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's reversal of defendant's conviction on the grounds that the section of the Code that required defendant to prove she was unfit to stand trial was unconstitutional and remanded the action for a new trial.
