Underground Contrs. Ass'n v. Chicago


No. 48109


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 371; 362 N.E.2d 298; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 264; 5 Ill. Dec. 827



April 5, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Raymond K. Berg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment against appellant city and in favor of appellee contractors association in an action brought by the association for declaratory relief that sought to have declared invalid a plan devised and used by the city's purchasing agent to encourage the hiring of minorities by firms that bid on public works projects.


OVERVIEW: The city adopted a canvassing formula, which allowed the city's purchasing agent to reduce a bid by a limited amount determined by the percentage of total hours minority workmen would have been employed on the project; thus, the recipient need not have actually been the lowest responsible bidder as required by the statute. The association filed suit and requested declaratory judgment. Finding no genuine, disputed issue of fact, the circuit court entered an order of summary judgment in favor of the association and found that the canvassing formula was invalid. The city appealed. The court found that there were two main requirements for standing to bring an action for declaratory relief. There had to be an actual controversy and the party seeking the declaration had to be interested in the controversy. The court held that the association's representational capacity alone was not enough to give it standing, absent a showing that it had a recognizable interest in the dispute, peculiar to itself and capable of being affected. Because the association did not show that it had a direct interest in the action, the association could not have maintained an action for declaratory relief.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment and remanded with directions to dismiss the complaint.

 

480 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Snow v. Dixon


No. 48694


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 443; 362 N.E.2d 1052; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 273; 6 Ill. Dec. 230



April 5, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 27, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Donald J.O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed as modified; cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer brought an action against defendants, state officials and railroad, to restrain and enjoin the disbursement of public moneys by officers of the state under the Public Monies Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 102, para. 11 et seq. (1975). The Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granted summary judgment for the taxpayer. The state officials and railroad appealed.


OVERVIEW: The predecessor railroad received a special tax rate (rate) under its charter, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 102, para. 373, 374 (1975). The railroad bought the predecessor railroad's assets and used the rate. The court affirmed the decision that the railroad was unable to use the rate. The court held that the taxpayer had standing under the Act to bring the lawsuit. The amount of money spent to collect the tax was irrelevant where the taxpayer was injured by the misapplication of the funds. Under 49 U.S.C.S. § 5, the Interstate Commerce Commission (ICC) approved the transaction between the railroads because the public interest was met. Because the state was unable to interfere with the ICC's jurisdiction and the ICC made no findings about the transfer of the rate, the purchase did not include the rate. Because the charter did not state that the rate was transferable and there was no law that transferred the rate, the rate was not transferable. The predecessor railroad was dissolved. The court modified the amount of the taxes owed to the difference between what was paid and what was owed and ordered that the tax be calculated based on each county the railroad owned property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision for the taxpayer, but remanded the decision because of the court's modification of the amount of the retrospective taxes owed by the railroad and how the tax was to be calculated.

Gilliland v. Board of Education


No. 48375


Supreme Court of Illinois


67 Ill. 2d 143; 365 N.E.2d 322; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 309; 8 Ill. Dec. 84



April 5, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Tazewell County, the Hon. James D. Heiple, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant board of education sought review of an order of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which reversed the affirmance of the board's decision to dismiss appellee teacher.


OVERVIEW: The trial court affirmed the board's decision dismissing the teacher for incompetence and cruelty. The appellate court reversed, holding that the board's finding that the causes for dismissal were not remediable was against the manifest weight of the evidence. The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and affirmed the trial court's decision because the cumulative effect of the evidence was such as to preclude a holding that the board's findings were contrary to the manifest weight of that evidence. The record contained considerable testimony of damage to the teacher's students and to the school itself, including detailed expert testimony that the causes for dismissal were irremediable. There was evidence that the teacher's complained-of conduct extended over a period of four school years despite numerous parental complaints culminating in discussions between the teacher and her superiors concerning her conduct. Further, the board did not sit idly by, permitting remediable causes to expand into irremediable ones and thus evade the notice requirement. The board discussed the teacher's conduct with her and sent her a letter expressing the board's concerns.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's decision and affirmed the trial court's judgment affirming the dismissal of the teacher.

People v. C. Betts Realtors, Inc.


Nos. 48359-64 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 144; 361 N.E.2d 581; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 234; 5 Ill. Dec. 258



March 23, 1977, Filed

DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, the People sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed complaints charging defendants with unlawful solicitation for the sale of residential property after receiving notice that the owner did not desire to sell or be solicited for such sale, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 70-51(d)(2) (1973).


OVERVIEW: Defendants filed motions to dismiss and alleged that para. 70-51(d)(2) was unconstitutional. The trial court agreed and dismissed the People's complaints. On appeal, the court at the outset found that the complaints were sufficient to charge defendants with the unlawful solicitation of the sale of real estate. The complaints charged that defendants solicited an owner of residential property after the owner had notified defendants in writing that he did not desire to sell or list his property. The court noted that the United States Supreme Court had rejected the notion that a vendor had a constitutional right to send unwanted material into the home of another. The court also found para. 70-51(d)(2) was not fatally vague because it gave defendants a fair warning and clearly set forth the prohibited conduct.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the cases for further proceedings.

Sweet v. Department of Public Aid


No. 48509


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 195; 361 N.E.2d 1118; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 241; 5 Ill. Dec. 590



March 23, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County; the Hon. William J. Sunderman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant public aid department sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Vermilion County (Illinois), which held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 4--1.3 and all regulations promulgated by the department thereto were invalid and unenforceable because they violated 42 U.S.C.S. § 602(a)(8)(A)(ii), awarded appellee benefits recipient $ 1,662, and held that the recipient was entitled to benefits in the future.


OVERVIEW: The benefits recipient filed a claim with the department for medical assistance under the state's Aid to Families With Dependent Children Related (AFDC) program. Her claim was denied on the grounds that she was ineligible for medical assistance because her husband had a full-time job and her children were not dependent within the meaning of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 4--1.3 (1975). On appeal, the department argued that the trial court erred in reversing its denial of benefits to the recipient. Upon review, the court agreed with the department and reversed the judgment of the trial court. The unfairness of the recipient's situation resulted in large degree from the fact that her husband was employed at a very low wage rate. It was not a constitutional requirement that the programs were structured in such a manner as to remedy the problem of inadequate wages in addition to the stated goals of those programs. The record supported the decision of the department that the dependency requirement established by state and federal law and regulations was not met, for which reason the recipient was ineligible for AFDC benefits or for medical assistance.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, reinstated the decision of the department, and held that the recipient failed to show that her children met the dependency requirement necessary to receive benefits under the AFDC program established by state and federal law.

People v. Yocum


Nos. 47934, 48013 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 211; 361 N.E.2d 1369; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 242; 5 Ill. Dec. 665



March 23, 1977, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Champaign County; the Hon. Birch E. Morgan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court aff'd in pt. and rev'd in pt; circuit court aff'd.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant and the state petitioned for leave to appeal a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which reversed in part and affirmed in part a judgment of a circuit court that convicted defendant, on a plea of guilty, for aggravated incest under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-10(a), (b) (1973)) and indecent liberties with an adopted minor daughter.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-10(a), (b) (1973) unconstitutional and reversed the aggravated incest conviction. Defendant had contended that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-10(a), (b) (1973), and the female counterpart, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-11(a) (1973) discriminated between fathers and mothers, violating Ill. Const. of 1970 art. I, § 18, which assured equal protection should not be denied or abridged on account of sex. A male was guilty of aggravated incest under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-10(a), (b) (1973), and a female was guilty of only incest by committing the same conduct with a minor son under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-11(a) (1973). Aggravated incest carried a potential 1 to 20 years in prison and incest carried a potential 1 to 10 years in prison. The appellate court affirmed the indecent liberties conviction. On further appeal, consolidating the petitions for leave to appeal, the court held Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-10(a), (b) (1973) constitutional based on precedent and reversed in part the appellate court's decision in favor of the state. The conviction for aggravated incest was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in part the judgment of the appellate court by finding the aggravated incest statute constitutional and by affirming the circuit court's conviction for aggravated incest in favor of the state. The court affirmed in part the judgment of the appellate court, which affirmed the indecent liberties conviction and sentence.

People v. Phillips


No. 48726


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 412; 362 N.E.2d 1037; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 269; 6 Ill. Dec. 215



March 23, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 26, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County; the Hon. Raymond O. Horn, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Illinois challenged an order from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois), which reversed a decision that held defendant ineligible for treatment in lieu of prosecution under the Dangerous Drug Abuse Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91 1/2, para. 120, and remanded for another determination of defendant's eligibility.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted for unlawful possession of a controlled substance. Two burglary charges were consolidated with the indictment. Defendant filed a petition, claiming that he was an addict under the Act, so that he elected to undergo treatment instead of prosecution. The trial court found him ineligible because he was on probation for a prior offense and his probation officer did not consent to treatment. Defendant then pled guilty to the charges. The appellate court reversed the decision and remanded for a determination of defendant's eligibility under the Act. In reversing the decision and affirming the trial court's determination, the court found that the failure of defendant's probation officer to consent to treatment did not constitute an interference with judicial authority by a nonjudicial officer in violation of Ill. Const. art. VI, § 1 (1970). The required consent of the probation officer did not dictate the sentence or infringe upon the sentencing power of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's order and affirmed the trial court's decision, which held that defendant was ineligible for treatment in lieu of prosecution under the Act.

 

486 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. Chicago


Nos. 48399, 48611 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 423; 362 N.E.2d 1030; 1977 Ill. LEXIS 271; 6 Ill. Dec. 208



March 23, 1977, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 26, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 48399. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Daniel A. Covelli, Judge, presiding.

No. 48611. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Walter P. Dahl, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two separate actions plaintiff taxpayers challenged the constitutionality of the Chicago Transaction Tax Ordinance. The Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois) and the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) both held the tax ordinance invalid and defendant city appealed from those judgments.


OVERVIEW: The first taxpayers attacked those portions of Chicago, Ill. Municipal Code ch. 200.1--2 dealing with the tax on the lease or rental of personal property. They alleged that the transaction tax violated their due process and equal rights and created an arbitrary classifications as to items taxed and different rates paid. The appellate court held the tax invalid. The second taxpayers challenged those provisions of the act relating to the tax on real estate transfers, alleging similar infirmities as the first taxpayers. The trial court declared the ordinance unconstitutional as applied to transfers of real property. The suits were consolidated for appeal. The court held that (1) legislative bodies had broad powers in establishing classifications defining the objects of taxation which would withstand constitutional attack so long as the classifications were reasonable, (2) the taxpayers bore the burden of proving the classifications to be unreasonable, (3) the language of Chicago, Ill. Municipal Code ch. 200.1--2(A)(5) did not create an unreasonable classification of transactions subject to tax, and (4) the complaints failed to overcome the ordinance's presumption of constitutionality.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the trial court and the appellate court and remanded the cases with directions to enter an order granting the city's motions to dismiss the complaints.

 

487 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ratliff


No. 48244


Supreme Court of Illinois


65 Ill. 2d 314; 357 N.E.2d 1172; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 440; 2 Ill. Dec. 729



December 3, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Anthony J. Bosco, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of the decision of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed a conviction of defendant for violation of bail bond under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 32-10 (1972).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was originally charged with the offense of theft and released on bail. After several court appearances and continuances, the case was set for trial. When defendant failed to appear in court, the trial court forfeited defendant's bond and issued a warrant for defendant's arrest. The trial court entered judgment on the bond forfeiture pursuant to § 110-7(g) of the Code of Criminal Procedure of 1963, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110-7(g) (1973). Defendant was subsequently charged by information with the offense of violation of bail bond. After waiving his right to a trial by jury, defendant was convicted in a bench trial. Defendant testified that he was incarcerated for all but eight days. The trial court found defendant guilty. The appellate court reversed and the court affirmed. The court held that the failure to prove that notice was sent did not preclude the State from proving that defendant acted willfully. However, the testimony of defendant tended to establish that defendant's failure to appear was not willful. Defendant's failure to surrender himself during the nine days he was released did not constitute sufficient proof that he was guilty of the offense.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision reversing defendant's conviction.

 

488 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brooks


No. 48167


Supreme Court of Illinois


65 Ill. 2d 343; 357 N.E.2d 1169; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 445; 2 Ill. Dec. 726



December 3, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Richard Eagleton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the judgment of the Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois), which, after consolidating several actions, affirmed the trial court's dismissal of the indictments against defendants, agreeing that though defendants were charged with theft, they could only be prosecuted for violation of the Illinois Public Aid Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 11-21 (1975), the statute of limitations for which had run.


OVERVIEW: The indictments charged defendants with obtaining monies from the Illinois Department of Public Aid and various of its county affiliates by falsely representing that they had little or no income. In dismissing the indictments, the trial court ruled that because defendants' actions were specifically barred by § 11-21 of the Illinois Public Aid Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 11-21 (1975), the State was restricted to prosecuting defendants under it, and because its statute of limitations had expired, the indictments could not be maintained. In affirming the trial court, the appellate court agreed with its reasoning. However, on appeal, the court reversed the judgments of both the appellate and trial courts. In doing so, it found that the actions allegedly taken by defendants could be prosecuted under either the Public Aid Code or the statutory provision governing theft. Moreover, the State had discretion in deciding which statute to prosecute defendants under and it did not violate equal protection to charge them with the offense carrying the more severe penalty.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the appellate and trial court and remanded the case to the trial court for further proceedings.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant employees sought review under a consolidated appeal from the judgments of the Appellate Court for the Fifth District, (Illinois), the Circuit Court of St. Clair County, (Illinois), and the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found in favor of appellee employers in the employees' action for damages under the Structural Work Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 48, para. 60 (1975).

Each appellant received workmen's compensation benefits either from their employer or the contractor of the work sites. Stat. ch. 48, para. 138.1(a)(3) and 138.5(a), but disallowed an employee whose employer did not have workmen's compensation insurance to recover under both sections, the classification was arbitrary; thus, the classification was unconstitutional.

People ex rel. Scott v. Briceland


No. 48729


Supreme Court of Illinois


65 Ill. 2d 485; 359 N.E.2d 149; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 460; 3 Ill. Dec. 739; 7 ELR 20283



December 3, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 28, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Paul C. Verticchio, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency and its director (EPA), sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, the Illinois Attorney General (attorney general), in a declaratory judgment action to enjoin the EPA from instituting and prosecuting enforcement actions before the Pollution Control Board (Board).


OVERVIEW: The EPA filed five separate enforcement complaints before the board. The attorney general sought a declaratory judgment that the attorney general was the only attorney empowered to institute and prosecute such actions on behalf of the State of Illinois (state) and sought to enjoin the EPA from instituting and prosecuting enforcement actions before the board. The circuit court held that § 4(e) of the Environmental Protection Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 111 1/2, par. 1004(e) (1975), delegated authority to prosecute enforcement cases before the board to the EPA but that the delegation of prosecutorial authority violated the Attorney General Provision of the Illinois Constitution, Ill. Const. art. V. § 15 (1970). The EPA claimed on appeal that proceedings before the board were administrative and not legal, and that it had independent authority to prosecute actions before the board based upon Ill. Const. art. XI, § 1, 1970. The court rejected the EPA's claim. The court held that § 4(e) was unconstitutional to the extent that it authorized the institution and prosecution of proceedings before the board by an officer other than the Illinois Attorney General.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment in favor of the attorney general. The court held that delegation of authority to the EPA to prosecute cases before the board was unconstitutional because the attorney general was the only official charged by the Illinois Constitution with representing the people of the State of Illinois in all legal proceedings.

Fuchs v. Bidwill


Nos. 47944, 47947 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


65 Ill. 2d 503; 359 N.E.2d 158; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 461; 3 Ill. Dec. 748



December 3, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 28, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Lee White, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: App. ct. rev'd; cir. ct. aff'd.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants officials challenged a judgment of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which reversed a judgment in their favor in appellee taxpayers complaint seeking an accounting, the declaration of a constructive trust, and other equitable relief, as a result of secret purchases and sales of stock in racetracks.


OVERVIEW: Taxpayers filed a complaint against officials, seeking an accounting, the declaration of a constructive trust, and other equitable relief, as a result of the officials' secret purchase and sale of stock in racetracks. The court reversed judgment in favor of the officials, and they challenged that judgment. The court reversed. The court held that there was no authority under which the taxpayers were had standing to bring the action where the funds or lands would become public property only upon the imposition of a constructive trust. Instead, the Attorney General was the only official empowered to represent the state in actions where it was the real party in interest.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment in favor of the taxpayers because they lacked standing to bring the action against the officials where the funds or lands would become public property only upon the imposition of a constructive trust.

Cronin v. Lindberg


No. 48867


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 47; 360 N.E.2d 360; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 470; 4 Ill. Dec. 424



December 3, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 28, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated actions, appellants, the state superintendent of education and the state comptroller, challenged the judgment of the Court of Cook County (Illinois) that held that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 1-1 et. seq. (1975) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 18-12 (1975), which mandated reduced funding to appellee school board and its superintendent for not providing a school term of 185 days, was in violation of Ill. Const. art. X, § 1.


OVERVIEW: When the school board did not have a full school term of 185 days due to a teacher's strike, the state superintendent of schools reduced its funding as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 1-1 et seq. (1975) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 18-12 (1975). When the state superintendent submitted vouchers for the reduced amount to be prorated over three years, the state comptroller refused to pay them on the grounds that he had to prorate the funds within one year. Both the state and local school superintendents filed for declaratory and injunctive relief against the state comptroller, and the school board and its superintendent filed against the state superintendent challenging the reduced funding on the grounds that it violated Ill. Const. art. X, § 1. The trial court limited its decision to declaring the laws unconstitutional. On review the court examined the legislative intent and the rules of statutory construction, and held that there was no constitutional proscription against conditioning state funding on a school district's compliance with minimum requirements. The statutes were found to be constitutional but the funds could be prorated over three years.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded with instructions. The judgment that it was unconstitutional for the state superintendent of schools to reduced funding to the school board for not having a full school term was reversed and the cause remanded with instructions to dismiss the school board's action. The trial court was directed to order appellant state comptroller to prorate the funds over three years.

People ex rel. Scott v. Chicago Park Dist.


No. 48061


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 65; 360 N.E.2d 773; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 471; 4 Ill. Dec. 660; 7 ELR 20346



December 3, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 16, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Francis T. Delaney, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant steel corporation appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which allowed the motion for summary judgment of the plaintiffs, the Illinois attorney general, governor, secretary of state, treasurer, and comptroller (attorney general), that state legislation was void on the grounds that it violated the public trust doctrine.


OVERVIEW: The Illinois general assembly passed legislation, subsequently signed by the governor, that provided for the conveyance by the state of 194.6 acres of land submerged in waters of Lake Michigan to the steel corporation. The attorney general filed an action seeking a declaratory judgment that the legislation was void. The corporation contended that previous cases considered by the court regarding the legislation at issue operated as a bar under the doctrine of res judicata to the attorney general's challenge to the validity of the legislative action, but the court ruled that when a cause of action was dismissed on the ground that the plaintiff lacked standing, as in the earlier cases, the court need not have considered the substantive issues involved, amounting to an adjudication on the merits. The court affirmed the summary judgment for the attorney general that the legislation was void on the ground that it violated the public trust doctrine because the primary purpose was private and the public benefit was only incidental and remote.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment for the attorney general, finding that the legislation that granted the use of submerged lands to the steel corporation violated the public trust doctrine because the claimed benefit to the public was only incidental and remote, and the direct and dominating purpose was a private one.

People ex rel. Phillips Petroleum Co. v. Gitchoff


No. 48242


Supreme Court of Illinois


65 Ill. 2d 249; 357 N.E.2d 534; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 434; 2 Ill. Dec. 367



November 24, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Original petition for mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied; supervisory order entered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Claims based on the same event were pending in two different counties. Petitioner petroleum company sought to consolidate in the second county. The motion was granted but the judge in the first county ordered the clerk not to send the record to the clerk in the first county. The petroleum company brought a petition for a writ of mandamus to compel the judge in the first county to comply with the consolidation order entered in second county.


OVERVIEW: The litigation concerned the explosion of a tank car leased by the petroleum company. Several actions were brought in relation to the explosion, and the petroleum company was added to one of them in the first county. The petroleum company then sought a declaration in the second county as to its general liability for the explosion. A counterclaim was then filed against the petroleum company in the first county. While motions to dismiss the claim and the counterclaim in county 1 were still pending, the petroleum company requested consolidation in the second county. That motion was granted. The judge in the fist county refused to send the record and the petition for mandamus followed. The court found that having separate suits involving identical parties and issues before different judges was incompatible with the orderly and efficient administration of justice. The court also found that regardless of the propriety of the order consolidating the proceedings in the second county, the refusal of the judge in first county to abide by that order was improper.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that the judge from the first county vacate the order that directed the clerk not to send the record, that he dismiss the counterclaim, and that no further action be taken in the first county to interfere with orders entered in the second county proceedings.

Hamer v. Kirk


No. 48482


Supreme Court of Illinois


65 Ill. 2d 211; 357 N.E.2d 506; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 426; 2 Ill. Dec. 339



November 15, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lake County; the Hon. Harry D. Strouse, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Lake County (Illinois), which found in favor of appellee Director of the Department of Local Government Affairs in the taxpayers' action that sought a declaration that § 146 of the Revenue Act of 1939, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 627 (1975), as amended by 1975 Ill. Laws 2192, was unconstitutional and that sought injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers sought to compel the local officials and the State of Illinois to assess and equalize property for taxing purposes. The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment. 1975 Ill. Laws 2192 provided that real and personal property were to be assessed at 33 1/3 percent rather than 50 percent of the actual value as determined by the Department's assessment to sales ratio studies for the three most recent years that preceded the assessment year. The taxpayers challenged the three-year period that was established by § 146 of the Act for implementing the Department's equalized assessed property values. Even though the taxpayers had to pay proportionately more than taxpayers in other counties to qualify for state assistance, § 146, as amended, was constitutional. The legislative scheme did postpone the arrival of intercountry uniformity for taxing purposes; however, the three-year transition period was not so patently unreasonable that it should have been struck down.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's judgment.

Allen v. County of Cook


No. 48695


Supreme Court of Illinois


65 Ill. 2d 281; 357 N.E.2d 458; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 437; 2 Ill. Dec. 291



November 15, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Walter P. Dahl, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayers sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their complaint for declaratory relief that sought to find a county ordinance invalid and for an injunction to prevent appropriations that were assessed by defendants, the county, the board of commissioners, and the individual board members (board), without obtaining a two-thirds vote.


OVERVIEW: The board adopted Ord. No. 75-0-33 to appropriate $ 2,000,000 from the motor fuel tax fund to the Regional Transportation Authority. The city members voted in favor of the ordinance, and the suburban members voted against it. At the same time, the board adopted Ord. No. 75-0-34, which allowed appropriations over $ 5,000 if authorized by a majority vote. On appeal, the court affirmed the dismissal of the taxpayers' complaint. The court held that adoption of the Ord. No. 75-0-34 was a proper exercise of power by a home rule unit of government because appropriation of funds related to its government and affairs as contemplated by Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(a). The court also held that the Open Meetings Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 102, para. 41 et seq., did not require for notice be given that the ordinance in question would be presented for adoption at that particular meeting. The court held that Ord. No. 75-0-34 did not render an improper change in the county's form of government and noted that nothing in the board's rules prevented the amendment of a prior ordinance, Ord. No. 73-0-8, or supersession of a related statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 34, para. 951.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the taxpayers' complaint for injunctive relief and for a declaratory judgment that a county ordinance regarding appropriations was invalid.

 

498 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Lunding v. Walker


No. 47607


Supreme Court of Illinois


65 Ill. 2d 516; 359 N.E.2d 96; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 462; 3 Ill. Dec. 686



November 15, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 28, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Nathan M. Cohen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant governor sought review of the order from the Cook County Circuit Court (Illinois), which entered a temporary injunction prohibiting the governor or his agents from interfering with plaintiff board member's performance of his duties as a member of the board.


OVERVIEW: The board member was notified by letter from the governor that he was being removed as a member of the State Board of Elections for negligent duty. The board member obtained a temporary injunction, and the governor appealed the interlocutory order under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 307, 58 Ill. 2d R. 307. On appeal, the court held that it was plain that the legislators intended, and the public interest demanded, that board members not be amenable to political influence or discipline in the discharge of their official duties. The court held that to subject a neutral, bipartisan, and independent board to the unbridled whim of the governor under the rule that his power of removal was incident and co-extensive with his power of appointment would have destroyed its purpose and efficacy. The court held that the governor could have only removed a member of the board for cause and that the question of whether the board member's conduct was sufficient neglect of duty to have justified the removal was a question reviewable by the court. The court affirmed the issuance of the temporary injunction as the court held that the board member was entitled to have been heard.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order from the trial court which issued a temporary injunction prohibiting the governor or his agents from interfering with the board member's performance of his duties as a member of the board, holding that the board member was entitled to a hearing on the matter.

Walker v. State Board of Elections


No. 47981


Supreme Court of Illinois


65 Ill. 2d 543; 359 N.E.2d 113; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 463; 3 Ill. Dec. 703



November 15, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 28, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. J. Waldo Ackerman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and reversed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, individuals and an organization (organization), filed suit against defendants, a board member and the State Board of Elections (board), seeking injunctive relief and a declaratory judgment that portions of the statute creating the board were unconstitutional. The Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois) granted the organization's motion for a judgment on the pleadings. The board and board member appealed.


OVERVIEW: A third party had filed a complaint with the board against the organization. The instant action was subsequently filed to enjoin the board from proceeding with that other complaint. The instant complaint also alleged that the statutory method of selecting board members by a legislative officer, provided in Ill. Rev. Stat. 1973, ch. 46, art. 1A, violated Ill. Const. of 1970, art. V, § 9(a). It was also alleged that the tie-breaker provisions of the art. 1A violated due process because it caused decisions to be made by lot or by chance. When a tie-vote occurred, the statute provided for the disqualification of one board member by lot. The court found that (1) members of the board were executive officers within the meaning of art. V, § 9(a); (2) the legislative appointment of board members violated art. V, § 9(a); (3) the tie-breaker provisions caused decisions to rest on an arbitrary basis and violated due process; and (4) the trial court erred by allowing the unconstitutionally selected board members to continue in office.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, in so far as it found that the statute was unconstitutional. The judgment was reversed, in so far as it allowed the members of the board to continue in office.

People v. Chambers


No. 48054


Supreme Court of Illinois


66 Ill. 2d 36; 360 N.E.2d 55; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 469; 4 Ill. Dec. 308



November 15, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 28, 1977.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County; the Hon. Alan W. Cargerman, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State of Illinois sought review of the order from the Second District Appellate Court (Illinois), which reversed defendants' convictions for violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 2371 (1973) on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The defendants were convicted for violating Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 2371 (1973), a curfew statute. The appellate court reversed the conviction on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that the statute was concerned with the conduct of children under the age of 18 and affected their conduct only between specified hours, and then only if they were not accompanied by an adult. The court held that it was the primary interest of the state was its traditional right to protect its children and the state was justified in acting upon the statute. The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order from the appellate court. The court held that the primary interest of the state was its traditional right to protect its children, and the state was justified in acting upon the curfew statute.

 

501 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


O'Leary v. Allphin


No. 48329


Supreme Court of Illinois


65 Ill. 2d 268; 357 N.E.2d 491; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 436; 2 Ill. Dec. 324



November 15, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Donald J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Director of the Illinois Department of Revenue and others, sought review of the affirmance of the trial court's injunctive order by the Circuit Court of Cook (Illinois). Plaintiff cigarette purchaser brought this action challenging the applicability of the Illinois Cigarette Tax Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120 para. 453.9c (1973), to individuals transporting cigarettes into Illinois for their own use and not for sale.


OVERVIEW: After his arrest for illegal transportation of 27 cartons of unstamped cigarettes into the state without a permit in violation of § 9c of Act, the cigarette purchaser brought this class action seeking a permanent injunction against defendants from enforcing § 9 and § 18 of the Act against individuals transporting cigarettes into the state for their own use, and not for the sale to others. The trial court imposed an injunction against defendants, and the appellate court affirmed the trial court's order. The court reversed the judgments of the trial and appellate courts and held that the term "transporter" in § 9c of the Act applied to all individuals carrying more than 2,000 cigarettes into the state, and not just to business engaged in the business of selling cigarettes. The court ruled that if the legislature intended to limit the "transporter" definition as suggested by the cigarette purchaser, it would have done so, as there were other exceptions enumerated in § 9c. Moreover, the court held that there was no inconsistency between the purpose of the Act and the purpose of the Cigarette Use Tax Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the appellate and trial courts. The court set aside the permanent injunction order of the trial court but held that it did so assuming that defendants would perform its duties consistent with the Illinois Cigarette Tax Act regarding the availability of application forms and the adoption of procedures for "transporters" under the Act.

 

502 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Schwartz


No. 47900


Supreme Court of Illinois


64 Ill. 2d 275; 356 N.E.2d 8; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 373; 1 Ill. Dec. 8



October 1, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George Dolezal, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that granted defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint charging him with violating the Adoption Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 4, para. 12--5 (1973) on the ground that § 12--1 of the Act was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an attorney, was charged with requesting and receiving compensation for placing out a child for adoption in violation of the Act. The trial court granted defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint on the ground § 12--1 of the Act was unconstitutional. The state appealed, and the court reversed and remanded. The trial court ruled that the statute was unconstitutionally vague because it did define "placing out" with sufficient specificity. When called upon to decide a vagueness question, the court assumed, absent contrary legislative intent, that the words of the statute had their ordinary and popularly understood meanings. The court conceded that the statute could have been more clearly drafted but it found no ambiguity which would cause men of ordinary understanding to guess as to the nature of the conduct it defined. It was obvious that the purpose of the statute was to prevent profiteering from the placement of children in "baby markets."


OUTCOME: The judgment granting defendant's motion to dismiss the complaint charging him with placing a child in violation of the Act was reversed and remanded.

 

503 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Rudman v. Rini


Nos. 48194, 48232


Supreme Court of Illinois


64 Ill. 2d 321; 356 N.E.2d 4; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 377; 1 Ill. Dec. 4



October 1, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 48194. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. John Verklan, Judge, presiding.

No. 48232. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Rock Island County; the Hon. Robert J. Horberg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 48194 -- Reversed and remanded. No. 48232 -- Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, appointee and county board, sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois) that declared the appointee's appointment invalid and commanded the county board to seat the political party's appointee. Appellant ousted appointee sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Rock Island County (Illinois) that declared his appointment invalid.


OVERVIEW: In each of these actions, a vacancy was created for a county position by the death of the holder of that position. Further, in both cases, the political parties affiliated with the deceased holders and the county boards each appointed persons to fill the vacancy. At the time the appointments were made, the Election Code had been amended to provide for appointment by committees of the political party. In the Will County case, the trial court declared that the county board's appointment was invalid and commanded the county board to appoint the political party's appointee. In the Rock Island County case, the trial court ruled in favor of that county board's appointee and declared the appointment of the ousted appointee invalid. All parties appealed, and the court reversed and remanded as to the Will County case and affirmed as to the Rock Island County case. The power to appoint public officers was the sovereign power of the state and could not be conferred upon a private person or group but had to be delegated, if at all, to some public agency. Therefore, the amendment vesting power to make appointments in the political parties was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded as to the judgment declaring the appointee's appointment invalid and affirmed as to the judgment declaring the ousted appointee's appointment invalid.

 

504 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Joliet v. Bosworth


Nos. 47976, 48078 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


64 Ill. 2d 516; 356 N.E.2d 543; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 397; 1 Ill. Dec. 355



October 1, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 12, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 47976. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Michael A. Orenic, Judge, presiding.

No. 48078. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. Charles Iben, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant county treasurers challenged the orders of the Circuit Courts of Will and Peoria Counties (Illinois), which entered declaratory judgments in favor of plaintiff taxing bodies, holding § 21 of "An Act concerning fees and salaries, and to classify the several counties of this state with reference thereto," Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 53, para. 39a (1974 Supp.), to be in violation of Ill. Const. of 1970, art. VII, § 9(a).


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to § 21 of "An Act concerning fees and salaries, and to classify the several counties of this state with reference thereto," Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 53, para. 39a (1974 Supp.), the county treasurers billed the taxing bodies a percentage of the taxes they collected to recover the taxing bodies' proportionate shares of the cost of the extension and collection of the taxes. The circuit courts awarded the taxing bodies a declaration that the statute violated Ill. Const. of 1970, art. VII, § 9(a). The county treasurers appealed directly to the court under Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 302(a), and the court affirmed. The court held that the constitutional provision reflected a determination by the framers of the Constitution that the collection of taxes by county officers was a county function that was to be supported by county taxes and not fees. The court found that the debates upon the purpose of the statute indicated the legislative intent to preclude counties from seeking, in any form, reimbursement from the various taxing bodies for county services rendered in the collection of taxes.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the circuit courts that declared unconstitutional the statute that permitted the counties to assess a fee for the collection of taxes.

 

505 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Cicero v. Fox Valley Trotting Club, Inc.


No. 47735


Supreme Court of Illinois


65 Ill. 2d 10; 357 N.E.2d 1118; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 405; 2 Ill. Dec. 675



October 1, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 2, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant racing associations challenged the orders of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that denied their motion to dismiss and that granted the motion of appellee town for summary judgment in an action brought by the town to collect an amusement tax.


OVERVIEW: The town adopted an ordnance that assessed a tax of 10 cents per person attending or witnessing thoroughbred or harness race meets conducted by the racing associations at a track within the town's boundaries. The state legislature subsequently adopted a statute that expressly permitted such an ordnance. The racing associations appealed from the trial court's grant of summary judgment to the town. The court affirmed. The court determined that Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(a) (1970) granted the town, as a home rule entity, extremely broad taxing authority. The court also determined that the state had not acted, pursuant to Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(g), (h) (1970) to limit this authority. As a result, the court found that the ordnance was a valid exercise of the town's taxing authority. Additionally, the court found that the tax was not an occupation tax, which the town had only a limited authority to impose under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(e) (1970).


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed and the cause was remanded for further proceedings.

507 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Spaulding v. Illinois Community College Board


No. 47476


Supreme Court of Illinois


64 Ill. 2d 449; 356 N.E.2d 339; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 390; 1 Ill. Dec. 213



September 20, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 12, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. L. Sheldon Brown, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Illinois Community College Board sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found in favor of plaintiff residents in their declaratory judgment action and determined that § 6-6.1 of the Public Community College Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 1-6-6.1 (1973), was unconstitutional and enjoined the Board from organizing a new school district.


OVERVIEW: The residents lived in areas that the Board proposed to include when forming a new community college district. The court reversed the circuit court's judgment that declared § 6-6.1 of the Act unconstitutional. Section 6-6.1 of the Act (former Act) provided that the Board was authorized to either establish new districts or to annex to an adjacent district each parcel of territory that was not a part of a district. In the case of annexation, the voters of a territory could have petitioned for a referendum; however, there was no provision for a referendum when new districts were established. Subsequent to the appeal, § 6-6.1 of the Act (new Act) was amended to provided for a referendum when new districts were created and the residents voted against the new district. However, the issue was not moot because the new § 6.6.1 of the Act was not an amendment, but was a reenactment of the former section. The former § 6-6.1 did not deprive the residents of the equal protection of the law. The State's interest in education was so pervasive that it was allowed to establish or alter school districts without any local referendum.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment, vacated the injunction, and remanded the action to the circuit court to determine if the referendum under the new § 6-6.1 was valid.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, Environmental Protection Agency (EPA), Pollution Control Board (board), and environmental organization, appealed from the judgment of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed the trial court's judgment dismissing an action filed by plaintiffs, corporation and its president, seeking an injunction to terminate board proceedings brought by the EPA and the environmental organization against the corporation.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the corporation's action for injunctive relief on the ground that the complaint failed to establish that the corporation exhausted its remedies under Section 41 of the Environmental Protection Act, Ill. The appellate court reversed, holding that the proceedings before the board were barred by a prior prosecution under a municipal ordinance. On appeal the issue was whether the corporation's allegation of double jeopardy, or alternatively, res judicata, invoked an additional exception to the requirement that administrative remedies be exhausted prior to seeking judicial relief. The court reversed, holding that the corporation sought review of an unappealable interlocutory order by the board and that the complaint failed to state facts which warranted an exception to the exhaustion doctrine.

509 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Greater Chicago Indoor Tennis Clubs, Inc. v. Willowbrook


No. 47878


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 400; 349 N.E.2d 3; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 327



May 28, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Second District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Phillip F. Locke, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff corporation, which operated an indoor tennis club, sought review of a decision of the Appellate Court for the Second District (Illinois), which reversed a judgment of the circuit court and held that an ordinance adopted by defendant non-home-rule municipality (village) imposing a tax on the fees and charges paid for the use of indoor tennis courts within the village was valid.


OVERVIEW: The village enacted an amusement tax on the gross receipts of indoor tennis facilities. The tennis club asserted that Illinois Municipal Code § 11-42-5, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-42-5 (1973), did not empower the village to regulate tennis and that it was, therefore, without authority to tax it. The tennis club further argued that the ordinance created an unreasonable classification in violation of the state and federal equal protection clauses. The circuit court held in favor of the tennis club but the appellate court reversed. On further appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the power to regulate and the power to raise revenue were separate and distinct and that neither was dependent on the other. Because the ordinance at issue was a revenue measure, the court held that it did not need to consider whether tennis was subject to the police power. The court then held that the term "amusement," under § 11-42-5, included participative as well as exhibitive amusements and, therefore, the village had the authority to tax indoor tennis under the statute. The court finally ruled that the club lacked standing to raised any constitutional issues regarding equal protection.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the appellate court in favor of the village in the corporation's action challenging the village's tax on the use of the corporation's tennis courts.

Rios v. Jones


No. 47343


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 488; 348 N.E.2d 825; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 338



May 28, 1976, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Nathan M. Cohen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the Illinois Department of Mental Health (department), challenged the order of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which found that § 13a of the Illinois Medical Practice Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 91, para. 14(a) (1973), was unconstitutional, affirmed the granting of injunctive relief to plaintiff doctors with 10 or more years of service, and reversed the denial of relief to the other doctors.


OVERVIEW: The doctors filed an action seeking to enjoin the department from enforcing the provisions of § 14(a) requiring examination of the doctors, who had been educated in foreign countries. The trial court found that § 14(a) was unconstitutional and enjoined the department from enforcing it with regard to the doctors who had 10 years or more years of service with the department. The doctors who were denied relief and the department appealed, and the appellate court held that § 14(a) was unconstitutional, affirmed the trial court's order granting the injunction to the doctors with 10 or more years service, and reversed the order denying relief to the other doctors. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The court held that the appellate court erroneously determined the constitutionality of § 14(a), because prior to the appellate court rendering its opinion, § 14(a) was amended. Thus, the constitutionality of § 14(a) should have been decided as it stood on the date of the appellate court's opinion. The court held that § 14(a), as amended, was not unconstitutionally vague and did not violate the Due Process Clause, the Privileges and Immunities Clause, or the Equal Protection Clause.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court holding that the Act was unconstitutional and remanded for further proceedings.

Schiller Park Colonial Inn, Inc. v. Berz


No. 47619


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 499; 349 N.E.2d 61; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 339



May 28, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 28, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. F. Emmett Morrissey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant members of the Liquor Control Commission (commission) appealed the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which enjoined the enforcement of § 12a of article VI of "An Act Relating to Alcoholic Liquors" (Liquor Control Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 132 (1973) and held that § 12a unconstitutionally abridged the rights of plaintiff liquor licensees to make political contributions.


OVERVIEW: The licensees made political campaign contributions, and the commission charged them with violating § 12a. None of the plaintiffs were employees or agents of the licensees. The lower court found that the restrictions contained in § 12a violated the First and Fourteenth amendments of the Constitution of the United States and Ill. Const. art. I, §§ 1, 2, 4 (1970). The court reversed, holding that no constitutional rights of the licensees had been violated. The First Amendment rights of the licensees were not violated because the state had a substantial interest in regulating liquor which overrode the marginal interest of the licensees in making campaign contributions. The court ruled that the licensees lacked standing to contend that the Liquor Control Act was overbroad by preventing contributions by employees or agents of licensees because no employees or agents were parties to the appeal. The court held that § 12a did not create an arbitrary classification in violation of the licensees' equal protection rights because there were substantial differences between the liquor licensees and other licensees which justified the different treatment of the different classes of licensees.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court, which enjoined the commission's enforcement of the law prohibiting campaign contributions by the licensees and which held that the licensees' constitutional rights were violated by restrictions on political campaign contributions made by licensees. The matter was remanded for proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

Supreme Court of Illinois

Wright v. Central Du Page Hosp. Ass'n


No. 48075


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 313; 347 N.E.2d 736; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 317; 80 A.L.R.3d 566



May 14, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. David A. Canel, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated action, appellants, Director of Insurance, a medical society, and a physician, sought review of a judgment by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held invalid Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para. 1013a (1975). Appellants, a hospital and a physician, sought review of the circuit court's judgment that held invalid Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, paras. 58.2-58.10 (1975) and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 70, para. 101 (1975).


OVERVIEW: Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 73, para. 1013a (1975) was a provision of the Illinois Insurance Code (Insurance provision). Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, paras. 58.2-58.10 (1975) were provisions of the Civil Practice Act (Civil Practice provisions), and Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 70, para. 101 (1975) was a provision of the Public Act (Public Act provision). The court held that under the Civil Practice provisions, the physician and lawyer members of the medical review panel were empowered to make conclusions of law and fact according to the applicable substantive law over the dissent of the circuit judge. Thus, the nonjudicial members of the medical review panel were empowered to exercise a judicial function in violation of the Illinois Constitution. Because these statutes providing for medical review panels were unconstitutional, the procedure prescribed therein as the prerequisite to jury trial was an impermissible restriction on the right of trial by jury. The court also held that the Public Act provision limiting recovery only in medical malpractice actions to $ 500,000 was arbitrary and constituted a special law, as did the Insurance provision, and were in violation of the 1970 Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and vacated in part the judgment of the circuit court.

 

514 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Saragusa v. Chicago


No. 46757


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 288; 348 N.E.2d 176; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 313



May 14, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Raymond K. Berg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a 79 year old woman, challenged the judgment from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which reversed a judgment that denied appellee city's motion to dismiss the complaint for injuries suffered when the woman fell into a hole in the sidewalk. The appellate court found insufficient service under the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, § 8-102 (1971).


OVERVIEW: The city argued that the woman failed to comply with notice requirements of the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, § 8-102 (1971), in effect at the time of her accident. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that the original notice did bear a signature as required by the act. The notice also gave the name and address of the attending physician, from whom the city could have ascertained the name of the treating hospital. Further information was disclosed in answers to interrogatories. The court held that the claimed deficiency in the notice did not warrant dismissal of the woman's complaint. The court concluded that § 8-102 prescribed no minimum period by which the service of notice was required to antedate commencement of the action. The filing of a complaint within the six-month period afforded as much time to investigate the claim as if the notice had been filed within that period and cured the defect in the notice.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court that the woman's service against the city was insufficient. The court held that the complaint was filed within the six-month period and that the claimed deficiency in notice did not warrant dismissal of the complaint.
