People v. Boyer


No. 47305


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 433; 349 N.E.2d 50; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 331



May 14, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 28, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Logan County; the Hon. John T. McCullough, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State sought review of a decision of the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which held that the penalty provision of the aggravated incest statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-10 (1973), was unconstitutional. The appellate court affirmed defendant's conviction for aggravated incest but remanded the case with instructions that defendant be resentenced for a Class 3 felony.


OVERVIEW: The issue before the court was the constitutionality of the aggravated incest statute. Defendant could have been sentenced from one to 20 years in the penitentiary. He argued that males charged with the offense of aggravated incest were discriminated against on the basis of their sex because females guilty of the same conduct faced possible punishment of from one to 10 years in the penitentiary. The court held that the State demonstrated an interest which justified the classification at issue. The court found that a female victim of a father-daughter incestuous relationship was exposed to potential harm to which male victims of incestuous relationships were not exposed. The possibility that the female victim could become pregnant added considerably to the potential harm that could result. The physical change in a female who became pregnant could be a source of trauma to the female. The court found that the physical and psychological dangers of incest were greater when the offense was committed by a male and the victim was his daughter. The court held that the State's interest in protecting potential victims of incestuous relationships justified the statutory classification.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the appellate court and affirmed the decision of the circuit court.

 

516 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ward


No. 47479


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 437; 349 N.E.2d 47; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 332



May 14, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 28, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Peoria County; the Hon. John A. Whitney, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Peoria County (Illinois), which convicted him of the offense of obscenity in violation of § 11-20(a)(1) o the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11-20(a)(1) (1971).


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an operator of a bookstore, was convicted of obscenity for selling two obscene publications. On appeal, defendant alleged that para. 11-20 was unconstitutional and that the magazines in question were constitutionally protected. The court affirmed defendant's conviction. The court held that para. 11-20 was sufficiently clear to withstand constitutional objections because it adequately defined the type of sexual conduct that could be depicted. Also, although contemporary community standards were relevant in determining whether the publications were obscene, they bore no relevance to the questions of how or to whom obscene materials could be distributed. It was within the police power of Illinois to make the commercial distribution of obscene materials a crime. Therefore, the sale of obscene materials was a crime in Illinois even though the publications were not forced upon unwilling audiences or made available to minors. Further, the publications were not protected by the First Amendment or Ill. Const. art. I, § 4. The publications depicted, in a patently offensive way, sexual conduct defined by para. 11-20.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

517 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Baird v. Chicago, B. & Q. R. Co.


No. 48037


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 463; 349 N.E.2d 413; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 335



May 14, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 28, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. J. Waldo Ackerman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant railroad appealed from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois) order affirming the lower court judgment for damages, on retrial, upon jury verdicts in favor of plaintiffs, decedents' estate administrators, in their wrongful death suit arising from a motorcycle-train collision, which killed two teenagers.


OVERVIEW: The two decedent teenagers were killed in a collision between a motorcycle operated by one decedent, with the other as his passenger, and defendant's train. The first jury verdict in favor of their estates was reversed and remanded for retrial on damages only. A second jury also returned verdicts for decedents' estates and this judgment was affirmed. Granted leave to appeal, the railroad argued the testimony of the estates' economist was erroneously admitted. It argued Illinois required discounting future loss to present value, and that income projections should have been based on the life expectancy of the next of kin rather than that of decedents, and should have been discounted for expenses. It also challenged certain jury instructions. It claimed these errors resulted in excessive verdicts. The court disagreed and affirmed the judgments. The instructions were not unconstitutionally vague and the verdicts were not so excessive as to show passion or prejudice.


OUTCOME: Judgment on jury verdict on retrial for damages awarded to decedents' estates was affirmed, as the amount was not so excessive as to require reversal.

 

518 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


USA I Lehndorff Vermoegensverwaltung GmbH & Cie v. Cousins Club, Inc.


No. 47770


Supreme Court of Illinois


64 Ill. 2d 11; 348 N.E.2d 831; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 345



May 14, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 28, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lessor appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which reversed the trial court's decision and held that the Illinois distress for rent provisions, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 80, paras. 16-34 (1973) were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The lessor instituted the procedures under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 80, paras. 16-34 (1973) for distraining defendant tenant's personal property for being in arrears in rent. The court reversed the appellate court's determination that the statutory provisions were unconstitutional, holding that the state was not significantly involved; thus, there could have been no due process violation under U.S. Const. amend. XIV or Ill. Const. art. I, § 2 (1970). The state was not "significantly involved," where, as here, the lessor took possession of his tenant's property pursuant to a statute that simply codified the lessor's common law right to do this and that did not have the state carry out the lessor's rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's determination that the distress for rent provisions were unconstitutional and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

519 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Telco Leasing, Inc. v. Allphin


No. 47736


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 305; 347 N.E.2d 729; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 316



May 14, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Samuel B. Epstein, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lessor appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) granting summary judgment in favor of defendants, Director of Revenue for the State of Illinois (director), State Treasurer, and State Attorney General, in the lessor's action for declaratory and injunctive relief alleging that taxes were improperly assessed against it under the Illinois Use Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 439.3 (1973).


OVERVIEW: The lessor leased equipment to nonprofit institutions. Defendants assessed taxes against the lessor for the use of the leased equipment pursuant to the Illinois Use Tax Act (Act), which the lessor paid under protest. The lessor then filed an action for declaratory relief, alleging that the Act was unconstitutional as applied. The lessor also sought an injunction prohibiting defendants from assessing a use tax on the property leased to nonprofit institutions. The parties filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court granted defendants' motion for summary judgment. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court ruled that a lessee was not a "user" as defined by the Act because a lessee did not exercise ownership rights over leased property. As the owner and user of the property, the lessor was subject to the tax. The court also ruled that the Act did not deny equal protection or violate Ill. Const. art. IX, § 2 (1970) by creating an improper tax classification because property sold to a nonprofit institution was put exclusively to charitable use. In contrast, leased property was still used by its owner to make a profit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court granting summary judgment in favor of defendants in the lessor's action for declaratory and injunctive relief. The court also dissolved temporary injunctions that restrained the revenue director from transferring the taxes paid by the lessor under protest to the State Treasurer for deposit in the general revenue fund.

 

520 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


King v. Lindberg


No. 48123


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 159; 345 N.E.2d 474; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 300



March 29, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. J. Waldo Ackerman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Superintendent of the Illinois State Fair Agency, challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court, in Sangamon County (Illinois), which upheld the constitutionality of the State Fair Board Act, 1975 Ill. Laws 79-1129, in the Superintendent's action against appellee Comptroller for a declaratory judgment that the act was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The Superintendent's contention was that the State Fair Board Act, 1975 Ill. Laws 79-1129, establishing a 15-member State Fair Board to replace the former State Fair Agency, violated the provisions of Ill. Const. art. V, § 9(a), which stated in part that the general assembly should have no power to elect or appoint officers of the executive branch. The Comptroller contended that the Act was constitutional because the interim board members did not hold an "office" because of the temporary nature of their positions. The court agreed that the Act was unconstitutional. The only temporary aspect to the positions under consideration was the tenure of the interim board members. The position itself was intended to be permanent and the duties of the Board were intended to be continuing duties. The fact that some incidental duties of the Board would cease in 1978 did not affect the continuing nature of the Board's primary duties. And the fact that all of the interim office holders would be replaced by permanent members of the Board by 1978 did not alter the permanent nature of the office itself. These were officers of the Executive Branch within the proscriptions of § 9(a).


OUTCOME: The court reversed decision of the circuit court, which had upheld the constitutionality of the Act in the Superintendent's action for a declaratory judgment that the act was unconstitutional.

 

521 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Kobylanski v. Chicago Bd. of Education


Nos. 47084, 47454


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 165; 347 N.E.2d 705; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 301



March 29, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 27, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: No. 47084. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. George Schaller, Judge, presiding.

No. 47454. -- Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas H. Fitzgerald, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 47084 -- Judgment affirmed. No. 47454 -- Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff parent appealed a decision of the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), affirming a judgment for defendants, a school board and a teacher. In a consolidated appeal, defendant school district sought review of a decision affirming a judgment for plaintiff student. Both cases involved claims that the schools and the teachers were liable for injuries to students resulting from their allegedly negligent conduct.


OVERVIEW: In the first case, the trial court found that the parent had failed to prove wilful and wanton misconduct and directed a verdict for the school board and the teacher. In the second case, the trial court refused to instruct on wilful and wanton misconduct, and the jury returned a verdict in favor of the student on her claim that the school district failed to provide proper supervision. The court of appeals affirmed the trial court's judgment in each case. The court affirmed the decision affirming the directed verdict for the school board and the teacher and reversed the decision affirming the judgment for the student. The court held that, under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, paras. 24-24 and 34-84a (1967), educators were immune from suits for negligence arising out of nondisciplinary matters and that, to impose liability, wilful and wanton misconduct had to be proved. The court found that the statute was constitutional and that the immunity was not waived by the Local Governmental and Governmental Employees Tort Immunity Act, specifically Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 85, para. 9-103(b) (1967).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the court of appeals' decision affirming the judgment for the school board and the teacher against the parent. The court reversed the decision affirming the judgment in favor of the student and against the school district.

 

522 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Barker


No. 47364


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 113; 345 N.E.2d 484; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 293



March 29, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of McLean County; the Hon. Wendell E. Oliver, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appellate court reversed; circuit court affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant State of Illinois sought review of a judgment from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which reversed a circuit court's decision that affirmed an inheritance tax assessment order and declared § 11 of the Illinois Inheritance Tax Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 385 (1973), unconstitutional in the State's actions against appellee estate representative.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court entered an order that assessed treasury bonds that were part of the estate at their fair market value rather than the par value that was suggested by the attorney general. The State appealed to the same circuit court that issued the assessment pursuant to § 11 of the Act, and the circuit court affirmed the order. The appellate court reversed the circuit court's decision on the basis that § 11 of the Act was unconstitutional. Section 11 of the Act provided that a circuit court that was designated by the chief judge was empowered to assess the cash value of all estates that were subject to the inheritance tax. An appeal of the assessment was to be filed in the circuit court of the proper county. Section 11 did not violate the separation of powers doctrine because Ill. Const. of 1970, Trans. Schedule § 4(d) allowed the circuit courts to exercise non-judicial functions. An assessment order was not considered a final judgment, but an administrative order. The term "appeal" that was used in § 11 of the Act was construed to mean the judicial review of an administrative action.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appellate court's judgment and affirmed the circuit court's decision.

 

523 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mayberry


Nos. 47495, 47640 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 1; 345 N.E.2d 97; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 279



March 18, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 47495. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. Robert L. Gagen, Judge, presiding.

No. 47640. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, the state appealed from the judgments of the Circuit Court of St. Clair County (Illinois) and the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which dismissed the indictments against the St. Clair defendant brought under § 401 of the Illinois Controlled Substance Act and the indictment against the Sangamon defendant brought under § 5 of the Cannabis Control Act.


OVERVIEW: The Sangamon defendant was indicted under the Cannabis Control Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 701 et seq. (1973), charging him with delivery of between 30 and 500 grams of a substance containing cannabis. The St. Clair defendant was indicted under the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1100 et seq. (1973), charging him with delivery of 200 or more grams of a controlled substance. The trial courts dismissed the indictments against defendants, holding that the graduated penalty provisions of the respective acts potentially punished defendants for the weight of innocuous substances and therefore were unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed the judgments of the trial courts and remanded with instructions to reinstate the indictments. The classifications under the respective acts had a reasonable basis and, therefore, they did not violate the Due Process or Equal Protection Clauses of the United States or Illinois Constitutions. The Illinois legislature could have believed that a drug was more dangerous if it was mixed with an innocuous substance because it could be delivered to more people.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments of the trial courts, which dismissed the indictments against defendants. The court remanded the respective causes to the respective trial courts with directions to reinstate the indictments.

 

524 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Cessna v. Montgomery


Nos. 47738, 48002


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 71; 344 N.E.2d 447; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 289



March 18, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] No. 47738. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Lawrence County; the Hon. Philip Benefiel, Judge, presiding.

No. 48002. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Irwin Cohen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: No. 47738 -- Reversed and remanded. No. 48002 -- Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mothers' complaints were dismissed for being statute-barred. One mother appealed from the judgment of the circuit court, and the Appellate Court for the Fifth District reversed and remanded. Defendant father obtained leave to appeal. The second mother challenged the dismissal of her action by the Circuit Court of Cook County and the court allowed defendant father's motion to transfer.


OVERVIEW: The mothers contended that Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 106 3/4, para. 54 (1973), denied an illegitimate child equal protection as his right of support from his natural father was conditioned on establishing paternity within two years, absent formal acknowledgment, while a legitimate child's support right was not so conditioned. They urged that para. 54 denied both equal protection and due process to the illegitimate child because his support right could be terminated for conditions over which he had no control. They argued that para. 54 did not authorize a child to bring an action himself, by next friend or guardian; nor did it specifically authorize a state's attorney to file an action on his own initiative. The court held that Illinois had a legitimate interest in preventing the litigation of stale or fraudulent claims and a paternity action had to be brought within two years of the most recent statement or significant contribution. The fathers urged dismissal of the actions because they were not brought in the name of the state or controlled by public prosecutors. The court held that private prosecution of a paternity suit did not violate due process.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the first action and vacated and remanded the second action. The court remanded both cases to the trial courts for further proceedings.

 

525 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Bradley v. Lunding


No. 48178


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 91; 344 N.E.2d 472; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 290



March 18, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Announced January 19, 1976.

Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. J. Waldo Ackerman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant members sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County (Illinois), which found in favor of plaintiff candidates in their action seeking to hold unconstitutional a regulation adopted by the members dealing with the order in which the names of candidates were arranged upon primary ballots.


OVERVIEW: The members of the State Board of Elections were directed to certify the candidates for nomination for elective offices in the order in which nominating petitions were filed pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 7-14. In connection with this legal duty, the members adopted a regulation prescribing a lottery system to determine the order in which simultaneously filed petitions were deemed to have been filed. The lottery system allowed that candidates filing a group petition for the same office were treated as one for purposes of the order. The candidates had each filed individual nominating petitions simultaneously on the first day of filing, and later successfully challenged the constitutionality of the lottery system in the circuit court. The court ruled that regulation had not purposefully discriminated against individual candidates because its application with respect to any particular office always depended upon the number of vacancies to be filled, and the number of candidates filing individual or group petitions. Furthermore, there was no evidence that where a candidate was placed on the ballot effected the number of votes he or she received.


OUTCOME: The court reversed in favor of the members in the candidates' action seeking to hold unconstitutional a regulation adopted by the members dealing with the order in which the names of candidates were arranged upon primary ballots.

 

526 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Farr


Nos. 47459, 47460, 47585 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


63 Ill. 2d 209; 347 N.E.2d 146; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 303



March 18, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 27, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Nos. 47459, 47460. -- Appeals from the Circuit Court of Hancock County; the Hon. Keith Scott, Judge, presiding.

No. 47585. -- Appeal from the Circuit Court of Winnebago County; the Hon. John T. Beynon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The people appealed from two judgments of the Circuit Court of Hancock County (Illinois) and the judgment of the Circuit Court of Winnebago County (Illinois), which held unconstitutional § 11-501.1(d), codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501.1(d), of the Illinois Vehicle Code. In separate and unrelated occurrences, defendants were arrested and charged with driving while under the influence of intoxicating liquor.


OVERVIEW: In each instance defendants filed a motion to dismiss the proceeding on the ground that § 11-501.1(d) was unconstitutional for the reason that it violated Ill. Const. art. II, § 1. The circuit courts entered judgments of dismissal. Defendants argued that the Illinois Secretary of State, as an executive officer, was vested with the power to suspend drivers' licenses, and the statute in question attempted to take that power from the Secretary and delegate it to the judiciary. The people contended that the statute did not violate Ill. Const. art. II, § 1. On appeal, the court reversed, holding that: (1) the doctrine of separation of powers did not inexorably preclude one of the three departments of government from exercising powers which could also be given to another department; (2) the statute was explicit that if the circuit court found that a person refused to submit to the required test requested by an officer, the Secretary should thereupon suspend the license; and (3) the court did not agree with defendants that the statute delegated to the judiciary either the power to suspend licenses or the discretion to determine whether such licenses should be suspended.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decisions of the circuit courts and remanded the causes for further proceedings consistent with the court's opinion.

People v. Grammer


No. 47350


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 393; 342 N.E.2d 371; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 263



February 5, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Third District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of La Salle County; the Hon. John S. Massieon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Appellate Court for the Third District (Illinois) affirmed the trial court's order that dismissed defendant's post-conviction petition filed pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 122--1 et. seq. (1971). Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of aggravated incest and sentenced to 2 to 10 years in prison. On defendant's appeal of his post-conviction petition dismissal, he abandoned the issues initially raised and challenged the constitutionality of the aggravated incest statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 11--1038 (1969), on the basis that the statute denied him equal protection of the law under the Illinois Constitution of 1970 and the Fourteenth Amendment because the statute applied to males only. The appellate court held that defendant waived the issue of the statute's constitutionality by failing to raise it at his trial or in his post-conviction petition. The court affirmed the lower courts and held that the aggravated incest statute was not unconstitutional as applied to defendant. Defendant's conviction was final prior to the effective date of the 1970 Illinois Constitution. The classification distinction between the aggravated incest statute and the incest statute was justified because of the potentially more serious consequences of pregnancy as a result of incest for a daughter as opposed to a son. The statutory classification was not arbitrary or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's orders that dismissed defendant's post-conviction petition.

People ex rel. Department of Registration & Education v. D. R. G., Inc.


No. 47687


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 401; 342 N.E.2d 380; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 264



February 5, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Walter P. Dahl, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Illinois Department of Registration and Education appealed a decision from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered a judgment on the pleadings in favor of defendants, a corporation and the directors, in the Department's suit seeking to enjoin the corporation, and other corporate entities, from engaging in certain practices without securing a certificate of registration as a real estate broker issued by the Department.


OVERVIEW: The trial court held provisions of the Real Estate Brokers and Salesmen License Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 114 1/2, para 101 et seq. (1973), upon which the Department relied were unconstitutional. The complaint alleged the corporation was engaged in the business of buying and selling real estate without a valid certification as a broker by the Department. The corporation answered, stating it was engaged in the business of obtaining certificates of purchase from tax sales issued pursuant to the requirements of the Revenue Act. The corporation stated it sold the certificates to third parties, surrendered the certificate if redemption was made, or took some other course of action. The Department argued the corporation's activities brought it within the purview of the Act. The court held a certificate of purchase for delinquent real estate was not an interest in real estate. The court held the corporation's acquisition of certificates of purchase was not within the definition of real estate contained in the Act. The court held the corporation was not engaged in buying and selling real estate within the meaning of the 1973 statute at the time the Department sought injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court in favor of the corporation and the directors.

After the litigants were acquitted by a jury they requested the clerk return the full amount each had deposited. The clerk retained 10 percent of the bond deposit as authorized by § 110-7(f). The complaint claimed that the provision authorizing the retention of 10 percent of the bond deposit to cover administrative costs was unconstitutional. The trial court stayed proceeding pending the determination of the court of another case challenging the constitutionality of the same administrative cost provision. The provision was found to be constitutional. The trial court dismissed the complaint. The court affirmed, holding that under § 110, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 110 (1969), access to Illinois courts was not denied solely because of the inability of an accused to pay; and (2) § 110-7 did not work to deny relief to the poor man merely because of his poverty.

530 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Touhy v. State Board of Elections


No. 48065


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 303; 342 N.E.2d 364; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 254



January 26, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Announced December 8, 1975.

Original proceeding for mandamus.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, chairman of the Illinois Democratic Central Committee, brought a petition against the State Board of Elections (board) for a writ of mandamus. The chairman sought to judicially determine the application of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 46, para. 7 -- 14.1 (1973) in relation to the method used in apportioning the delegates to the national political party convention among the congressional districts within the state.


OVERVIEW: The chairman brought a petition for a writ of mandamus against the board, relating to the method to be used in apportioning the delegates to the Democratic National Convention among the congressional districts within the state. The chairman insisted upon a plan which would have resulted in an increase of 19 delegates to be selected from the congressional districts within the city of Chicago and a corresponding decrease in the number of delegates to be selected from congressional districts elsewhere in the state. The court considered the issue of whether the rules of a national political party must have been accorded primacy over nonconforming state law. The court found that the record contained factual questions for which resolution was necessary to determine the chairman's entitlement to relief, and not questions of law. The court held that the chairman failed to show the requisite entitlement for a writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The court ruled in favor of the board and denied the chairman's petition for a writ of mandamus to determine the appropriate method for apportioning the delegates to the national political party convention.

 

531 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pembrock


No. 47242


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 317; 342 N.E.2d 28; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 255



January 26, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Dwight McKay, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.William J. Scott, Attorney General, of Springfield, and Bernard Carey, State's Attorney, of Chicago (James B. Zagel and Jayne Carr, Assistant Attorneys General, and Laurence J. Bolon and James S. Veldman, Assistant State's Attorneys, of counsel), for the People.

Robert H. Smith, Mark Spiegel, and Lucy A. Williams, of Mandel Legal Aid Clinic, and Thomas Allen (law student), all of Chicago, for appellee.

Howard Eglit, of Chicago, for amicus curiae American Civil Liberties Union.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed from the judgment of an appellate court (Illinois), which reversed the trial court's judgment finding defendant to be a sexually dangerous person and committing him to custody until he was recovered and released as provided by the Sexually Dangerous Persons Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. par. 105-1.01 et seq. (1971).


OVERVIEW: After defendant was charged with committing the offense of indecent liberties with a child, the state petitioned for a hearing to determine if defendant was a sexually dangerous person. The trial court found defendant to be a sexually dangerous person and committed him until he recovered. The appellate court reversed and remanded, holding that the proper standard of proof that should have been applied under the Act was proof beyond a reasonable doubt and not a preponderance of the evidence. On appeal the court affirmed, holding that: (1) the standard of proof required for commitment under the Act was proof beyond a reasonable doubt because the requirements of due process mandated that the drastic impairment of the liberty and reputation of an individual which resulted from civil commitment needed to be justified by proof beyond a reasonable doubt; (2) the Act did not violate the constitutional requirement of equal protection of the law because defendant failed to show how a classification based on these factors is unreasonable; and (3) the Act was not unconstitutionally void for vagueness because sufficient objective criteria existed in the Act to meet constitutional requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the appellate court's decision, which reversed defendant's commitment and remanded the case for a new hearing under the proper standard of proof.

 

532 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Nicks


No. 47278


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 350; 342 N.E.2d 360; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 260



January 26, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. Rodney A. Scott, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision from the Appellate Court for the Fourth District (Illinois), which affirmed the trial court's conviction of defendant on one count of armed robbery. The appellate court reversed the conviction for the remaining two counts of armed robbery because the offenses arose from the same course of conduct. The appellate court refused to reduce the consecutive sentence that had been entered by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: After defendant's conviction, the trial court imposed a sentence of 10 to 30 years in the penitentiary, which was to be served consecutively to any and all sentences heretofore imposed. Defendant had been previously convicted of an unrelated armed robbery and had been sentenced to 12 to 20 years. The sole issue on appeal was the propriety of the consecutive sentence under § 5-8-4, codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4 (1972 Supp.), of the Unified Code of Corrections, effective January 1, 1973. Defendant argued that the aggregate minimum of his consecutive sentence, which totaled 22 years, exceeded twice the statutory minimum for armed robbery, which totaled eight years. The State argued that under the language of § 5-8-4(h), codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4(h), the limitation on the aggregate minimum of consecutive sentences set forth in § 5-8-4(c) was not applicable to defendant. The court held that: (1) the portion of § 5-8-4(h) upon which the State relied was violative of the equal protection clauses of the Federal and State constitutions; and (2) the portion relied upon by the State could be severed without affecting the remaining portions.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the appellate court insofar as it affirmed the consecutive sentence. The court remanded the cause to the trial court with directions to issue an amended mittimus indicating that the sentence for armed robbery in this cause was to run concurrently with the sentence previously imposed.

 

533 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Leader v. Cullerton


Nos. 47308, 47323 cons.


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 483; 343 N.E.2d 897; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 270



January 26, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Supplemental Opinion Filed on Denial of Rehearing March 25, 1976, Reported at 62 Ill. 2d 483 at 493.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the First District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Daniel A. Covelli, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Aff'd in pt. & rev. in pt. & rem.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayers sought review of a decision from the Appellate Court for the First District (Illinois), which affirmed an award of attorneys fees in an action objecting to the award for such fees filed against appellees attorneys.


OVERVIEW: Three law offices successfully represented a class in an action to have a taxing statute declared unconstitutional. Members of the class were informed that taxes paid would go into a special from which the attorneys would be paid. Seventy members of the class paid into the fund. The attorneys filed a verified join petition for fees and nine of the taxpayers who paid into the fund objected. A hearing was held and the court allowed fees of 15 percent of the fund. The appellate court affirmed and the taxpayers sought review, contending the fees were excessive. The court agreed and determined that the fees should more properly have been based on the number of hours the attorneys worked rather than a percentage of the fund. The court then proceeded to recalculate the fees. The court affirmed the part of the judgment which allowed the attorneys to be paid from the fund but reversed and remanded the award of fees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the finding that the attorneys fees could be paid from the fund but reversed and remanded the amount and means of calculating those fees.

 

534 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Board of Education v. State Board of Education


No. 47577


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 517; 344 N.E.2d 5; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 274



January 26, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 25, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff school district appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, in Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant State Board of Education's motion to dismiss the mandamus action filed by the school district against the State Superintendent of Public Instruction that sought to compel him to pay to the school district reimbursement for costs of transporting pupils to its schools. The Board was substituted as defendant.


OVERVIEW: The school district characterized the act of withholding transportation reimbursement as a "penalty" unlawfully imposed upon it by the Board for failure to furnish transportation to nonpublic school pupils or for challenging the validity of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 29-4 (1973), requiring it to so provide nonpublic school pupils transportation. By the petition for mandamus, the school district sought to compel reimbursement for those prior years during which it was admittedly not complying with Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 29-4. The court affirmed the judgment because it was unable to perceive any basis in either logic or equity why the school district should be entitled to such reimbursement. In a prior suit, in sustaining the Board's power to withhold all State funds for such noncompliance, the court necessarily sustained the refusal to make specific reimbursements for which the school district had failed to qualify. The withholding was not an unlawful penalty, but was simply the result of the school district's refusal to meet a requirement of eligibility established by the School Code.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment by the circuit court that dismissed the school district's mandamus action seeking reimbursement from the Board for costs of transporting pupils to its schools.

 

535 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Gravelle v. Gates


No. 47320


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 217; 342 N.E.2d 57; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 240



January 20, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Philip Locke, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the county superintendent of education and objectors to a petition for the organization of a community unit school district, appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court, in Du Page County (Illinois), which reversed a decision by the superintendent denying appellee proponents' petition for the school district upon their complaint for administrative review of the order by the county superintendent.


OVERVIEW: The circuit court reversed the decision of the superintendent on the ground that it was against the manifest weight of the evidence, held unconstitutional the provision of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 122, para. 11-6 (1971), which required the approval of the Superintendent of Public Instruction before an election could be held, and directed the county superintendent to call an election on the proposition of the organization of the proposed school district. On appeal, the county superintendent and the objectors contended that the decision of the county superintendent found ample support in the record and that, in holding that it was against the manifest weight of the evidence, the circuit court erred. The court held that the county superintendent's decision was not contrary to the manifest weight of the evidence, and the judgment of the circuit court was reversed. The effect of the circuit court's decision was to hold that as only minimal detriments would affect the adjacent districts, the electorate of the proposed district, alone, should determine whether the new district should be organized. Clearly, that was not the correct standard for review of the county superintendent's decision.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's judgment that in turn reversed the decision by the county superintendent denying the proponents' petition for the organization of a community unit school district upon the proponents' complaint for administrative review of the order by the county superintendent.

Patchett v. Baylor


No. 46688


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 426; 343 N.E.2d 484; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 265



January 20, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 25, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County; the Hon. Victor N. Cardosi, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, the state director of insurance, appealed an order from the Circuit Court of Kankakee County (Illinois), which entered a judgment setting aside defendant's order and directed that the licenses of plaintiff, an insurance broker and agent, be reinstated in an action involving plaintiff's violation of Ill. Ins. Code § 502.


OVERVIEW: An insurance company granted plaintiff authority to settle claims by policyholders and furnished plaintiff with books of blank drafts drawable upon the company. Defendant director of insurance initiated proceedings against plaintiff in a letter advising plaintiff that the insurance company had submitted documented evidence of highly irregular activities by plaintiff through his claim draft authority. After a hearing, defendant revoked plaintiff 's broker and agent licenses as well as a firm license for a firm in which plaintiff was the only designated member. The court held that the circuit court's order declaring Ill. Ins. Code § 502 unconstitutional was erroneous. The court found that the actual revocation of plaintiff's license did not take place until after defendant's order, which was based upon findings made by a hearing officer as a result of a hearing. The court did not find any evidence to indicate that the hearing officer was biased or that he had any personal or pecuniary interest in the subject matter of the hearing, or that he had played a role in defendant's investigative activities, which led to the hearing.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment setting aside the order of defendant director of insurance and reinstating the licenses of plaintiff insurance broker and agent, because the circuit court erroneously concluded that the insurance code was unconstitutional.

 

537 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Meyer v. Marshall


No. 47076


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 435; 343 N.E.2d 479; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 266



January 20, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 25, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Appellate Court for the Fifth District; heard in that court on appeal from the Circuit Court of Monroe County; the Hon. Alvin H. Maeys, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant homeowners sought review of an order of the Appellate Court for the Fifth District (Illinois), which reversed an order of the trial court granting costs and attorney fees to appellants on the ground that appellants' zoning claim for an injunction against respondent house builders was moot.


OVERVIEW: Appellant homeowners brought an action against respondent house builders to enjoin respondents from building a house in violation of the zoning laws. The trial court granted a temporary injunction, and awarded appellants' attorney fees in connection with the injunction. While the appeal of the injunction was pending respondents rendered the action moot by selling the property. The appellate court declared the case moot, but reversed the grant of attorney fees, and ordered that appellants pay attorney fees to respondents. On further appeal, the court reversed and remanded, holding that because the action was moot the judgment of the trial court should stand, and the appellate court should not have considered the issue of costs and attorney fees. The court also held that attorney fees could be awarded only pursuant to statute. The court found that the award of attorney fees to respondent was not justified under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 11-13-15 (1973), which applied only to plaintiffs, or Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 69, para. 12 (1973) which applied only if the preliminary injunction was dissolved before the case was disposed of on the merits.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the order of the appellate court that reversed an order of the trial court granting costs and attorney fees to appellant homeowners and granted attorney fees to respondent house builders. The court held that because the action was moot, the appellate court should not have considered the question of attorney fees, and should have let the trial court order stand.

 

538 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


United Private Detective & Sec. Ass'n v. Chicago


No. 47531


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 506; 343 N.E.2d 453; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 273



January 20, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 25, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Donald J. O'Brien, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, detectives and agencies, challenged an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant city's motion to dismiss their complaint seeking an injunction to prevent the city from enforcing Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code ch. 117 (1974) and a declaration that it was void.


OVERVIEW: The general assembly passed the Private Detective Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 201-27 (1974), which gave the state the power to regulate the private detective business. The city established a procedure for licensing security firms in Chicago, Ill., Mun. Code ch. 117 (1974). The detectives and agencies alleged that ch. 117 was void because it directly contravened the Act. The lower court dismissed the action. The court reversed and remanded. It held that the Act stated that the power to regulate the private detective business would be exercised exclusively by the state and that it could not be exercised by any unit of local government, including home rule units. A declaration of exclusivity under Ill. Const. art. VII, § 6(h) (1970) unconditionally barred a home rule unit's exercise of the affected power. The Act repealed by implication the section of the Chicago Municipal Code that authorized municipal regulation of private detectives concurrently with that by the state.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment dismissing the detectives and agencies' action seeking an injunction to prevent the city from enforcing the municipal code and a declaration that it was void. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

North Pier Terminal Co. v. Tully


No. 47849


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 540; 343 N.E.2d 507; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 277



January 20, 1976, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 25, 1976.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. F. Emmett Morrissey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, county and officials, sought review of the summary judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that held in favor of plaintiff taxpayers in the taxpayers' class action challenging the legality of omitted property assessments and the back taxes that were levied thereon, and that permanently enjoined defendants from assessing, levying, or collecting the void taxes from members of the class.


OVERVIEW: After defendants made assessments against omitted property pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 701 (1973), the taxpayers brought a class action against defendants, challenging the legality of such assessments and the back taxes that were levied thereon. The trial court entered summary judgment in favor of the taxpayers, declaring the tax unauthorized in law and void and permanently enjoining defendants from assessing, levying or collecting the void taxes from members of the class. Defendants sought review and contended that the assessment procedure that was followed was not violative of statutory provisions and that the tax was valid. On appeal, the court held that the assessments were not unauthorized by law. The court held that the taxpayers had an adequate remedy at law by way of paying the taxes under protest and filing objections to the application for judgment. Because the taxpayers were not entitled to equitable relief where there was an adequate remedy at law, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court remanded the matter with instructions for the disposition of the other issues that were not involved in the appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment in favor of the taxpayers in the taxpayers' class action that challenged the legality of defendants' assessments against omitted property. The court remanded the matter with instructions for the disposition of the other counts in the complaints that were not involved in the appeal.

 

540 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Berry v. Costello


No. 47598


Supreme Court of Illinois


62 Ill. 2d 342; 341 N.E.2d 709; 1976 Ill. LEXIS 259



January 20, 1976, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of St. Clair County; the Hon. Robert L. Gagen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the county tax collector, challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court, in St. Clair County (Illinois), which, in a class action by appellees, owners of an inhabited mobile homes, declared that the mobile home privilege tax was unconstitutional and granted injunctive and other relief requested by the owners.


OVERVIEW: The owners contended that the "privilege" of living in a mobile home was not a privilege but rather a right protected by the state and federal constitutions. Impliedly, they argued that the right of habitation could not be taxed. The court reversed the judgment because it found that the mobile home privilege tax was constitutionally valid. The owners failed to carry their burden of establishing the invalidity of the tax, as there was ample support for it as a "privilege" or non-property tax. The tax was a reasonable means of defraying the costs incurred by local governmental units in providing certain benefits to the occupants and owners of mobile homes. Owning an occupied mobile home was a taxable privilege. The class defined in the taxing statute was reasonable and the definition of "mobile home" in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 1201(1973), was neither vague nor overbroad.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the circuit court declaring the mobile home privilege tax was unconstitutional and granting the injunctive and other relief requested by the owners in their class action against the collector.

James J. v. People


Nos. 1-88-3231, 1-88-3232, 1-88-3239 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


193 Ill. App. 3d 75; 549 N.E.2d 834; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1996; 140 Ill. Dec. 183



December 29, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Gerald Winiecki, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant minors by their guardian ad litem sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted appellee state's motion to dismiss its petitions for adjudication of wardship. The Illinois Department of Children and Family Services (DCFS) registered petitions for adjudication of wardship based on § 2-3(2)(a)(ii) of the Juvenile Court Act of 1987, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 37, para. 802-3(2)(a)(ii) (1987) (Act).


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the petitions filed for wardship on behalf of the minors on the state's motion. The guardian ad litem for the minors appealed. The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the case. The court found that the cause had been properly appealed pursuant to Ill. Sup. Ct. R. 301, 107 Ill. 2d R. 301. The trial court erred when it refused to consider the state's motion on its merits, and it overlooked the purposes behind the Act. The court ruled that the trial court had an obligation to consider the merits of the motion to dismiss and should have evaluated whether dismissal was in the best interests of the minors, their family, and society. The court reasoned that § 2-13(1) of the Act became meaningless if the trial court reduced its role to that of a rubber stamp. The court found that proceedings under the Act were distinct from criminal prosecutions and that the inquiry did not infringe on the executive authority of the state's attorney's office to initiate and prosecute criminal matters.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court, which had dismissed the petitions for wardship after the state filed a motion for dismissal. The court remanded the case for further proceedings.

Six-Brothers King Drive Supermarket, Inc. v. Department of Revenue


No. 1-87-2745


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


192 Ill. App. 3d 976; 549 N.E.2d 586; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1932; 139 Ill. Dec. 860



December 27, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Irwin Cohen, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed the taxpayer's action for want of jurisdiction and entered judgment in favor of defendant Illinois Department of Revenue (revenue department) on its final tax assessments.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer sought judicial review of tax assessments that were made by the revenue department. The trial court dismissed the complaint due to the taxpayer's failure to provide an appeal bond. On appeal, the taxpayer contended that revenue department's hearing violated due process by denying the taxpayer's request for continuance to produce records and obtain new counsel. The court reversed the trial court's dismissal of the taxpayer's complaint and remanded the case to the revenue department for a new hearing. The court held that the revenue department abused its discretion in denying the taxpayer's request for a continuance. That was an inappropriate to sanction for the taxpayer's delay in producing its books and records. The trial court's refusal to continue the hearing also denied the taxpayer the opportunity to be represented by corporate counsel or counsel of the taxpayer's choice. Although the taxpayer's conduct was inconvenient to the revenue department, the revenue department was required to choose justice over speed. Based on the foregoing, the taxpayer was deprived of a fair and impartial hearing within the meaning of the Fourteenth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded the trial court's dismissal of the taxpayer's complaint for administrative relief and its entry of a judgment for the revenue department on its final tax assessments.

 

543 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gray


No. 1-86-1213


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


192 Ill. App. 3d 907; 549 N.E.2d 730; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1959; 140 Ill. Dec. 79



December 26, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Gino L. DiVito, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged by indictment with armed robbery. Following a jury trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) he was convicted and sentenced to natural life imprisonment pursuant to the Habitual Criminal Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B-1 et seq. (1985). He appealed, and in addition to evidentiary errors, he claimed that the sentencing statutes were unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: In reviewing instructions concerning the presumption of innocence and the burden of proof, the court noted that the trial judge did in fact instruct the jury at the close of the evidence and closing arguments. A generalized question to the jurors as a whole was sufficient to ensure that the venire harbored no prejudices, and no juror indicated that he or she had any reservations about following those concepts. Accordingly, the court followed the dictates of the Illinois Supreme Court and rejected defendant's argument. Convictions for felonies which were less than 10 years old were admissible for impeachment purposes. The fact that two weeks after the robbery defendant was in possession of a weapon and handcuffs identical in appearance to those used in the incident, coupled with positive identification of defendant by two witnesses, was more than sufficient to establish his guilt beyond a reasonable doubt. Further, any minor discrepancies in the witnesses' testimony went to the weight of the testimony as evaluated by the trier of fact. The Habitual Criminal Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33B-1 (1981), was properly passed in accordance with the Illinois Constitution.


OUTCOME: The court concluded defendant's evidentiary and constitutional claims failed, and affirmed his conviction and his sentence under the Habitual Criminal Act.

 

544 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Williams


No. 1-87-1801


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


205 Ill. App. 3d 751; 563 N.E.2d 762; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1949; 150 Ill. Dec. 635



December 26, 1989, Filed  
December 26, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 17, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James B. Bailey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action in initiated by plaintiff state, defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) that denied his motion to suppress his statements. Defendant also asserted that he was not proven guilty of murder beyond a reasonable doubt, and that the imposition of a life sentence violated U.S. Const. amend. VIII and U.S. Const. amend. XIV.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of murder under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 9-1(a) (1983). The court affirmed the judgment. No mitigating circumstances allowed a penalty of less than natural life for two or more murders. The sentencing provision, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1)(c) (1983), was specific and prevailed over a more general provision. No evidence was presented during trial to support defendant's contention that he could have unreasonably believed that circumstances existed that justified killing the victims. The court declined to disturb the denial of the motions to suppress because the trial judge based his decisions on matters contained in the record. The witnesses' accounts contradicted defendant's story. The finding of guilt beyond a reasonable doubt was proper when defendant brought a fully loaded weapon to the crime scene, did not try to revive the victims, and when the victims pleaded for their lives. Defendant's failure to object to the jury instruction limiting the claim of self-defense constituted a waiver. The prosecutor's remarks during closing arguments were proper because they restated the evidence or were supported by the record.


OUTCOME: In the state's criminal action, the court affirmed the judgment that denied defendant's motion to suppress and found him guilty of murder.

 

545 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bradley


No. 1-87-2137


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


192 Ill. App. 3d 387; 548 N.E.2d 743; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1906; 139 Ill. Dec. 358



December 18, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Romie J. Palmer, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which following a jury trial on plaintiff state's charge of possession of a stolen motor vehicle, found the alleged thief guilty, and sentenced him to five years imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant drove off with the motor vehicle after the true owner, with whom defendant had been drinking with that day, left for a moment. The state brought a charge of possession of a stolen motor vehicle, on which defendant was found guilty. The court affirmed the conviction on appeal. The court held that the admission of statements by defendant during police questioning were harmless error because he had not invoked his post-Miranda, Fifth Amendment rights where he refused to answer a single question during police questioning, and defendant had given explanations to the police about other matters in relation to the case. The court determined that defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of counsel was properly rejected where defendant was given an opportunity to make a statement before sentencing and claimed that his attorney failed to subpoena a number of witnesses who would have corroborated his story. The court held that defendant's statement was a mere protestation, not a post-trial motion, which would have required sworn affidavits, and the circuit court properly treated it as such.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction entered by the jury in the circuit court against defendant on the state's charge of possession of a stolen motor vehicle.

 

546 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Flowers


No. 1-86-2441


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


192 Ill. App. 3d 292; 548 N.E.2d 766; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1908; 139 Ill. Dec. 381



December 18, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected. Original Opinion of same date reported at 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1895 


PRIOR HISTORY: Original Opinion of December 18, 1989 Reported at 192 Ill. App. 3d 298 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part; vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of armed robbery and felony murder. On appeal, the court vacated the felony murder conviction, and remanded for a new trial. The state sought a rehearing on the decision to vacate defendant's murder conviction and raised the additional issue of whether the Reddick error was harmless in light of the felony murder charge.


OVERVIEW: The trial court had not given the jury the Reddick murder and manslaughter instruction charge. The jury returned a verdict of felony manslaughter, for the victim's death, which had occurred during defendant's commission of an armed robbery. Acknowledging the jury's armed robbery conviction, defendant asserted that the court had no way of knowing whether the jury found that the killing was "in the course of the robbery" to constitute felony murder. The court vacated the felony murder conviction. The state argued that the Reddick error was irrelevant to defendant's murder conviction because a valid conviction for armed robbery necessarily meant defendant was guilty of felony murder. The court disagreed and remanded for a new trial on the felony murder charge. The court stated that a murder conviction need not have been reversed despite the existence of a Reddick error if the error could have been deemed harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. The court found that the evidence was not overwhelming so that the jury could not have found anything but that the victim's death was caused during the course of the armed robbery. Therefore, the court held that the Reddick error was not harmless.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the armed robbery conviction, vacated the felony murder conviction, and remanded for a new trial on the felony murder charge.

 

547 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Aloha, Inc. v. Illinois Liquor Control Com.


No. 4-89-0277


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


191 Ill. App. 3d 523; 548 N.E.2d 116; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1864; 138 Ill. Dec. 886



December 14, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. Simon L. Friedman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff bar sought review of the findings and fine imposed by defendant, the Illinois Liquor Control Commission (Commission). The Circuit Court for Sangamon County (Illinois) affirmed the decision.


OVERVIEW: The bar was cited for maintaining its premises in an unclean and unsanitary manner in violation of Ill. Admin. Code tit. 11, §§ 100.160(a), 100.290(c). The Commission entered an order imposing a fine in the amount of $ 2,000 against the bar. The bar contended that § 100.160(a) violated its due process rights as it was unconstitutionally vague. The court held that the term "clean and sanitary" was not vague. However, nothing informed the bar the Commission would seek fines for a violation continuing after the day of the inspection. Nothing suggested the bar was charged with multiple violations of § 100.290. The Commission was limited to fining the bar for those charges on which the bar had reasonable notice. The statutory limitation on the Commission's fines was $ 500 per violation pursuant to the Liquor Control Act of 1934, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, para. 108, and the bar had adequate notice of only two violations.


OUTCOME: The decision of the circuit court was reversed as to the fine imposed and the cause was remanded with instructions for the circuit court to remand to the Commission to reduce the fine to $ 1,000. The circuit court's decision in all other respects was affirmed.

 

548 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Cramsey v. Knoblock


No. 4-89-0363


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


191 Ill. App. 3d 756; 547 N.E.2d 1358; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1872; 138 Ill. Dec. 737



December 14, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 17, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Adams County; the Hon. Robert L. Welch, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Adams County, Illinois, which dismissed the medical malpractice portions of their complaint against defendant doctor for failure to bring the action within the period allowed by the statute of limitations.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, individually and as administrators of the estate of a decedent, filed a claim against the driver of a vehicle involved in a collision with decedent's vehicle, and later filed an amended complaint against defendants, a treating doctor and clinic, alleging failure to diagnose a tumor in the course of treating the decedent's injuries. In affirming the order dismissing the complaint as barred by the statute of limitations, the court held that the statute began to run when plaintiffs knew or reasonably should have known not only that an injury had occurred, but also that the injury was wrongfully caused. As allegations of pain and suffering could only involve the period prior to death, the limitation period would ordinarily begin on that date. Plaintiffs knew that the tumor had not been diagnosed prior to the death, and estoppel did not apply, for there was no reliance on defendant's conduct which caused them to forego the filing of suit. There was no fraudulent concealment, as there was no affirmative act or representation calculated to induce a claimant to delay filing a claim or keep him from discovering its existence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order dismissing the malpractice portions of the complaint, as an action filed more than two years after death was barred by the statute of limitations.

Cummings v. Beaton & Assoc., Inc.


No. 1-89-0336


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fourth Division


192 Ill. App. 3d 792; 549 N.E.2d 634; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1861; 139 Ill. Dec. 908

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, husband and wife, sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which impounded the trial record and ordered the parties to refrain from discussing certain allegations found in the second amended complaint against defendant corporations.


OVERVIEW: The husband and wife filed a complaint against the corporations that was later dismissed. Subsequently, they filed a second amended complaint. At the hearing, the corporations objected to the filing of the second amended complaint, in part because it contained "scurrilous" allegations that had not been raised in the original complaint. One of the allegations in this complaint supposedly tied the chairman of the board of one of the corporations to a plot to murder the husband. The trial court allowed the husband and wife to file the second amended complaint, but impounded the trial record and ordered the parties to refrain from discussing the allegations. The husband and wife argued that the order violated the free speech and due process clauses of the federal and sate constitutions. The court vacated the order, holding that the corporations did not demonstrate what important or substantial governmental interest was at stake and in need of protection by the gag order.


OUTCOME: The court vacated and remanded the order, which impounded the trial record and ordered the parties to refrain from discussing certain allegations found in the second amended complaint against the corporations, because they did not demonstrate what important or substantial governmental interest was at stake and in need of protection by the gag order.

 

550 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rocha


No. 2-88-0942


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


191 Ill. App. 3d 529; 547 N.E.2d 1335; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1858; 138 Ill. Dec. 714



December 13, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Ogle County; the Hon. John L. Moore, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from the Circuit Court of Ogle County (Illinois), which granted defendant's motion to bar evidence of the out-of-court statements of the three year-old victim under the hearsay exception pertaining to victims of sexual abuse under age 13, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115 -- 10 (1987). The trial court held that the evidence was inadmissible because the victim was not unavailable to testify.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with aggravated criminal sexual assault in violation of the Criminal Code of 1961, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12 -- 14(b)(1) (1987). Because the child would not be testifying at trial, the hearsay evidence in question was offered under the then new statutory provision applicable when the child victim was "unavailable as a witness." Counsel for defendant and the State stipulated that the child was not competent to testify at trial because of her young age. The trial court held that the child's statements were not admissible under either a common-law hearsay exception or the provisions of the statutory hearsay exception because the victim's incompetence to testify was not within the meaning of the word "unavailable" as used in the statute. On appeal, the court reversed because a child's first accounts of an incident of sexual abuse were sometimes more reliable than later testimony given in the often intimidating courtroom setting. The court held that, if the child was unwilling or unable to testify, this would support a finding that the witness was "unavailable" for Sixth Amendment purposes and the confrontation guarantees of the Illinois constitution.


OUTCOME: The court held that the trial court's ruling rested upon an incorrect interpretation of the statute. Therefore, the court reversed the trial court's order granting the motion of the defendant to exclude the out-of-court statements of the child victim and remanded for further proceedings in conformity with this opinion.

 

551 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Reding


No. 2-87-0486


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


191 Ill. App. 3d 424; 547 N.E.2d 1310; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1820; 138 Ill. Dec. 689



December 7, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. John L. Nickels, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order by the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which found defendant guilty of reckless homicide as a result of circumstances arising out of an automobile collision.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction, alleging numerous errors on the part of the circuit court. The court, however, found that the circuit court had not abused its discretion in admitting evidence of defendant's blood-alcohol content, as contended by defendant. Further, it was not an abuse of discretion to allow an expert to give an opinion based upon his investigation as to the point of impact. In addition, the circuit court had not abused its discretion regarding any procedural matters at trial. Defendant failed to establish that his attorney's conduct fell below an objective level of reasonableness and that "but for" his attorney's conduct, the outcome would probably have been different. The court found that there was sufficient evidence presented from which the jury could have found defendant guilty of reckless homicide beyond a reasonable doubt. The jury was presented with evidence that defendant was driving while intoxicated at the time of the collision. Additionally, it was shown that defendant turned his vehicle in front of oncoming traffic, which caused the collision and the victim's death. Therefore, defendant was proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the circuit court's conviction of defendant for reckless homicide.

Rivera v. O'Leary


No. 3-89-0119


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


191 Ill. App. 3d 367; 547 N.E.2d 1035; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1824; 138 Ill. Dec. 609



December 6, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Edward F. Masters, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prisoner sought review of the order of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which dismissed his petition for a writ of habeas corpus after he was denied parole.


OVERVIEW: The prisoner was serving an indeterminate term for murder. He had been denied parole on at least seven occasions. In denying his last parole request, the Prisoner Review Board (board) cited as its rationale that granting him parole would deprecate the seriousness of his offense. On appeal, the petitioner first argued that the board denied his request for parole based on arbitrary and capricious reasons and that the statutory standard for parole was invalid since it establishes a deterrent criterion, while the Illinois Constitution mandated a rehabilitative criterion. The court affirmed, holding that the trial court properly dismissed the prisoner's petition for failure to state a claim because the Illinois Habeas Corpus Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 10 -- 101 et seq. (1987), did not provide relief to a prisoner whose request for parole had been unreasonably, arbitrarily, or capriciously denied. The court also held that the board could properly consider principles of retributive justice and general deterrence in rendering its decisions. The court stated it found no due process violation in the prisoner's case.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which dismissed the prisoner's petition for habeas corpus relief.
