Earnhart v. Director of Dep't of Revenue


No. 5-88-0267


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


191 Ill. App. 3d 613; 548 N.E.2d 81; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1835; 138 Ill. Dec. 851



December 6, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. Michael J. Meehan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff store owners appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois), which upheld the constitutionality of the Charitable Games Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 121 et seq. (1987), and affirmed a penalty assessed on the store owners by the Director of the Illinois Department of Revenue (Director) for holding charitable games without a license as required by the Act.


OVERVIEW: The store owners were assessed a penalty by the Director for operating charitable games without a license as required by the Act. The store owners brought an action challenging the constitutionality of the Act and the penalty imposed by the Director. The trial court upheld the act and affirmed the penalty. The store owners appealed, contending that the Act was unconstitutionally vague and thus denied the store owners due process, that the Act was overbroad, reaching beyond gambling to other games, and therefore denied the store owners due process, and that the Act was an unlawful delegation of legislative authority because it did not specify the games to which it applied, thereby allowing the Illinois Department of Revenue to determine what games to license under the Act. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the Act was not overbroad because it did not reach beyond its purpose to regulate certain games, that no fundamental right was infringed by the Act because the activity licensed was not speech, and that the act did not deprive the store owners of equal protection of law. The Act allowed only specified games to be played and required a license to hold an event.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which upheld the constitutionality of Act and affirmed a penalty assessed on the store owners by the Director for holding charitable games without a license.

Berkin v. Orland Park Plaza Bank


No. 1-88-2685


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


191 Ill. App. 3d 1056; 548 N.E.2d 534; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1808; 139 Ill. Dec. 149



December 5, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Myron Gomberg, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individuals appealed an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which granted defendant bank's § 2-611 of the Code of Civil Procedure, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-611 (1987), motion against plaintiffs and their attorneys and assessed attorney fees and costs solely against plaintiffs.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs contended that the § 2-611 motion was not timely filed, and even if it was, the sanction award was improperly assessed against them and included improperly assessed fees. In reversing the order of the circuit court, the court held that former § 2-611 applied. Under former § 2-611, the circuit court lacked discretion to exact a penalty incommensurate with time, effort, and expense incurred by the aggrieved party as a consequence of untrue pleadings. The court noted that the record was devoid of proof that any plaintiff actually caused sanctionable conduct. Furthermore, the court found that neither the pleadings nor any of the other matters appearing in the record justified a finding of sanctions against plaintiffs. Rather, the court concluded that the facts in the record indicated that the responsibility for the untrue pleadings rested solely with plaintiffs' counsel. According to the court, former § 2-611 did not apply to attorneys.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the circuit court.

 

555 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Bessler


Nos. 2-88-0118, 2-88-0119, 2-88-0120 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


191 Ill. App. 3d 374; 548 N.E.2d 52; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1802; 138 Ill. Dec. 822



December 4, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 8, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Robert A. Nolan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was arrested for weapons offenses and possession of an illegal substance. He filed a pretrial motion to suppress evidence claiming the search of his garage pursuant to a search warrant was based on an unlawful warrantless administrative search. The Circuit Court of DuPage County (Illinois), denied the motion and convicted defendant in a bench trial. Defendant appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed that an administrative search by a housing inspector was unlawful and the evidence seized pursuant to the search warrant issued after the unlawful warrantless search should have been suppressed. The state claimed the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule applied. The court reversed and remanded. The court noted that the good faith exception to the exclusionary rule extended to a warrantless administrative search of a business premises even though the state statute on which the search was based was subsequently found unconstitutional. The court would not extend the good faith exception to defendant's home. The expectation of privacy that the owner of commercial property enjoyed differed significantly from the sanctity accorded an individual's home. In the absence of consent or exigent circumstances, the entry into a home to conduct a search or make an arrest was unreasonable without a warrant, and where the initial search was unlawful, the information gained therefrom could not form the basis for the issuance of a search warrant and evidence so obtained was inadmissible. The denial of the motion to suppress was erroneous.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction was reversed and the case was remanded for a new trial. Evidence seized pursuant to the search warrant and statements made subsequent to defendant's arrest were suppressed.

 

556 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Gentry


No. 1-87-2913


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


192 Ill. App. 3d 774; 549 N.E.2d 609; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1783; 139 Ill. Dec. 883



December 1, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 22, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James J. Schreier, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted after a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), on a charge of possession of a stolen motor vehicle pursuant to para. 4-103 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103 (1987). Defendant appealed his conviction.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that para. 4-103 violated due process guarantees. Specifically, defendant asserted that the statute violated due process because it punished every possessor of a stolen motor vehicle who had knowledge the vehicle was stolen without regard to when that knowledge was acquired or how innocently possession was obtained. The court ruled that the statute was not unconstitutional and affirmed defendant's conviction. The statute was reasonably related to the purpose of preventing vehicle theft and "chop shop" operations because it worked directly against activities involved in the procurement of stolen motor vehicles and chop shop operations by making it an offense to conceal, sell, dispose of, or transfer stolen vehicles. It was further related to its intended purpose by its inclusion of any individual who received or possessed a stolen vehicle. It was immaterial whether para. 4-103 was the most direct means for effectuating those purposes. The statute contained the requisite culpable conduct necessary to effectuate the purpose of the statute, and the constructive knowledge aspect of the statute did not create a conflicting mental state requirement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

People ex rel. Rice v. Graves


No. 4-89-0381


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


191 Ill. App. 3d 220; 547 N.E.2d 717; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1764; 138 Ill. Dec. 550



November 30, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. James Hendrian, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant state sought review of a decision by the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) that issued an order dismissing a petition to establish parentage and support filed against appellee father, as related by the mother, on behalf of her minor child. The action was dismissed on grounds that it was not refiled within one year of the previous dismissal without prejudice, or within the remainder of the limitation period.


OVERVIEW: The prior action was filed by the mother and subsequently dismissed for failure to prosecute. The current action as brought by the state on behalf of the child. The father contended that the instant proceeding was barred by the fact a paternity action filed by the state on the relation of the mother was dismissed for want of prosecution. The court held that the statute of limitations did not bar the second action because while the mother might be prohibited from filing another action, the child was not so barred. The court held that an action under the Ill. Parentage Act of 1984, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2501 et seq. (1987), might be brought by or on behalf of the child not later than two years after the child attained the age of majority. The court reasoned that technically, the child had no cause of action under the Paternity Act and, therefore, the dismissal of the mother's action had no effect whatsoever on the right of the child to bring an action under the Parentage Act.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of dismissal and remanded for further proceedings.

People v. Daniel


No. 1-86-2617


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division

November 17, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James M. Bailey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, citing Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 7-1, 9-2(b), 9-1(c), 1005-8-1(a)(1)(b) (1985), appealed a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted and sentenced him for murder, attempted murder, and aggravated battery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot two men during a gang turf incident. He contended that he acted in self-defense or should have been found guilty of no more than voluntary manslaughter, that the trial court erred in failing to instruct the jury on defendant's belief in his justification, and that the sentence was excessive. The court affirmed the judgment. The court determined that the evidence supported the jury's rejection of self-defense. The court noted that the mitigating factor of no prior involvement with the police was considered and was the reason defendant was not sentenced to death, and found no error in the omission of any reference to the statutory section under which sentence was imposed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting and sentencing defendant for murder, attempted murder, and aggravated battery.

People v. Pehrson


No. 2-88-0326


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


190 Ill. App. 3d 928; 547 N.E.2d 613; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1708; 138 Ill. Dec. 446



November 14, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Richard A. Lucas, Judge, presiding.

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction and sentence in a bench trial in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) for delivery of less than one gram of cocaine under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(c) (1987) and for possessing with intent to deliver more than 1 but less than 15 grams of cocaine under § 1401(b)(2).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested at a party after two men identified defendant as the person who had sold them cocaine. OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence for delivery of less than one gram of cocaine and for possessing with intent to deliver more than 1 but less than 15 grams of cocaine.

People v. Jimenez


No. 1-86-3471


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


191 Ill. App. 3d 13; 547 N.E.2d 616; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1717; 138 Ill. Dec. 449



November 14, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 12, 1989. As Corrected.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Ronald J.P. Banks, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him for violating Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 12 -- 14(b)(1) (1987) (aggravated criminal assault), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 12 -- 13(1) (1987) (criminal sexual assault), aggravated kidnapping, and attempted aggravated kidnapping in connection with the attempted abduction and the abduction and sexual assault of two young children.


OVERVIEW: Defendant unsuccessfully attempted to kidnap one child but successfully kidnapped and sexually assaulted another child. The children accurately described defendant and his car and were able to identify him in a lineup. Neither the criminal sexual assault (CSA) statute nor the aggravated criminal sexual assault (ACSA) statute were unconstitutional on the ground that they punished innocent behavior because the mental states of intent, knowledge, or recklessness were implied for offenses involving "sexual penetration." Thus, the statutes required some degree of culpability and did not punish innocent behavior. The court held that only one conviction for ACSA was proper; however, the court held that it did not believe that improper multiple convictions were considered at sentencing because the trial court indicated that all such convictions were merged and imposed a single sentence under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, par. 12 -- 14(a)(2). The court vacated the order, however, and remanded to correct that order to reflect a single conviction for ACSA. Resentencing was not required, however, because nothing suggested that the sentence for ACSA was influenced by the conviction for CSA.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's sentence; however, the court vacated all but one conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault.

 

561 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hagen


No. 4-89-0328


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


191 Ill. App. 3d 265; 547 N.E.2d 577; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1699; 138 Ill. Dec. 410



November 9, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Sangamon County; the Hon. John A. Mehlick, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the conviction for operating a motor vehicle with obstructed, or tinted, front side windows that the Sangamon County Circuit Court (Illinois) adjudged against him.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the pertinent statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 12 -- 503(a) (1987), violated his rights to equal protection of the laws guaranteed by the United States and Illinois Constitutions, in that the statute only applied to vehicles built on or after a certain date. The prosecution prevailed. The court noted that the statute's purpose was to protect the safety of law enforcement personnel who stopped and approached a vehicle. The court observed that the statute was subject to only a rational basis level of review, so that it was presumptively constitutional. If there could be any possible rational basis for the legislation, the statute had to be upheld. The legislature was not obligated to give a reason for enacting a statute, especially where line-drawing was involved. The decision on where to draw the line was a difficult one and was best left to the wisdom of the legislature. Whether this decision by the legislature was wise or the best course chosen was not a proper subject of judicial inquiry. The statute was a permissible exercise of legislative authority under both the federal and Illinois Constitutions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

People v. Heidelberg

The court affirmed.

563 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Ramsey


No. 5-88-0487


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


190 Ill. App. 3d 723; 546 N.E.2d 1108; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1688; 138 Ill. Dec. 53



November 3, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Jefferson County; the Hon. Lehman Krause, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of conviction by the Circuit Court of Jefferson County (Illinois) for aggravated criminal sexual assault, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 12-14(b)(1) (1987). Defendant contended that the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute deprived him of due process under the United States and Illinois Constitutions.


OVERVIEW: The state argued that because defendant was convicted of placing his penis in the anus of the victim, his standing to challenge the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute was limited to that type of conduct. The court agreed and affirmed the judgment of conviction. A defendant may challenge a statute as overbroad on the ground that it may be applied unconstitutionally to situations and questions not before the court only if the statute was one that may inhibit the exercise of rights of expression or association protected under the First Amendment. The hypothetical situations posited by defendant as examples of the statute's overbreadth did not implicate the First Amendment rights of expression or association. Thus, the court found that defendant lacked standing to challenge the statute as overbroad. The defendant also argued that the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute violated due process because no mental state was required for conviction. However, the court found that the aggravated criminal sexual assault statute implicitly required that the act of sexual penetration must be intentional or knowing. Therefore, the court found no violation of due process.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction for aggravated criminal sexual assault against defendant was affirmed.

 

564 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Fyke


No. 5-87-0858


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


190 Ill. App. 3d 713; 546 N.E.2d 1101; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1671; 138 Ill. Dec. 46



November 2, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Marion County; the Hon. Michael R. Weber, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Marion County (Illinois), which convicted him of murder. Defendant was sentenced to 50 years in prison.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction resulted from his participation in a conspiracy to kill a man whom the conspirators believed to be an informant who was jeopardizing their drug enterprise. On appeal, defendant argued that his arrest warrant was not valid because it had not been sworn to as required by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 111-3(b). The court found that the warrant was valid because the state's attorney who prepared and signed the information was present when the documents were presented to the judge, so there was no doubt as to their authenticity. The court concluded that defendant's arrest would have been valid without a warrant because he was arrested outside his home. The court found that the trial court properly admitted evidence of guns and ammunition, not connected with the crime, that was found in defendant's home. The court found that this evidence was relevant because it tended to indicate that defendant was prepared to use deadly force to defend his drug enterprise. The court found that the trial judge properly instructed the jury on the law of accountability. The court concluded that the imposition of the extended-term sentence was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for murder and his sentence of 50 years in prison.

 

565 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Miller


No. 1-86-2296


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


193 Ill. App. 3d 918; 552 N.E.2d 988; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1640; 137 Ill. Dec. 761



October 27, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Michael Getty, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and vacated in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgments of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of two counts of voluntary manslaughter and sentenced him to consecutive prison sentences.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the trial court erred in imposing consecutive sentences and in relying on the impact testimony of a victim's brother at the sentencing hearing. The court affirmed the judgments of conviction but vacated the consecutive sentences. It stated that the trial court's authority to impose consecutive sentences was limited. The court found that imposition of the consecutive sentences was improper because the evidence failed to establish that there was a substantial change in the nature of defendant's criminal objective during defendant's course of conduct in the commission of the two manslaughter offenses. It further reasoned that the manslaughter deaths could not be considered the severe bodily injury required for imposition of a consecutive sentence under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-4 (1987) because the severe bodily injury of death was also an essential element of voluntary manslaughter. The court concluded that admission of the victim impact testimony was not erroneous because it was truly innocuous and there was no evidence that the trial judge relied on it in determining and imposing the imprisonment sentence for each manslaughter conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed that portion of the trial court's judgments convicting defendant of manslaughter. It vacated that portion of the judgments requiring that the two imprisonment sentences be served consecutively and ordered that the sentences be served concurrently.

People v. Brown


Nos. 1-87-0485, 1-87-0530 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


194 Ill. App. 3d 958; 553 N.E.2d 712; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1647; 143 Ill. Dec. 5

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Kenneth L. Gillis, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted them of possession of burglary tools and attempted residential burglary and sentenced both defendants to concurrent terms of 10 years for burglary and 3 years for possession of burglary tools.


OVERVIEW: Defendants were charged with possession of burglary tools and attempted residential burglary. After a bench trial both defendants received concurrent terms for burglary and possession of burglary tools. Defendants appealed and the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court held that the first defendant did not demonstrate any error on the part of the trial court in denying severance for him. The court held that the police officers, acting with knowledge of the attempted burglary, during a surveillance of the car that had the license number identified by the witnesses to the attempted burglary, and having viewed the first defendant approach the auto and place an object in the trunk, had sufficient probable cause to arrest him. Accordingly, the court found that the trial court's rulings that denied the first defendant's motion to quash and admitted the post-arrest lineup identification were proper. The court held that a proper foundation was established for the admission of the second defendant's license registration, and the state also provided additional evidence of that defendant's control of the car.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments of the trial court that convicted defendants of possession of burglary tools and attempted residential burglary and sentenced them to concurrent terms.

People v. Wehrwein


No. 1-87-1487


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


190 Ill. App. 3d 35; 545 N.E.2d 1005; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1589; 137 Ill. Dec. 244



October 16, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James M. Schreier, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant for possession of a stolen motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for possession of a stolen motor vehicle in connection with his possession of stolen tractor-trailer. At trial, a police officer testified that while working undercover he saw defendant operate the vehicle, that he saw a car registered to defendant following the car, and that after the truck had pulled over to the side of the road, defendant had disappeared. The officer also testified that he subsequently identified defendant in a photo lineup. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction. The court held that: (1) defendant was proven guilty beyond a reasonable doubt because the state proved the identification of defendant and proved each element of the crime charged; (2) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in allowing the state to recall a witness; (3) the trial court did not err in allowing the state to call a certain witness during its case in chief where the name of the witness was not included in the state's answer to discovery; and (4) defendant's conviction and sentence did not need to be vacated because the statute under which he was convicted and sentenced was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a stolen motor vehicle.

 

568 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jenkins


No. 1-87-3785


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


190 Ill. App. 3d 115; 545 N.E.2d 986; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1582; 137 Ill. Dec. 225



October 13, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph J. Urso, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied his motion for a directed verdict, his post trial motion, and convicted him of aggravated battery and felony murder.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged and convicted of aggravated battery and felony murder. Defendant challenged the application of the felony murder doctrine, the use of non-pattern jury instructions, evidentiary rulings, prosecutorial comments, and the constitutionality of the sentence. The court affirmed the convictions and the imposition of sentence for felony murder because defendant knowingly struck a police officer who was holding a cocked and loaded gun while engaged in his official duty, it was foreseeable that the gun would fire during a struggle and cause injury, and the battery formed the basis for the forcible felony that substituted for the intent required for felony murder. The court found that: 1) the non-pattern jury instructions properly stated the law applicable to the facts; 2) the widow's civil lawsuit against the city and the post-trial discovery of evidence discrediting the officer's reputation had no probative value in determining defendant's guilt or innocence; 3) the state's closing argument was not inflammatory and was appropriate; 4) the deadlocked jury instruction to continue deliberating was neutral; and 5) the sentence did not violate the Eighth Amendment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction on charges of aggravated battery and felony murder and the imposition of sentence.

People v. Cameron


No. 4-89-0071


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


189 Ill. App. 3d 998; 546 N.E.2d 259; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1554; 137 Ill. Dec. 505



October 5, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Brown County; the Hon. David K. Slocum, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed and cause remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Brown County (Illinois), which entered a jury verdict convicting defendant of unlawful possession and distribution of cocaine and cannabis, aggravated battery of a peace officer, and fleeing or attempting to elude a police officer, sentencing defendant to imprisonment, and imposing a fine.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with the various narcotics offenses after he purchased narcotics from an undercover officer. Defendant was charged with assault and fleeing an officer after he sped away during an investigatory stop, injuring an officer. On appeal from his convictions, the court affirmed, holding that the trial court properly limited defendant's cross-examination of the undercover officer with regard to a civil action filed against him for misidentification of a narcotics purchaser. Any alleged incentive on the officer's part to give favorable testimony because of the pending civil suit was remote and uncertain, and testimony of the officer's prior conduct would have initiated a lengthy side issue, which would have distracted the jury from the main issue of the case. Further, the admission of improper hearsay evidence from an informant concerning defendant's recent purchase of illegal drugs and intention to dispose of them because he thought the police were watching him was harmless. The admission was harmless because of the uncontested and overwhelming nature of the evidence of the factual matters involved in the controlled substance offenses which the hearsay concerned.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed all of the convictions and sentences entered against defendant. The court also remanded with directions to credit defendant with the amount imposed as a fine.

People v. Dale


Nos. 1-86-0515, 1-86-0716 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


189 Ill. App. 3d 704; 545 N.E.2d 521; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1548; 136 Ill. Dec. 997



September 29, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Michael P. Toomin, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants challenged the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted them of murder, rape, home invasion, residential burglary and robbery, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, paras. 9-1, 11-1, 19-3, 18-1 (1983). The court sentenced defendants to extended-term sentences of 60 and 80 years for the murder convictions and concurrent sentences of 30 years for rape and home invasion, 15 years for burglary and 7 years for robbery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant two appealed his sentences as excessive, while defendant one appealed both his conviction and sentence based on multiple contentions. The court found it was necessary to remand defendant one's case challenging his conviction because a two-part Batson hearing needed to be conducted by the trial court. The court held that after reviewing the trial and suppression hearing evidence concerning the totality of the circumstances, the trial court's finding that the state proved the voluntariness of defendant one's confession by a preponderance of the evidence was not against the manifest weight of the evidence. Further, the court held that the trial court's determination that the officers had probable cause to arrest him was not manifestly erroneous. Also, the court found his confrontation with his accomplice's untainted statement, which was obtained prior to his arrest, was an intervening circumstance that purged the taint of any illegal arrest. Finally, as to defendant two the court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in sentencing him because he was not a passive observer of the conduct of the defendant one.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed in part and remanded the conviction of defendant one, finding that he was entitled to a Batson hearing. Defendant two's sentences were affirmed because he could be liable as an accomplice.

Department of Transp. ex rel. People v. First Galesburg Nat'l Bank & Trust Co.


Nos. 3-88-0585, 3-88-0590 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


189 Ill. App. 3d 797; 545 N.E.2d 770; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1524; 137 Ill. Dec. 117



September 27, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Warren County; the Hon. Scott I. Klukos, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowner challenged the order of the Circuit Court of Warren County (Illinois), which denied its traverse and motion to dismiss the complaint for condemnation and "quick take" motions filed by plaintiff, the Illinois Department of Transportation (Department).


OVERVIEW: The Department filed a complaint for condemnation seeking to acquire fee simple title to the existing right-of-way for which it already had a surface-only dedication, and to strips of land adjacent to the existing right-of-way in order to widen a highway. The Department filed "quick take" motions, and the landowner filed a traverse and motion to dismiss. The court reversed the trial court's order. The court held that the landowner could appeal the court's findings as to the Department's authority to exercise the right of eminent domain, the susceptibility of the property to its exercise, and its proper exercise in the case, pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 47, para. 2.2(b) (1969) (repealed 1979, now codified at Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 7-104(b) (1979). The court held that: (1) § 4-501 of the Illinois Highway Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121, para. 4-501 (1987), provided sufficient standards to guide the Department in the exercise of its discretion; (2) the Department could not take more of an interest in the property that it demonstrated it had a need for; and (3) the Department did not meet its burden to establish a prima facie right to condemn the property.


OUTCOME: The court reversed that portion of the circuit court's order that denied the landowner's motion to dismiss the Department's action to condemn the fee interest to the land already in use as a highway pursuant to a prior dedication.

People v. Crest


No. 2-88-0493


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


188 Ill. App. 3d 768; 544 N.E.2d 825; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1449; 136 Ill. Dec. 139



September 25, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Du Page County; the Hon. Richard A. Lucas, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction in the Circuit Court of Du Page County (Illinois) for burglary in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19--1(a).


OVERVIEW: After reading a burglary report indicating that wire had been stolen from a local company, a police officer received tips from an anonymous informer on defendant's attempt to sell stolen wire. The officer watched defendant's home and later stopped the car in which defendant was a passenger to determine its contents. After finding wire in the trunk, the officer arrested defendant. The trial court denied defendant's motion to quash the arrest and suppress evidence and convicted defendant of burglary. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction, holding that (1) the initial stop of the car did not violate the Fourth Amendment because the officer had an articulable suspicion that the persons in the car were involved in criminal activity, justifying a stop of the car for investigatory purposes; (2) the articulable suspicion was supported by the officer's own observations combined with reliable tips from the informant; and (3) the officer had probable cause to arrest defendant after searching the car where the officer took investigative steps to corroborate reliable tips from the informant and found in the trunk the same type of wire that was reported to have been stolen.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of burglary.

Kawasaki Shop of Aurora, Inc. v. Kawasaki Motors Corp., U.S.A.


No. 2-88-1058


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


188 Ill. App. 3d 664; 544 N.E.2d 457; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1442; 136 Ill. Dec. 4



September 22, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County; the Hon. Patrick J. Dixon, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant manufacturer appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois), which ruled in favor of plaintiff dealer in an action for breach of contract and a violation of the Motor Vehicle Franchise Act (act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121 1/2, para. 751 et seq. (1987). Dealer cross-appealed.


OVERVIEW: Manufacturer terminated dealer's franchise because it did not approve of the location to which dealer wanted to move. Dealer brought an action alleging that the termination violated the act and that manufacturer had breached its contract. The complaint alleged that manufacturer's conduct was willful and wanton and sought treble damages. Manufacturer counterclaimed. The trial court ruled in favor of dealer on both counts, found that manufacturer's actions were willful and wanton, awarded attorney fees, but did not award treble damages. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the trial court properly instructed the jury as to site control because improper site control in violation of the act could be accomplished by means other than through the provisions of a lease. The court held that the trial court's verdict was not against the manifest weight of the evidence because implicit in the act was the idea that a dealer should not be terminated for affiliating with a competing line. On the cross appeal, the court held that the trial court's denial of treble damages to dealer was proper because the act provided that the power to award treble damages was permissive, not mandatory.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court in favor of dealer and against manufacturer as to both the appeal and cross appeal.

Evanston v. Evanston Fire Fighters Asso.


No. 1-87-0473


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


189 Ill. App. 3d 233; 545 N.E.2d 252; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1446; 136 Ill. Dec. 728



September 22, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Joseph M. Wosik, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant firefighter's association appealed from an order of the Circuit Court of Cook County in favor of plaintiff city, finding defendant in violation of the Solicitation Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 5111(d)(1985), and enjoining defendant from using its name and emblem in soliciting funds from the public.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff city brought an action for an injunction against defendant, an association of city firefighters, under the Solicitation Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 23, para. 5111(d)(1985). The trial court granted the injunction, restraining defendant from the use of its name and logo, both of which included the name of plaintiff city, in soliciting funds. Defendant appealed, and the court reversed. The court held that the state Attorney General was exclusively empowered to seek injunctive relief under the Act, and, therefore, that plaintiff had no standing. Further, the court found that plaintiff had not proven a violation of the Act. The court noted that no evidence was presented that defendant's use of plaintiff's name tended to confuse or mislead the public into believing that plaintiff was connected with defendant's fundraising campaign. Pointing to defendant's extended previous relationship with the community, its long history of existence and use of its name and logo, and the substantial steps made to ensure that the public was correctly informed of defendant's identity and purpose, the court found no violation as a matter of law.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the circuit court's order granting the relief requested by plaintiff city, which found defendant firefighter association to be in violation of the Illinois Solicitation Act (Act), and enjoined defendant from the use of its name and logo in soliciting funds. The court held that plaintiff had no standing to seek enforcement of the Act, and that defendant was not in violation as a matter of law.

People v. Barnhill


No. 5-87-0818


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


188 Ill. App. 3d 299; 543 N.E.2d 1374; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1443; 135 Ill. Dec. 627



September 19, 1989, Filed

DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with murder in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1)(b). He entered a plea of guilty but mentally ill. The Circuit Court of Franklin County, Illinois, sentenced defendant to imprisonment for his natural life. Defendant filed a pro se motion to withdraw his guilty plea. The trial court denied the motion and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant lured a female victim to a vacant house where he raped and killed her, choking her with a wire coat hangar, his bare hands, and a foot. The court found that defendant was properly queried under 107 Ill. 2d R. 402(b) regarding the voluntariness of his plea. In affirming, the court found that the trial court substantially complied with Rule 402(b), and was not required to apply the rule verbatim. The court held that defendant's guilty plea was not revocable simply because he subjectively believed that he would receive a certain sentence. The court held that the phrase "exceptionally brutal or heinous behavior indicative of wanton cruelty" under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 1005-8-1(a)(1)(b) (1985) was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to his case because defendant engaged in cold-blooded behavior, devoid of mercy and compassion. The court held that a sentence of natural life imprisonment was proper because the trial court considered defendant's age, his drug and alcohol use, and his mental illness, but found that the day after the murder he drank alcohol, used drugs, and committed another crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's imposition of imprisonment for defendant's natural life and held that evidence supported the trial court's finding that the murder was brutal and heinous.

People v. Malone


No. 1-87-2347


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


188 Ill. App. 3d 1094; 545 N.E.2d 168; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1412; 136 Ill. Dec. 644



September 15, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Fred G. Suria, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which found him guilty of possession of a stolen motor vehicle, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103(a)(1) (1985), sentenced him to four years' probation, and ordered him to pay restitution to the victim.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed on appeal that the offense created by § 4-103(a) did not bear a reasonable relation to a legitimate state purpose or use a reasonable method to further or protect the state's interest for which the statute was enacted, that in setting a greater penalty for the crime of possession than for the included offense of theft, § 4-103(a) violated the due process and proportionate penalty clauses of the Illinois Constitution, and that § 4-103(a) violated due process guarantees because it embodied contradictory mental states that denied citizens fair notice of what conduct was prohibited thereunder. The court affirmed, concluding that defendant's first two claims were foreclosed by a prior decision of the Illinois Supreme Court and that the third claim was without merit. With regard to the third claim, the court found that the statute comported with due process requirements because it provided persons of ordinary intelligence with a reasonable opportunity to ascertain what conduct was prohibited thereunder. Further, the court determined that the statute was sufficient to apprise defendant that his conduct was prohibited.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

People v. Clark


No. 4-88-0610


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


188 Ill. App. 3d 79; 544 N.E.2d 100; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1359; 135 Ill. Dec. 743



September 7, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Macon County; the Hon. Jerry L. Patton, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his convictions by the Circuit Court of Macon County (Illinois) for two murders, two robberies, home invasion, and aggravated criminal sexual assault and his sentence to imprisonment for natural life. Defendant was convicted after the trial court denied his motion to suppress statements made to police and allowed testimony to statements that he made while in juvenile detention.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had admitted to several people that he and another person had entered the victims' home to burglarize it and when defendant came upon one of the victims, he beat her, jumping on her chest and breaking her sternum. Defendant was convicted and sentenced to life in prison. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that the police were not obligated to advise defendant of the nature of the charges to be brought against him, the possible punishment for those charges, or all of the material facts known to them before interrogating defendant. The court held that the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to suppress the statements given to the police officers. The court held that the trial court did not error in admitting testimony of two witnesses as to statements defendant made while in juvenile custody because the admissions were connected to the murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for two murders, two robberies, home invasion, and aggravated criminal sexual assault. The court affirmed defendant's sentence to imprisonment for natural life.

Beverly Bank v. Board of Review


No. 3-88-0557


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


193 Ill. App. 3d 130; 550 N.E.2d 567; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1383; 140 Ill. Dec. 682



September 7, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Modified on Denial of rehearing February 15, 1990.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Will County; the Hon. Herman S. Haase, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner attorneys sought review of the judgment of the Circuit Court of Will County (Illinois), which substantially reduced the fees requested by the attorneys in a class action against defendants, a county and board of review.


OVERVIEW: The attorneys worked on a class action brought on behalf of the taxpayers of the county on the basis of allegedly illegal discriminatory increases in the assessed valuation of commercial and industrial real and personal property. A settlement of the action was approved by the trial court. The attorneys for the taxpayers sought attorney fees and costs pursuant to § 1988 of the Civil Rights Act, 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The trial court reduced the hourly rates requested by the attorneys on the ground that small law firms, like the attorneys' firms, charged lower hourly rates than medium or large firms. The attorneys also asserted that the trial court erred in reducing the number of hours computed by the attorneys. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court found that the trial court erred in relying upon the previous billings of a small number of the attorneys' clients in determining the prevailing market rate. In addition, the trial court erred in reducing the number of compensable hours because the work records of the attorneys were sufficiently specific to indicate the subject matter of the billable hours.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which substantially reduced the fees requested by the attorneys in a class action.

 

579 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Christy


No. 3-88-0741


Appellate Court of Illinois, Third District


188 Ill. App. 3d 330; 544 N.E.2d 88; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1363; 135 Ill. Dec. 731



September 5, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Whiteside County; the Hon. John Donald O'Shea, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and vacated in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Circuit Court of Whiteside County (Illinois) convicted defendant of armed violence and kidnapping, in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 33A-2, 10-1 (1987), and sentenced him to concurrent extended-term prison sentences of 60 years for the armed violence conviction and 14 years for the kidnapping conviction. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed on appeal that the application of the armed violence statute to his kidnapping conviction resulted in an unconstitutionally disproportionate sentence. The court agreed, vacating defendant's armed violence conviction and sentence. The court noted that kidnapping, which was a Class 2 felony, was a lesser-included offense of aggravated kidnapping, which was a class 1 felony, and that armed violence predicated on kidnapping was a Class X felony requiring the same elements as aggravated kidnapping. The court thus found that through the application of the armed violence statute, defendant's kidnapping conviction was, in effect, enhanced to a Class X felony and was punished more severely than the greater felony of aggravated kidnapping, resulting in an unconstitutionally disproportionate sentence. The court also concluded that the trial court erred in imposing an extended-term sentence for kidnapping because kidnapping was not the most serious offense that defendant was convicted of. The court thus reduced defendant's sentence on the kidnapping conviction to the maximum nonextended term of seven years' imprisonment.


OUTCOME: The court vacated defendant's armed violence conviction and sentence and remanded the matter for resentencing based on the offense of aggravated kidnapping. The court affirmed defendant's kidnapping conviction, but reduced his sentence to the maximum nonextended term of 7 years' imprisonment.

Lamson v. Hagen


Nos. 5-87-0771, 5-87-0772


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1333



August 31, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the circuit court of Clay County, Illinois. No. 86-L-8, Honorable E.C. Eberspacher, Judge Presiding.

Appeal from the circuit court of Clay County, Illinois. No. 86-L-10, Honorable E.C. Eberspacher, Judge Presiding.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff patients appealed the judgment from the Circuit Court of Clay County (Illinois), which dismissed with prejudice the patients' complaints against defendant chiropractor. The patients alleged tortious assault and battery, intentional infliction of emotional distress, invasion of privacy, and of breach of fiduciary duty.


OVERVIEW: The patients filed separate complaints against the chiropractor and alleged that the chiropractor sexually molested each patient during examination and treatment. The chiropractor filed motions to dismiss the complaints and argued that the complaints failed to allege sufficient facts to state a cause of action and that the complaints did not each contain an affidavit of a reviewing health professional as required in malpractice claims by Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-622 (1985). The trial court dismissed the complaints with prejudice for failure to attach the required affidavits. The patients appealed and contended that the circuit court erred in finding that statutes pertaining to medical malpractice were applicable to their complaints. On consolidated appeal, the court reversed, remanded, and held that para. 2-622 was not applicable to the charges made and that the circuit court was erroneous in its conclusion that it applied. Sexual molestation was not part of any healing art treatment and whether the alleged acts occurred before, during, or after the treatment by the chiropractor was not relevant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the dismissal of the patients' intentional tort and breach of fiduciary duty complaints with prejudice and remanded the case for further proceedings.

 

581 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hall


No. 1-88-0357


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


187 Ill. App. 3d 1084; 543 N.E.2d 1038; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1348; 135 Ill. Dec. 470



August 30, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Matthew J. Moran, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of possession of a stolen motor vehicle, in violation of § 4-103 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103 (1985), and sentenced him to two years' probation.


OVERVIEW: Defendant claimed on appeal that § 4-103(a)(1) provided for two different and conflicting mental states and, therefore, that it did not comport with due process requirements because it failed to provide fair notice of what conduct was prohibited. He contended that under the statute, a person could be found guilty if he acted with either scienter or constructive knowledge and, therefore, that a person of ordinary intelligence had no notice of what the law required. Further, defendant claimed that the penalty provision, § 4-103(b), was unconstitutional because it imposed a harsher penalty for the lesser-included offense of theft and it did not bear a reasonable relationship to its legislative purpose of preventing auto theft or "chop shop" operations. The court affirmed, concluding that the mental states referenced in § 4-103(a)(1) were not irreconcilable and that the section merely provided that knowledge that a vehicle was stolen could be inferred from a person's exclusive and unexplained possession over a vehicle. The court thus found that § 4-103(a)(1) provided persons with fair notice of the prohibited conduct. Further, the court rejected defendant's challenge to § 4-103(b).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence on a charge of possession of a stolen motor vehicle.

 

582 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Balthazar


No. 1-86-1607


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


187 Ill. App. 3d 964; 543 N.E.2d 994; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1304; 135 Ill. Dec. 426



August 29, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Steven A. Schiller, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of possession of a stolen motor vehicle in violation of § 4-103(b) of the Illinois Vehicle Code, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 4-103(b) (1985).


OVERVIEW: On appeal defendant argued that the State failed to prove ownership of the vehicle and the statute that defined the offense was unconstitutional. The State contended that the statute under which defendant was charged did not require proof of ownership but instead presented the issue as to whether or not defendant had a right to possession of the motor vehicle. The court held that the evidence clearly supported the trial court's conclusion that defendant had possession of the stolen automobile. The court also decided that the statute under which defendant was convicted was not unconstitutional. The offense of possession of a stolen motor vehicle was not a lesser-included offense of general theft and therefore it was permissible for the penalty for possession of a stolen motor vehicle to have been greater than that of general theft.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction.

 

583 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


In re Application of County Collector for Judgment etc.


No. 1-88-0929


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


188 Ill. App. 3d 1068; 545 N.E.2d 145; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1309; 136 Ill. Dec. 621



August 29, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 1, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Francis Barth, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant guardian challenged a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied the guardian's motion for a declaratory judgment, filed on behalf of an elderly property owner in response to appellee tax sale buyer's petition for an order directing the county clerk to issue a tax deed conveying the elderly owner's property to the buyer.


OVERVIEW: The owner had allegedly become severely mentally impaired and had refused the help of others, including a council on aging. Thus, after the buyer purchased the owner's property, the buyer attempted to comply with the notice provisions of the Illinois Revenue Act of 1939 (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 482 et seq. (1987), by serving the owner personally, publishing a notice, and also alerting the council. However, the guardian argued that the notice provisions of the Act were unconstitutional and violated due process because they failed to take into account persons living in the unique situation of the owner. On appeal, the court reversed the judgment of the trial court denying the guardian's motion for a declaratory judgment. Instead, the court held that the notice to the council demonstrated that the buyer was aware that the owner was in need of assistance and that the buyer should have known that the notices were inadequate to inform the owner that her property was at risk. Thus, the court held that the tax sale, without effective notice to the owner, was a violation of due process. Accordingly, the trial court's judgment was reversed.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had denied the guardian's motion for a declaratory judgment.

 

584 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


New Yorker Magazine, Inc. v. Department of Revenue


No. 1-88-0379


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


187 Ill. App. 3d 931; 543 N.E.2d 957; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1293; 135 Ill. Dec. 389



August 28, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Earl Arkiss, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant magazine publisher challenged a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which upheld appellee Illinois Department of Revenue's decisions as to the magazine's tax deficiencies for 1975-77 and 1979-81. The magazine contended that the circuit court erred in finding the department properly applied the Illinois Income Tax Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 120, para. 1--101 et seq. (1985), and that the Act was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The department found that the magazine underreported its sales under the Act's three-factor apportionment formula applicable to a corporation engaged in a multistate business and assessed it $ 56,279 and $ 39,325 for the two periods in question. The magazine contended that the department failed to properly apportion its receipts from advertising space, subscription sales, and newsstand sales under the Act and that the Act as applied to the magazine was unconstitutional. The court affirmed, holding that the apportionment provisions were correctly applied. The court concluded that receipts for the sale of advertising were properly considered to be sales of tangible personal property under the Act, not a service transaction, given that the advertising space was an integral part of the publication. Further, the court ruled that the "throwback" provision of the Act had been correctly applied. Moreover, the court noted that the Act's combination of property, payroll, and sales factors was a widely used formula and concluded that it was constitutional as applied to the magazine. Finally, the magazine failed to prove an overlap in taxation resulting in gross distortions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the circuit court, which upheld the department's decisions assessing tax deficiencies against the magazine.

 

585 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


American Federation of State, etc., Council 31 v. Illinois State Labor Relations Bd.


No. 4-88-0751


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fourth District


187 Ill. App. 3d 585; 543 N.E.2d 562; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1268; 135 Ill. Dec. 179



August 24, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Petition for review of order of Illinois State Labor Relations Board.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner union sought review of an order by the Illinois State Labor Relations Board (ISLRB), which directed that a representation election be held in a decertification proceeding brought by respondent employer. The order further indicated agreement with a hearing officer's determination that the union could not raise unfair labor practice issues as a defense to the decertification petition.


OVERVIEW: The union was the exclusive bargaining representative of employees of the employer bargaining unit. As a result of unfair labor practices, the employer was ordered to enter into collective bargaining with the union. After little progress was made in the negotiations, the union advised the ISLRB that it believed that the employer was engaging in "surface bargaining" only. The union did not file any further unfair labor practices charges. Fourteen months after the original order, the employer filed a decertification petition seeking to remove the union as the employee's representative. The union excepted to the petition citing the employer's surface bargaining as a defense. The court affirmed the ISLRB's order and specifically held that the decertification proceeding was an improper forum in which to address the surface bargaining issue. The National Labor Relations Board did not adjudicate unfair labor practice charges in representation proceedings and the court concluded that ISLRB properly followed that precedent. The issue should have been addressed in either an unfair labor practices complaint or a mandamus action seeking enforcement of the earlier collective bargaining order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order directing that a representation election take place and denying the union the opportunity to assert the employer's "surface bargaining" in defense of the union's decertification.

 

586 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Mannix v. Donnewald


No. 1-87-2865


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


187 Ill. App. 3d 472; 543 N.E.2d 329; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1236; 135 Ill. Dec. 94



August 16, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Arthur L. Dunne, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff estate administrator filed a class action suit after receiving a tax refund to recover interest earned on estate funds deposited with defendant state treasurer pending determination of the actual amount of inheritance tax due. The parties filed cross-motions for summary judgment, and the administrator appealed from a Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) order granting summary judgment in favor of the treasurer.


OVERVIEW: An estate administrator deposited funds with the state treasurer pending a final determination of inheritance tax due. The administrator filed a class action suit, alleging that the treasurer was required to pay interest on funds in excess of the tax. In upholding summary judgment in favor of the treasurer, the court stated that the sole issue presented for review was whether an estate was entitled to the interest earned on funds deposited with the state treasurer pending a determination of the amount of inheritance taxes due, when the amount determined to be due was less than the amount deposited and the estate received a refund. The court ruled that there was no statute providing for a "particular fund" to be set up in order to keep the funds segregated, nor a court order directing payment to a "particular fund" to be held by the treasurer as trustee. Thus, the treasurer was authorized to invest the estate's deposit and keep the interest income. The case did not present the circumstances required to invoke the equitable powers of the court, and use of the estate's deposit to earn interest was not a "taking" of private property for public use without just compensation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the summary judgment in favor of the state treasurer in the estate administrator's action to recover interest earned on funds deposited with the state treasurer pending determination of the inheritance tax due.

 

587 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Stevens v. Lou's Lemon Tree, Ltd.


Nos. 1-88-0963, 1-88-2206 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Second Division


187 Ill. App. 3d 458; 543 N.E.2d 293; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1226; 135 Ill. Dec. 58



August 15, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Myron T. Gomberg and the Hon. Odas Nicholson, Judges, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, administrator of a decedent's estate and the decedent's husband, appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which held that defendants, landowner and tavern, were only liable to plaintiffs for the damages specified by the Liquor Control Act of 1934 (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 43, paras. 94, 135 (1987), and that the Act was constitutional.


OVERVIEW: Neither the husband nor the decedent was employed when a patron of the tavern killed the decedent after the patron was served alcohol by the tavern. The husband sought consortium damages, and both the husband and the decedent's estate sought recovery in excess of the limitations imposed by the Act. The lower court's judgment held that the Act did not provide for consortium damages and that the limitations imposed upon the recovery of damages were constitutional. The court affirmed, holding that because there was no common law action for damages caused by the service of liquor, the courts were required to exercise more restraint in construing the Act than they would be required to exercise in construing judge created-doctrines. The court ruled that the Act did not provide that the husband was entitled to consortium damages because the Act restricted damages to means of support and not the loss of love and affection. The court held that the restrictions upon recovery contained in the Act, such as a short statute of limitations, did not violate plaintiffs' due process rights because the Act created rather than abrogated a remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment, which held that the landowner and tavern could only be liable to plaintiffs for the damages provided by the Liquor Control Act of 1934 (Act) and which held that the Act was constitutional.

Kawasaki Shop of Aurora, Inc. v. Kawasaki Motors Corp., U.S.A.


No. 2-88-1058


Appellate Court of Illinois, Second District


1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1208



August 14, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated on Denial of Rehearing September 22, 1989; Substituted Opinion reported at 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1442 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [*1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Kane County. No. 82-L-882, Honorable Patrick J. Dixon, Judge, Presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dealer brought an action for breach of contract against defendant manufacturer under the Motor Vehicle Franchise Act (Act), Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 121 1/2, para. 751 et seq. (1987). The Circuit Court of Kane County (Illinois) awarded the dealer compensatory damages and attorney fees. The manufacturer appealed and the dealer cross-appealed for treble damages.


OVERVIEW: The dealer entered into a franchise agreement with the manufacturer. Following a change of ownership, a new dealership agreement was entered into between the parties. The agreement listed the dealer's location as the old location and when the dealer moved its location again the manufacturer terminated the franchise contract. The court held that the prohibition against site control in the Act protected the dealer from being subjected to unreasonable control by the manufacturer. The court determined that there was no argument made that the new location would not be an appropriate site to market the products and the franchise agreement specifically provided for multilane dealerships. The court reasoned that under the Act a dealer should not be terminated for affiliating with a competing line. The court held that the manufacturer did not have good cause to terminate the franchise. The court determined that the dealer was not entitled to treble damages because it was unclear whether the jury found for the dealer under a theory of recovery in contract, in which case trebling of damages would be prohibited, or under the statute that provided for treble damages.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the circuit court on both the appeal and the cross-appeal.

In re Summary Suspension of Driver's License of Rakers


No. 5-88-0041


Appellate Court of Illinois, Fifth District


187 Ill. App. 3d 27; 542 N.E.2d 1311; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1230; 134 Ill. Dec. 804



August 14, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Madison County; the Hon. Jonathan Isbell, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant motorist sought review of an order of the Circuit Court of Madison County (Illinois). The lower court sustained appellee state's summary suspension of driving privileges, due to the motorist's refusal to submit to a chemical test of his breath following his arrest for driving under the influence of alcohol. The motorist argued that the governing statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501.1 (1987), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: A motorist's driving privileges were summarily suspended under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 95 1/2, para. 11-501.1 (1987) because he refused to submit to a chemical test of his breath following his arrest for driving under the influence of alcohol. The lower court sustained the summary suspension by the state, and the motorist sought review. On review, the motorist advanced the argument that the failure of the arresting officer to give him a written warning of the consequences of his refusal to have his breath tested violated the motorist's due process rights. The motorist also argued that the statute was void for vagueness. The court found that the statute did not require the written warning sought by the motorist and that the testimony of the arresting officer confirmed his verbal compliance with the warning requirement. The court also found that the statute was neither contradictory nor vague. The statute clearly defined the conduct held to be unlawful and provided standards so as to avoid arbitrary or discriminatory enforcement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court, which sustained the state's summary suspension of driving privileges.

People v. Coppage


No. 1-87-1251


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


187 Ill. App. 3d 436; 543 N.E.2d 269; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1204; 135 Ill. Dec. 34



August 14, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Matthew J. Moran, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), for burglary in violation of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 19--1(a) (1985).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was tried in absentia in a bench trial and found guilty of burglary. Defendant contended that his conviction should be reversed and a new trial ordered because he was not properly admonished in accordance with Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 113--4(e) (1985); he was never notified of the new trial date by certified mail as required by Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 115--4.1(a) (1985); and the State failed to show that his absence from trial was willful. On appeal, the court affirmed the burglary conviction. The court noted that defendant conceded that the trial court informed him that if he failed to appear for trial or any court dates, he could be tried in absentia. Thus, the curt ruled that the trial court substantially complied with Ill Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 113--4(e) (1985). The court found that defendant was not entitled to receive notice of the new trial date. The court reasoned that common sense and simple logic dictated that the mailing provision be inapplicable to situations where trial had already begun. The court determined that because the statutory requirements were met, a prima facie showing of willful avoidance of trial was set forth.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's burglary conviction.

 

591 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Parks v. Romans


No. 1-88-1924


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division


187 Ill. App. 3d 445; 543 N.E.2d 277; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1200; 135 Ill. Dec. 42



August 14, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. John P. Ryan, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff mother appealed the order of Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which entered a child support order which limited the amount to the amount granted by the Illinois Department of Public Aid (IDPA), denied retroactive support, and entered a withholding order applicable only to defendant father's current employer.


OVERVIEW: After a paternity action, the mother and the IDPA brought a support action against the father. The trial court only considered the reimbursement due the IDPA and so entered a child support order in that amount rather than 20 percent of the supporting parent's net income as required by the Illinois Marriage and Dissolution of Marriage Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 505(a) (1987). On appeal, the court reversed and remanded. The trial court should have considered the statutory factors of para. 505(a). The court determined that the withholding statute, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2520(B)(3) (1987), mandated that the withholding order be directed at any payor rather than the father's current employer. Although there could have been a conflict of interest between the mother and the IDPA's representation by the state's attorney if the father's support were sufficient to cancel all public assistance, there was no conflict in this case and the state's attorney could continue to represent the mother. The court remanded to the trial court for it to consider the factors of Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 40, para. 2514(b) (1987) and determine if retroactive support should have been awarded.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order of child support equal to the child's IDPA grant and remanded for further consideration in light of the statutory factors.

Calabrese v. State Farm Mut. Auto. Ins. Co.


No. 1-88-2113


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


187 Ill. App. 3d 349; 543 N.E.2d 215; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1194; 134 Ill. Dec. 932



August 9, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 15, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Albert Green, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed in part, and reversed in part and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff insured filed a complaint in the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois) against defendant insurer seeking vacatur of an arbitrator's award for the insurer, and declaratory judgments that the arbitration had not been completed and that statutory provisions requiring arbitration of uninsured motorist claims were unconstitutional. The insured appealed the dismissal of his complaint and denial of leave to file an amended complaint.


OVERVIEW: The insured brought an uninsured motorist claim against his insurer, and an arbitration award was rendered in favor of the insurer. In reversing an order denying leave to file an amended complaint, the court noted the amended complaint specifically alleged that the neutral arbitrator was representing plaintiffs in cases against other parties insured by the insurer. The court held that those allegations were sufficient to plead a claim for vacatur of the arbitration award on the basis of fraud or bias. The court stated that it did not mean to suggest that every arbitrator must disclose the number of cases, no matter how small, involving one of the parties to an arbitration which he had handled, but believed that the insured adequately alleged grounds for vacating the arbitration award in the amended complaint and that that amendment should have been allowed in the interests of justice. In affirming the dismissal of counts alleging that statutes were unconstitutional, the court held that having submitted to the arbitration without objection the insured waived its right to insist that the statutes conferring such jurisdiction were an invasion of its constitutional right.


OUTCOME: In the insured's suit for uninsured motorist coverage, the court affirmed the dismissals of two counts of the original complaint and a summary judgment issued on the third count, but reversed the denial of leave to file an amended complaint and the denial of a motion to compel discovery.

Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, First Division

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, corporation and registered voters, and appellees, city clerk and members of the Board of Elections, both sought review of a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed appellants' complaint and enjoined appellees from issuing a proclamation certifying local election results.


OVERVIEW: Appellants initiated a case against appellees challenging the referendum petitions that were filed in support of the local election concerning redistricting. The lower court dismissed appellants' complaint based on lack of standing and the doctrine of laches, and enjoined appellees from issuing a proclamation and certifying the local election results.
