The court vacated the lower court judgment as it enjoined appellees from issuing a proclamation and certifying the local election results. Chemed Corp. v. State

OVERVIEW: The corporate taxpayer was based in another state but sold products within Illinois, through one of its subdivisions. The subdivision shipped some of the goods sold from an in-state warehouse. As the result of an audit, the department determined that the corporate taxpayer owed additional municipal retailers' occupational and authority retailers' occupational taxes. People v. Tucker


Nos. 1-87-1377, 1-87-1388 cons.


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


186 Ill. App. 3d 683; 542 N.E.2d 804; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1098; 134 Ill. Dec. 458



July 21, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Ronald Himel, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendants of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and burglary.


OVERVIEW: At defendants' trial, the state presented several witnesses who testified regarding their observations of defendants in or near an automobile. The defense presented no evidence, and the jury found both defendants guilty on the charges of possession of a stolen motor vehicle and burglary. On appeal, defendants argued that the trial court committed reversible error when it undercut the state's burden of proof through its comments during voir dire that defendants began the case with a slight advantage, and that the trial court further erred during voir dire when, in response to a prospective juror's statements that he had been the victim of a burglary involving a theft of auto parts and vandalism, the court stated that the facts of the case were similar. The court affirmed because, even if defendants had not waived the issues to which they interposed objections on appeal by their failure to object at trial, no reversible error occurred in the absence of a showing that defendants were prejudiced by the remarks of the court. Further, the evidence, viewed in its entirety, was sufficient to support defendants' conviction for burglary and possession of a stolen motor vehicle.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' convictions.

 

596 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Robinson v. Jones


No. 1-89-0752


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


186 Ill. App. 3d 82; 542 N.E.2d 127; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1031; 134 Ill. Dec. 127



June 30, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Eugene L. Wachowski, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff candidates appealed the judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which dismissed their complaint filed against defendant candidate for an election contest of the special election and for an injunction because their complaint was not filed within the five-day statute of limitations set forth in Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 21-27 (1987).


OVERVIEW: No candidate in a special election won a majority of the votes so a special run off election was called. Plaintiffs filed a complaint for an election contest and an injunction and alleged that the write-in votes were invalid and thus plaintiffs had actually won the election. The trial court dismissed the complaint. The court affirmed the dismissal. The court found that the right to contest an election was statutory and there had to be strict compliance with the statutory procedure. The court held that pursuant to Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 24, para. 21-27 (1987), a complaint to contest an aldermanic election had to be filed within five days of the election and that plaintiffs' complaint was untimely. The action was filed 16 days after the election. Therefore, the trial court was without jurisdiction to hear it. The court found that the injunction could not be issued because courts had no jurisdiction to enjoin the holding of an election except where it was necessary to prevent a waste of public funds by conducting an election under an unconstitutional election statute or an election called in violation of the constitution.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's dismissal of plaintiffs' complaint for an election contest of the special election and for an injunction.

People v. Kapsalis


No. 1-87-3500


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


186 Ill. App. 3d 96; 541 N.E.2d 1323; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1043; 133 Ill. Dec. 885



June 30, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 3, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Edward M. Fiala, Jr., Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review from a judgment of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted defendant of criminal sexual assault. He was sentenced to a term of seven years' imprisonment in a case brought by the State of Illinois.


OVERVIEW: Defendant grabbed the victim and dragged her 60 feet into a vacant lot. Defendant held a knife to her neck and then inserted his finger into her vagina. On trial, defendant asserted the affirmative defense of insanity. On appeal, defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to prove that he was sane at the time of the offense. The doctor concluded that defendant was sane at the time of the offense and that defendant was able to appreciate the criminality of the alleged offense and was able to conform his conduct to the requirements of the law. In light of the evidence presented, it could not have been said that the determination of the trial court was so improbable or unsatisfactory as to have raised a reasonable doubt as to defendant's sanity. Further, the legislature intended to enact a statute that provided triers of fact with a logical scheme by which to determine the criminal responsibility of a defendant who presented evidence of insanity or mental illness. The statute accomplished that goal. The guilty-but-mentally-ill statute did not violate the constitutional guarantee of equal protection of the law. The court affirmed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment, which convicted defendant of criminal sexual assault.

 

598 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Corbbins


No. 1-86-3303


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Sixth Division


186 Ill. App. 3d 588; 542 N.E.2d 751; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1026; 134 Ill. Dec. 405



June 30, 1989, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 28, 1989.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Michael C. Zissman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the order of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), granting the state's petition to increase defendant's bail.


OVERVIEW: While defendant was out on bail, he was arrested again. When defendant was brought into night bond court, the state asked the court for leave to file a petition for violation of bail bond conditions. The court granted the state's petition over defendant's objections. The state noted that defendant's criminal record included numerous bail bond forfeitures. Defendant claimed that the trial court violated his due process rights because it failed to provide reasonable notice and a hearing on the state's petition. He also contended that the statute authorizing an increase in bail was unconstitutionally vague. On appeal, the court dismissed the appeal as moot, finding that the issues raised by defendant ceased to exist since he was previously given a hearing on the violation of bail bond charges. The court noted that the procedure followed in the case had been in effect for several years but that it involved setting a bond on a petition for violation of bail bond conditions and was without foundation because the assertions in the petition of a violation of bond conditions were not in themselves a crime for which bail could be independently imposed.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed defendant's appeal as moot.

 

599 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


People v. Jones


No. 1-88-0214


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Fifth Division


190 Ill. App. 3d 416; 545 N.E.2d 1332; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 1023; 137 Ill. Dec. 317



June 30, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. James M. Bailey, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which convicted him of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver in violation of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(b)(2) (1987), and denied his motion to suppress evidence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted by a trial court of possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver in violation of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 56 1/2, para. 1401(b)(2) (1987), and the trial court denied his motion to suppress. Defendant appealed. The court affirmed the trial court's judgment because defendant failed to meet his statutory burden under Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 38, para. 114-12(b) (1987) of proving the allegations in his motion to suppress, and that he was not seized within the meaning of U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court determined that a reasonable person in defendant's position would have considered that he was free to leave. The court found that the state met its burden under of proving that defendant's consent was freely and voluntarily given. The court held that the search of defendant's shoulder bag was neither tainted by the preceding events nor independently amounted to a separate violation of U.S. Const. amend. IV. The court concluded that the encounter in defendant's case was consensual, and not an investigatory stop.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for possession of a controlled substance with intent to deliver in violation of the Illinois Controlled Substances Act because defendant failed to meet his statutory burden of proving the allegations in his motion to suppress. Defendant was not seized within the meaning of the Fourth Amendment, and the state met its burden of proving that defendant's consent was freely and voluntarily given.

 

600 of 2049 DOCUMENTS


Schultz v. Gotlund


No. 1-88-0378


Appellate Court of Illinois, First District, Third Division


185 Ill. App. 3d 943; 542 N.E.2d 53; 1989 Ill. App. LEXIS 982; 134 Ill. Dec. 53



June 28, 1989, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from the Circuit Court of Cook County; the Hon. Thomas E. Hoffman, Judge, presiding.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer sought review of a decision of the Circuit Court of Cook County (Illinois), which denied its petition to intervene, under Civil Practice Law § 2-408, Ill. Rev. Stat. ch. 110, para. 2-408 (1985), in a personal injury action by plaintiffs, employee and husband, against defendants, driver, relative, restaurant, and owner.


OVERVIEW: The employer had paid medical expenses for the husband under a group health insurance policy issued to the employee. It contended on appeal that it should have been permitted to intervene either as of right or permissively. The employee and her husband argued that the employer had no contractual right of subrogation. The court found that the purpose of the medical payments coverage of the group policy was to indemnify the employee or other beneficiary from pecuniary loss rather than to pay a sum certain on the happening of a given event, and thus found the coverage more comparable to that of fire and marine policies, under which there was a right of subrogation, than to life and accident coverage. The court stated that if an insurer paid a loss which was due to the wrongful act of another, it was subrogated to the rights of the insured independent of contract. The court determined that given the equitable nature and purposes of common-law subrogation, the cause should be remanded for a hearing on whether defendants driver and relative or their insurer knew of the employer's interest prior to their settlement with and release by the employee and husband.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order denying the employer's petition to intervene and remanded the cause with instructions.
